# 真诰

*The True Instructions*
*Scroll One*
*Chapter One: The Movement of Symbols*

**Poem of Erlü Hua**

The sacred peaks thrust through the clouds,
Towering summits rise a thousand fathoms high.
The numinous valley lies vast and still,
Jade groves flourish in solemn verdure.
*(One character here is heavily inked and unrecognizable. A stroke extends downward from its center, resembling the character "羊" [sheep]. The person’s name is Quan.)*

Born with beauty and grace,
In youth, his voice flowed with pure resonance.
His spirit dwelled by the ford of庄慧,
Transcending form in the forest of Wei.
Radiant within the vermilion gates,
Yet his heart soared beyond the common world.
I share with the Master’s clan
A lineage deep as the same abyssal pool.
The great ancestral legacy diverged,
And now we branch along separate paths.
Like gold and orchid bound by fondness,
The Three Friendships grow ever more profound.
In quiet reflection, I rejoice in this meeting,
Our refined discourse spanning the years.
Who says the hidden mirror is hard to find?
It lies within the square inch of the heart.
I lift my thoughts beyond the earthen enclosures,
Together we are scholars of the mountain crags.
Let not your soaring brush take flight,
Only to be swept away by the startled wind.
Though transformation depends on man,
The flourishing ram is not easily compared.
What I seek is no fleeting blossom—
In the twilight of years, it is you, my friend.

**Erlü Hua** claims to be a person of the Southern Mountains, though it is unclear which range. She appears as a woman of about twenty, clad in dark green robes above and below, her countenance surpassingly fair.

On the night of the tenth day of the eleventh month in the third year of the Shengping era, she descended. (Two characters here are cut off; they should be "Yang Quan.") From then on, she came and went, visiting as many as six times in a single month. She stated her original surname (one character is cut off; it should be "Yang") and presented (this character was originally "Quan," later altered) a poem, along with a fire-washed cloth handkerchief, a gold *tiaotuo*, and a jade *tiaotuo*. The *tiaotuo* were exceptionally large and exquisitely crafted. The divine woman said (this character was originally written as "Quan" in cursive, later changed to "see," with the stroke order adjusted): "Sir, be careful not to reveal my presence. If you do, both of us will incur guilt." Upon inquiring, this person was said to be Luo Yu, a woman who attained the Dao in the Nine Doubt Mountains. In a past life, she had been poisoned to death by her master’s wife while serving as a wet nurse. As her previous sins had not been absolved in the Dark Realm, she was sent down to this foul and turbid world to atone for her transgressions. She gave (this "Quan" is also in cursive, resembling the previous form but not identical) the elixir for *shijie* to Yang Quan. Now, she resides in the mountains east of the Xiang River. (Originally, a small section was missing here.) This woman is already nine hundred years old.

(Investigating this, it should be the descent to Yang Quan. Quan, styled Daoyu, was the youngest son of Yang Zhen. Later, he became the Yellow Gate Attendant for Emperor Jianwen of the Jin. He was also the grandfather of Yang Xin, who likewise practiced Daoist arts and ingested elixirs. This account was written by a certain Yang, likely because they shared the same surname, and thus inquired as if it were Yang Quan, recording the matter in detail in response.)

In the third year of Shengping (a *jiwei* year), six years before *yichou*, none of the Perfected had yet descended.

---

The above three entries were hastily written by Yang on paper. The Lady of Southern Peak spoke to her disciple, recording the details as follows. (The disciple refers to Yang herself. This gathering of the Perfected seems to have taken place in the Grotto Palace, which is why the Director of Destinies is listed first, serving as the host. The Lady explained the ranks and titles to Yang in this manner, not during the descent to Yang.)

The Perfected Lord Director of Destinies of the Eastern Peak,
The Perfected Lord of the Nine Essences of the Eastern Palace, Grand Minister of the Golden Portal, the Great Lord Green Lad,
The Right Immortal Duke of Penglai, Jia Bao’an (a native of Zheng; from here onward, all are referred to by the *zi* of the Perfected, not their given names, with their clans and lineages also found in secular Daoist texts and records),
The Celestial King of Qingxu Xiaoyou, Wang Zideng (as the Green Lad holds a lofty and revered position, his given name is not dared to be mentioned; this Qingxu is the master of the Southern Peak, yet his *zi* is still used. The *zi* of the Director of Destinies of Mao Mountain is uniquely not recorded, which is difficult to explain),
The Perfected of Tongbai, Right Assistant Wang, Director of the Five Peaks, Attendant to the Lord of Dawn, Wang Ziqiao,
The Perfected of the Green Canopy, Attendant to the Lord of Dawn, Guo Shigan (a native of Wei),
The Perfected of Rong Mountain, Right Immortal Duke of the Supreme Ultimate, Fan Bohua (a native of You),
The Perfected of Shaoshi, Gentleman of the Northern Terrace, Liu Qianshou (a native of Pei),
The Perfected of {Mountain} Zhong, Gentleman of the Left Prohibition, Wang Daoning (a native of Changshan),
The Perfected of Daliang, Wei Xianren (a native of Changle),
The Perfected of Min Mountain, Yin Youzong,
The Perfected of Luhun, Supervisor of the Supreme Ultimate of the West, Guo Youdu,
The Marquis of Nine Doubt Mountain, Zhang Shanggui (a native of Chu).

The Divine Marquis of Mount Tai, Overseer of the Netherworld {Right Prohibition Bureau}, Bao Yuanjie (a native of Donghai),
The Immortal Earl of Mount Hua, Qin Shuyin (a native of Fengyi),
The Perfected of Geyan, Zhou Jitong,
The Perfected of Yangluo, Overseer of the Western Return Transmission, Chunyu Taixuan (a native of the Western Regions),
The True Earl of Mount Qian, Zhao Zuyang (a native of Jun),
The Perfected of Mount Juqu, Recorder of the Right Prohibition Bureau, Mao Jiwei,
The Perfected of Mount Yuque, Pei Xuanren,
The Immortal Capital of Baishui, Zhu Jiaofu,
The Three Offices’ Life-Preservation Bureau, Mao Sihe,
The Perfected of Great Harmony, Shan Shiyuan.

The twenty-three Perfected sat in order,
beginning from the west and proceeding eastward in a south-facing arrangement.
(According to ritual propriety, the west should be the honored position when facing south,
and the female Perfected should then proceed eastward—thus, they ought to begin from the south.
The present reversal to the north is likely due to the proximity of the exalted Perfected.)

The Perfected Consort of Great Harmony, Left Lady of the Supreme Realms,
The Lady of the Six Subtleties of the Northern Sea, Mystic Clarity,
The Lady of the Seven Spirits of Northern Han, Right Lady,
The Right Lady of the Central Flower of the Supreme Ultimate,
The Lady Wang of the Left Palace of Purple Tenuity,
The Right Lady Ying of Canglang’s Cloudy Forest.
(Note: Lady Ying is the elder sister of the Purple Tenuity Lady,
yet here she appears afterward—this reflects the rise and fall of their respective positions.)

The Perfected Controller of Destiny, Lady of the Southern Marchmount,
(This is Lady Wei; as she speaks for herself, her surname is not given.)
The Dao-Mother of the Eight Spirits, Lady Jiang of the Western Marchmount,
(Note: Where multiple titles exist, the greater number is deemed higher. The Queen Mother of the West is called the Nine Spirits, so the Eight Spirits should precede the Seven Spirits. Yet here they appear afterward—this remains unexplained. Also, in the *Recitation of the Yellow Court* tradition, she is called Lady Jiang of the Northern Marchmount, differing from the present text.)
The Perfected Guardian of the Eastern Palace, Lady Wei,
Lady Li of Bright Spirit Terrace on Fangzhang,
The Pacifying Consort of Nine Flowers in the Upper Palace of Purple Clarity,
Lady Guan, Noble Concubine of the Northern Absolute Terrace on Vermilion Mound,
The Perfected Lady of the Northern Marchmount,
Lady of the Western Han,
Lady Du of Changling.
The fifteen female Perfected, facing east, seated from north to south.
(Though the month and day of this event are unrecorded, and the year unknown, as these are the names and ranks of the assembled Perfected, they are listed here at the fore. Regarding the ranks of the Perfected: as previously noted, the higher the number, the greater the honor—much like honorary titles in the present age.)

On the night of the twenty-first day of the sixth month, the Registrar of Destinies inquired, saying, "What path does Director Xu seek in his pursuit of the Dao?"
Deng replied with earnest devotion to the cultivation of true sincerity.
The Registrar of Destinies then said, "Formerly, there was Zhao Shutai and Wang Shiqing, who also spoke of their diligent study, yet ultimately failed to meet expectations. They were thus summoned into the service of the Northern Bright Lord’s Palace."
(This occurred in the sixth month of the yichou year.)

From this point onward, only the Registrar of Destinies’ transmission on the fifteenth day of the sixth month—a response to Director Xu’s letter discussing matters of Mount Mao—is recorded. Prior to this, there was another transmission, the date of which is not noted, both of which are contained in the fourth scroll. No earlier records exist before these.

The Northern Bright Lord’s Palace (the central administrative office of the celestial bureaus) once roamed the expanses of Heavenly Ford and gathered blossoms on Crimson Mound. At that time, its radiant presence stirred the sleeves of the numinous, and its dust-mantled splendor graced the lofty pines. (This refers to the initial descent upon the Huaqiao immortal.) From the resplendent peaks, its lofty discourse reached the distant clouds. It deemed itself stirred by the resonance of the mysterious, believing no path would remain obstructed. Bathed in the waves of the numinous, it truly hoped to share its glory with all things. Yet, unable to fully unfold its flourishing enterprise or wander freely among the peaks, it came to realize that in the moment of awakening, the response of the mysterious was minimal. Thus, it turned its carriage and returned, resting in stillness upon the kudzu terrace.

For the blade of the mysterious makes no partial distinctions, and the mirror of flowing insight eludes the untrue. If one assumes that a single ascent to the cloud-walled heights suffices, or that solitary strides alone achieve parity, then even the most humble beginnings may be cleansed, and every movement may subtly align with the hidden and the recondite. Only then will we all share in joy and sighs alike.

In the past, I saw that your intentions were deeply aligned with mine. The closing of your letter states: *"I prostrate myself to behold the sagely record, its events profound and wondrous. The golden tally is plainly inscribed, the azure register divinely fixed. Thus, you transcend the dust of the mundane and wander freely in the Purple Yang. How pure and distant is your clarity, how exalted and rare your true nobility! Such is the mark of one who has attained the Way. I humbly request to borrow this as an analogy."*

It further states: *"The steps to attaining the Dao are interwoven with the myriad spirits. To quiet the self and lodge in sincerity, to wash clean the heart and seek compassion—"*

As such, the Dao is already near. Yet between dusk and dawn, one must diligently cultivate. Only then may the hands weave the cords of Heaven, the feet tread upon the numinous web, the heart wander the Great Void, and the eyes behold the Cavern Chambers—all without need of many days.

Should the five passions stir their waves or the three souls stray in parsimony, then the Three Perfected shall dance with swords, and the Yellow Gates shall swiftly bar the way. Can one not strive? Can one not strive?

On the twenty-second day of the sixth month, at the crowing of the cock in the night, this was written in response. Such is the decree of the Purple Yang.

The two preceding passages were transcribed by the Prefectural Clerk.

The *Scripture of Treasured Spirits* as spoken by the Perfected One of Pure Numen states... (These cultivation matters are recorded in the third fascicle; they shall not be repeated here.)

The Lady of Purple Tenuity’s response is as follows... (This matter is also in the third fascicle.)

In the third year of the Xingning reign, cyclical year *yichou*, on the twenty-third day of the sixth month, in the night, this was written in response. That evening, among those who practiced the Dao, many suffered from dullness of ears and dimness of eyes. Desiring to petition for this method, they received a nocturnal visitation—this was the response they beheld. (This is Yang Jun’s personal account. The Prefectural Clerk, now past sixty, found his hearing and sight failing, hence his inquiry. Yang did not wish to name him directly, so he referred to “those among us.”)

It was further instructed: “As for Daoists whose ears are heavy...” (This matter is also in the third fascicle.)

The preceding passage is the word of the Perfected One of Pure Numen.

The Perfected One instructed: “When combing the hair, one should do so frequently.” (This matter is also in the third fascicle.)

The preceding passage is the word of the Lady of Purple Tenuity.

At the beginning of the night’s descent, just as the visitor entered the door and before taking a seat, they remarked: “This evening, the sound of waves was like thunder.” The disciple inquired as to the cause. The reply: “I had just seen the great waves of the Eastern Sea.” (Here, “disciple” refers to Yang Jun himself.)

The preceding passage is the word of the Lady of Southern Marchmount. Further instructions were given...

“Do you loathe blood?”
The reply: “I truly loathe it.”
“Blood lies upon the path. If you loathe it, how then can you walk?”
Another reply: “One should simply avoid it.”
Further instruction: “Avoiding it is well, yet still better is not to see it at all.”
The preceding passage is the word of the Lady of Southern Marchmount. From this point onward, the various Perfected Ones conversed together.

It was also said: “The *Scripture of Treasured Spirits* is the text from Master Pei Qingling’s brocade satchel, which his attendants always carried. Pei formerly received this scripture from the Lady of Purple Tenuity. I, too, possess a copy, transcribed exactly as the definitive edition kept in the Western Palace.”
Asked where the Western Palace lay, the answer came: “It is the terrace above the western jasper of the Northern Altar in the Dark Garden.”
All the sacred writings of the Heavenly Perfected are stored therein.
The preceding passage is the word of the Lady of Southern Marchmount.

Master Pei the Perfected further stated: “This scripture ranks with the *Hidden Writings*. Its matters are essential and may be put to immediate use. Another name for it is the *Sevenfold Mysteries of the Hidden Writings*.”
(Here ends the transmission of the twenty-third day.)

The Lady of Southern Marchmount further instructed:
“The Lady of the Left of Purple Tenuity is named Wang Qing’e, styled Yu’yi. She is the twenty-first daughter of the Celestial Matriarch and presides over Feathered Wilds and the Dark Mound Mountain. She oversees the instruction of those destined to become Perfected Ones.”
The preceding passage was transmitted the evening prior.
(This passage was received on the night of the twenty-second, the same evening as the instruction from Purple Yang. It was later noted that a great response was to follow, and the phrase “qi descending” also refers to this evening. Yang later recalled this matter and recorded it again under the twelfth day’s entry. Hence it is said to precede this evening.)

From Qingling, twelve passages in all were received, transcribed by the Senior Scribe.
On the night of the twenty-fourth day of the sixth month, the Lady Wang of Purple Tenuity descended. Upon alighting, she was asked:
“When the Perfected Ones descend in person among the dust and defilement of mortals, yet their hands and feet have never once set brush to writing—is this not a matter of humble or exalted traces {or advancing demeanor}? Ought it not be made manifest?”
Thus was the inquiry made.

May this instruction dispel my ignorance.

Thereupon, the Lady commanded me to be seated again. Immediately, she granted me leave to transcribe her response, saying:

*(This is Master Yang’s own account of the matter, as is often the case in these records.)*

The profound and empty mystery lies beyond all paths of pursuit. Words uttered into the void find no substance to grasp. Drifting and shifting with sudden swiftness, they transform and vanish without lingering—such are these two modes, both submerged in obscurity and darkness, {or flickering in stillness}. Thus, unrestrained and without guidance, they ride the wind’s gusts {or the oars’ sweep}, moving as if aboard an empty boat.

Therefore, within the real lies the void; within the void, existence; and within existence, the formless. As for the manifestation of written traces: brushstrokes take shape upon paper, patterns {or sunlight} flow into script, {and the marks appear}—yet the outer display is but the radiant flourish of the mysterious brush, while the material form serves to reveal. Silent elegance is thus confined, and form transmits through the dust and defilement.

If one were to expose the skeletal remains of things, allowing them to advance or retreat with the world, this would elevate {or jade-like} the songs of the transcendent Real, while below, it would breach the prohibitions of separation and obstruction. Such is not the way we follow, nor is it permitted by the numinous Dharma.

Now let us set forth the origins of writing. When the creation of script first began, it was the time when the five colors first sprouted and the patterns of literature were fixed in form. It distinguished the intercourse of humanity and marked the division of yin and yang. Thus arose the Three Origins and Eight Convergences—the script of the myriad directions that soars through the heavens—and also the luminous chapters of the Eight Dragons’ Cloud Seal. Later, in the age of the Two Sovereigns, the script of the Eight Convergences was expanded into the patterns of dragons and phoenixes. The traces of the Cloud Seal were refined to form the compliant shapes of Brahmi script. The two paths were sundered, the true and the mutable were separated, and the branches were matched to their roots, giving rise to the sixty-four kinds of writing. These were then disseminated across the thirty-six heavens and the ten directions above and below. Each took its own section and type, differing in use. Though their phonetic canons were uniform, their written traces diverged widely. Comparing and discussing them, the script of the Eight Convergences is the most authentic of writings, the progenitor of literary patterns. The Cloud Seal and Luminous Script are its root and origin, the beginning of all writing. The script of the Three Origins and Eight Convergences is now used by the august Highest Ultimate and the pure transcendents of the highest heavens. The chapters of the Cloud Seal and Luminous Script are what we now see as the characters of divine talismanic writing.

Yet in the later flourishing age, false and chaotic inventions arose. Together they crafted clever but trivial forms, pursuing shortcuts in inferior script. All were but flowing corpses of defiled literature and licentious, perverse characters—abandoning the root to imitate the false, mere clamorous and filthy dead traces. Why would a true transcendental being discard the authentic and essential script to draw with their own hand the licentious and disordered characters of the lower realms? One who has attained the rank of true person has mastered the real in every matter. How could they alone indulge in the trivial arts of the vulgar, the corrupt practices of superficiality, clinging to them without change and delighting in them without transformation?

When a person is in the world, those who were first skilled in writing and adept in affairs—once they attain true transcendence—will find that even the transformations of external script naturally reverse themselves along with their person. Those whose true affairs are all near at hand no longer discard the defiled script they have already mastered; rather, they first receive instruction in the superior script and only afterward come to know the true writing anew. The way of ghosts is likewise, though their characters may slightly deviate.

Moreover, with the numinous brush and true hand, they dare not descend to commune with fleshly beings. Even when there are those who have attained the Dao but whose bodies have not yet transcended the world, they still dare not lower their hands to display inked characters, revealing them in written traces. As for talismanic texts and divine verses—those sought and worn—they have been crafted from the very beginning. The reason for this is that worldly people fundamentally cannot fathom their origins, and it also prevents us from concealing anything. In the unseen realm, they are mutually understood; within and without, they are reciprocally connected.

Furthermore, the luminous statutes of the Four Poles and the prohibitions of the Most High are weighty, and they naturally do not permit us to again produce ordinary script for the world. Since I have already set my hand to this, and you surely do not comprehend, why would we pursue both paths and invite superfluous trouble? This, too, should be discerned in silence as to its propriety—it is hardly worth reproach. I imagine it may slightly ease the congestion in your heart, fully distinguishing you from those who do not write of themselves.

The Supreme Perfected Controller of Destinies, the Lady of the Southern Marchmount, transmitted this command as follows:

When one casts the cloud-wheel aloft, reins in the vast emptiness, hands guiding the celestial net, feet ascending the Jade Court, body rising to the imperial palace, parting the jeweled canopy of azure—above, discoursing on the transcendent measures of the Nine Mysteries; below, recording the great life of the myriad kalpas—then one startles the lightning of radiance into solemnity, and a thousand rosy clouds blaze with brilliance. True words surge like dark waves; lofty discourse resounds in the Jade Clarity. Crimson lips unleash flowing splendor; the sun’s qi scatters in droplets. Then one exhales beacons to repel smoke, strikes gold to play jade, where luan-bird songs bloom in radiance and phoenix chants resound in fine harmony.

Yet if one merely descends in response to the scene, turning back to the dust of the mortal realm, riding in a tattered carriage through the morning market, coming to perfect true talent and instructing my disciples—then jade chimes fall in muted resonance, and jasper bells are inwardly restrained. The eyes survey the Five Defilements; the heart contracts in the chamber of transgressions. The spirit labors amidst foul stench; the nose fills and the breath is held. Thus, the orchid tones of the Central Prime are sealed, and one retreats to strike the golden sounds, faint and faltering, to be heard.

The words of the divine are subtle when near, yet they reach across ten thousand leagues. Though rare melodies may touch the ear, the mirror of reflection remains unobstructed. Thus, once the principles of the true are distinguished, hearing from afar, the Dao ascends in lofty progression. Unpolished jade does not display its luster, yet it may still give rise to base and trivial perceptions.

Now you have arrived at the utmost of awakened intention, yet you entertain thoughts of suspicion and resemblance. Externally, you observe the responses of the vulgar; internally, you harbor hesitations and realizations. If you do not act in accord with what is fitting, you have already gone astray. What you should aspire to is the Dao; what you should ponder and chant is the wondrous. Once the Dao and the wondrous are attained, the sounds of high and low will surely become level.

This is not a matter for deliberation. You, my disciple, should apply the deepest consideration, dispersing these thoughts. Be cautious in this.

The three clauses above were written by Yang. On the night of the twenty-fourth day of the sixth month, the Lady of the Southern Marchmount bestowed this command. Previously, on the evening of the twenty-second day, there was a discussion on the Dao in a separate chamber. The Ladies of the Purple Tenuity and the Southern Marchmount spoke in voices and tones markedly inferior, their intent incomprehensible.

Herewith this writing is bestowed in answer to the doubts arising from our shared discourse. When first it was given, my countenance and qi remained unsettled. Only after the transmission was complete did I, the disciple, perceive that my complexion alone bore disquiet—nothing else could be spoken of. (This passage is also recorded by Master Yang as his own account.)

That evening, the Lady of the Southern Marchmount addressed me, saying: "Tomorrow I shall journey to the Qingxu Palace on Mount Wangwu. Let this be known to you as my destination." Later that same night, she added: "On the western slope of Mount Tongbai by the Eastern Sea, a landslide has just collapsed some two hundred zhang." The Lady of Purple Tenuity, Wang, remarked: "How could the thoughts and concerns of worldly people ever attain true clarity in every matter? Should one not simply respond to what their hearts seek?" The Lady of the Southern Marchmount spoke in jest, intending to affirm and establish it.

In the third year of the Xingning reign, the year *yichou*, on the night of the twenty-fifth day of the sixth month—(This marks the beginning of the Lady An’s descent, recorded separately in another scroll; hence the reign year and cyclical sign are noted anew)—the Lady of Purple Tenuity, Wang, descended once more, accompanied by a divine maiden. The maiden wore a cloud-brocade robe, its upper part cinnabar-red and lower part azure, resplendent with luminous patterns. At her waist hung a green embroidered sash, from which dangled over ten small bells, their colors alternating between azure and yellow. On her left side she bore a jade pendant, similar to those worn in the mortal world, though slightly smaller. Her garments, though dark, gleamed with a radiance that illuminated the chamber, as if sunlight were reflecting upon mica.

Her hair—(this should read *fazhen*, denoting lustrous black tresses)—was arranged with unparalleled precision: coiled into a topknot at the crown, with the remaining locks cascading down to her waist. Her fingers bore golden rings, and white pearls adorned her arms. She appeared to be about thirteen or fourteen years of age. Flanking her were two attendants.

One attendant wore crimson robes and carried a green-patterned satchel, in her hands a brocade pouch measuring one or two *chi* in length, containing some ten scrolls. The pouch was sealed with a white jade clasp, upon which was inscribed: *Jade Purity Divine Tiger’s Inner True Purple Primordial Cinnabar Scripture*.

The other attendant, clad in azure, bore a white casket bound with crimson cords.

The white casket resembled one made of ivory. The two attendants appeared to be about seventeen or eighteen years of age, exquisitely adorned. The goddess and her attendants bore radiant complexions, lustrous and translucent as jade, suffused with the fragrance of five incenses—like the scent of *xiangying* (a foreign incense known as "infant fragrance") burning.

As they entered the chamber, they followed behind the Lady of the Purple Tenuity. Once the lady had stepped inside, she announced, "Today, a noble guest has come to visit and converse with us." Thereupon, I rose to my feet. The lady said, "There is no need to stand. We shall simply sit together and exchange courtesies." The Lady of the Purple Tenuity sat facing south, while I, that evening, first sat beneath the dais, facing west. The goddess then joined us on the same couch, facing east. Each of us performed the greeting with our left hands. Once the courtesies were complete, the Lady of the Purple Tenuity said, "This is the youngest daughter of the Golden Terrace Lady Li, the Supreme Perfected of the Great Void. The Supreme Perfected of the Great Void once sent her to Mount Gui to study the Dao of the Highest Clarity. After mastering the Way, she received the scriptures of the Most High and was appointed as the True Consort of the Nine Florets of the Purple Clarity Upper Palace. Thus, she was bestowed the surname An, the given name Yupin, and the style Lingxiao."

The Lady of the Purple Tenuity then asked me, "Have you ever encountered such a person in the mortal world?" I replied, "Her divine grace and lofty refinement defy comparison." The lady laughed heartily and asked, "And what of you?" I made no further reply.

The True Consort of Purple Clarity sat for a long while without speaking. In her hand, she held three dates, their color like dried jujubes but larger in form, without pits and lacking the taste of dates—rather, they resembled the flavor of pears. She first offered one to me, then gave another to the Lady of the Purple Tenuity, keeping the last for herself. She instructed us to eat them, and once we had finished, after a short while, the True Consort asked my age and the month of my birth. I promptly answered, "Thirty-six, born in the ninth month of the *gengyin* year."

The True Consort then said, "Your teacher, the Lady of the Southern Perfection, holds authority over the Director of Destinies and possesses a Dao of sublime and perfect attainment—truly the paragon of noble virtue. I have long heard of your virtuous reputation and never imagined we would meet today to forge this joyous karmic bond. May our connection endure through the unseen workings of fate, like intertwining pine and vine."

Thereupon, I gave my name in reply, saying, "I am mired in the dust of the vulgar world, my essence tainted by its filth. Though I aspire to rise, I am unworthy to receive such divine favor, which I have so undeservedly been granted."

Overwhelmed with boundless joy, I could only receive her instruction to dispel my ignorance and deliver my primal spirit—this has been my deepest wish day and night.

The True Consort said, "You must not speak with such modesty and embellishment. Such humble words are entirely inappropriate."

After a long while, the True Consort addressed me again, saying, "I wish to compose a written piece to bestow upon you. Would you transcribe my humble thoughts with your brush?" I assented and immediately prepared the paper and ink. She then dictated the following poem to me:

---
The cloud-gate towers into empty heights,
Jade terraces rise amid lush mist.
The Purple Palace rides the verdant radiance,
The numinous abode gleams, towering and grand.
Within the vermilion chambers of the jade portico,
Supreme virtue blazes like crimson auroras.
Bending low, I sip from the cloud-vessel’s spring;
Raising my hand, I pluck the azure blossoms.
I bathe my feet in the Jade Celestial Pool,
And strike the drum to cross the Herdboy’s River.
Then I urge on my radiant cloud chariot,
Reining the dragon steeds along the dark slope.
I shake my robes at the dust’s edge,
My cold garments tread the turbid waves.
I vow to bind myself to the mountains and marshes,
Hard and soft in harmonious accord.
Together we enter the realm of dual purity,
Where the perfected of the Upper Realms walk the true Way.
In the Purple Tenuity, we meet in noble counsel,
Chanting and receiving, our blessings manifold.
---

When I finished writing, I presented it to her. She took it and said, "I now bestow this upon you to express my cinnabar heart. Do not dismiss it lightly. If there is anything you do not understand, you may inquire discreetly."

Then the Lady of the Purple Tenuity said, "I shall also compose a written piece through you to enlighten you and demonstrate what is virtuous." Once more, I prepared the paper and ink. She dictated the following poem:

---
The Two Images divide within and without,
The mysterious qi bears fruit in their midst.
Dark union requires no chariot—
What matters is to attain the true in one’s aspirations.
The Southern Marchmount forges luminous gold,
A distant gaze overturns the scripture-case’s contents.
Noble virtue soars, illumined by rosy clouds,
Thus moving the numinous ones of the radiant heavens.
Riding the whirlwind, they share their quilts in repose,
Together they grasp the crimson clouds in the sacred feast.
Awakening, I sigh at the boundary of heaven and man—
Within the reckonings, karmic bonds are already set.
The supreme Way is truly not crooked,
The dust’s filth is not what should be heard.
With shared vision, all perceive the eternal image;
A lofty chant becomes the cause for your sake.
---

When she finished, the Lady of the Purple Tenuity took the poem and read it. Afterward, she said, "I bestow this upon you."

Today, you are the host of my karmic bonds,
And I, the guest of your chant’s intent.
The Lady of the Purple Tenuity added,
"Tomorrow, the Lady of the Southern Marchmount shall return.
I will accompany the Perfected Consort to welcome her at the Cloud Kiln.
If she does not return tomorrow, it will be a matter of several days."

After a long while, the Lady of the Purple Tenuity said,
"I depart now.
Tomorrow, I shall return with the Perfected Consort to visit you."
Awakening, I stepped down from the bed, but she was nowhere to be found.

The Perfected Consort lingered briefly and said,
"Hidden feelings are not yet resolved,
And the spirit’s resolve is not yet forgotten.
I imagine you will compose verses together."
"Tomorrow, I shall return again."
Then she took my hand and held it as she descended from the bed.
Before she had passed through the doorway,
She suddenly vanished.

On the evening of the twenty-sixth day of the sixth month,
The host of Perfected Ones arrived.
The register is as follows:

Lady Wang of the Purple Tenuity,
Perfected Consort of the Nine Flowers of the Upper Palace of Purple Clarity,
The Lady of the Southern Marchmount, Controller of Destinies and Perfected One of the Upper Realm,
[Your] Master—
(All previous and subsequent instances of "某" refer to the same.)

(All instances of "某" refer to the same.)

The Perfected of Purple Yang,
The Lord of the Central Mao,
The Perfected of Pure Numinosity,
The Lesser Lord of the Mao,
And another person—
Young in years, of extraordinary refinement,
Wearing a lotus crown and crimson robes,
With white pearls sewn along the seams,
A sword at his waist, the like of which had never been seen.
This person often spoke of matters concerning Mount Jinting,
Conversing with the host of Perfected Ones.
There were also words beyond comprehension.
He bowed in reverence to the Three Perfected Ladies of Purple Tenuity, Purple Clarity, and the Southern Marchmount,
While with the others he spoke as equals.
He was said to be Wang Ziqiao, the Perfected of Mount Tongbai.
Throughout, he did not exchange a word with [Your] Master.

Moreover, when Perfected Ones first descended in earlier encounters,
They likewise did not immediately engage in conversation.
Each sat for a long while.
Then the Perfected Consort of Purple Clarity said,
"I wish to trouble your hand once more to record something,
That I may dispel lingering thoughts and forgetful words.
Would that be acceptable?"
[Your] Master again folded paper and awaited instruction.
The Perfected Consort then slowly and softly spoke:

"I am the youngest daughter of the Primordial Lord,
The beloved child of Lady Li of the Great Void.
Long ago, I first studied the Dao upon Tortoise Terrace,
Received jade scriptures from the Most High,
Bore the tiger register of the Purple Sovereign,
And wielded the jade axe of the Heavenly Emperor.
I received texts from the Consort of the Upper Perfected,
That I might wander the Jade Clarity.
Often, I personally opened the ninefold gates of Luo,
Trod the dark chambers with my feet,
Soared through the numinous void,
Gazed upon the roots of the sun,
Entered the feasts of the seven palaces,
And emerged driving cloud chariots.
I gathered the three luminaries to ascend together,
Scattered radiant clouds to fly my carriage.

Not that I could not have chosen a lofty chamber,
Sought among the purple youths,
Or found a worthy companion in the Jade Palace,
To pair with a transcendent spirit and form a union,
Joining the marvelous and guiding the wondrous,
Becoming a companion to the Imperial Lad.
Yet it was I who followed the turning of the mechanism and entrusted myself to fate,
Answered the reckoning of destiny,
Stooped to the dust and foam,
Descended with the dragons,
Summoned the hidden and sought the heroic,
Pursued those who matched my company.

From the beginning, our karmic bond was destined,
And so there was an inked pact to fix our names,
A pristine covenant in the Jade Realm,
A shared governance of twin blessings.
We journeyed side by side like wild geese,
Shared the gourd cup’s flavor,
Bound our robes with the wine-stained sash,
And attended to the inner chamber’s duties.
Such was the treasury of true methods.
Proceeding thus, our fates were already inscribed in the unseen records,
Our names written in the Azure Books of the Upper Prime.
Therefore, the heart’s inclinations toward refinement or vulgarity were already equal,
And the bounds of affection in the face of beauty were already set.
Having attained our wishes, we roamed with joy surpassing past intentions—
Was this not the workings of nature’s spontaneity?
This, again, is the great principle of the two images,
The appointed roles of inner and outer union.

Truly, it is not that I sought to alter the unchanging or return to simplicity,
To congeal emotions with the blade of emptiness,
To wield the numinous knife sevenfold,
To abandon the task of the Great Plain,
To preserve the true and open the jade,
Or to speak of the solitary radiance of the eight voids.
Rather, it is the flourishing stillness of lofty purity,
The luxuriant chariot of flowing clouds,
Where phoenixes sing on the paths of heaven,
Dragons chant and tigers roar,
The celestial sovereigns of twin radiance,
Far ascending the starry towers,
Flying stars casting their light,
Sun and moon illuminating the body,
Mouth exhaling dark mist,
Eyes flashing lightning.
Above, I repose in the jade chambers,
Wandering through the Jade Clarity,
Hand grasping radiant clouds,
Feet treading Mount Jinting.

If, from this time onward,
At the moment of attaining the Dao,
Should one thoroughly exhaust both inner and outer,
Harmonizing principle with the unyielding like metal and stone,
Entwining affections in dual devotion,
Uniting hearts within the bed curtains—
Or must one embrace the shared quilt and equal care,
Yet still have fleeting encounters,
Defiling the seven spirits,
Grieving the soul and burdening the hun and po?

This is merely my inquiry to you, O Illustrious One, regarding lineage—
There is no impropriety in it.
Now, having realized our aspirations and embraced the true,
Our hearts are as one.
We shall soon join our chariots in the Jade Void,
Journey together to the Northern Mystery,
Pluck the crimson fruits in the Jade Orchard,
Gather the cinnabar blossoms in the [Gate of Goodness] Garden,
Share the waters of the Purple River,
Bathe together on the banks of the Azure Stream.
Clad in robes of purple blossoms,
Crowned with lotus diadems,
We shall wander freely in the Upper Clarity."

Together we shall attend the Three Primordials’ court,
As the Eight Radiant Ones emerge and descend.
Through phoenix gates and cloud-barred passes,
We shall gaze upward to sip the golden marrow,
Chant and sing of the jade mystery.
Drifting in the void, we shall recline in banquet,
Holding high assembly in the Grand Dawn.
The Four Equilibrants shall intone in clear song,
Fragrant Mothers shall waft incense smoke,
And side by side we shall behold the paired visions.
Hand in hand, our sashes intertwined—
Is this not joy?
Is this not the fulfillment of our aspirations?
O Illustrious One, may you follow the turning of fate and join the gathering,
For I shall surely not refuse.
Moreover, I myself cannot turn from truth to return to darkness,
So long as I may follow the promptings of my heart.

When the transmission was complete, she took the text back to examine it once more, then said:
“Now I present this letter to you,
That it may dispel all lingering doubts.”

Having spoken, she laughed,
And after a long while,
The Lady of the Purple Tenuity said:
“The words of the Perfected Consort are now exhausted,
And the bonds of affection are firmly established.
You can no longer entertain any hesitation.
The dark workings of fate and hidden allotment have made it so.”

The Lady of the Southern Marchmount, having received the letter, said:
“Hidden destinies and numbered influences have moved in accord,
And the dark workings of fate have aligned.
By karmic portion, you have come to be betrothed,
Newly weaving the threads of this bond—
A fine matter indeed for those who join in truth.
It is but to manifest the name of paired counterparts,
To define the roles within and without,
Not to blindly follow the corrupt and defiled ways of the world,
Nor to tread the lower paths of licentious impurity.
To couple with a numinous consort and meet the radiant scene,
To be betrothed to a noble Perfected maiden—
In such intimate communion,
There is great benefit for the advancement of your practice,
And no cause for fear of severance or harm.
The thousand spirits may now be made to witness,
And no further objections may be raised.
The Perfected Banner shall surely be able to proceed,
And the clouds shall surely be able to bear our shared chariot.”

“I once before, through the Lady of the Purple Tenuity,
Conveyed this intent to you.
Now that it has come to pass as wished,
It brings me even greater delight.
Take care never again to harbor doubts in your heart.

Yesterday, in the Clear Void, I saw the Lady Li of the Golden Terrace,
Who said that you still held doubts in your heart,
That your qi and complexion bore slight signs of hesitation—
(She meant the characters should read *xinliang xinliang*).
To reject this undertaking would be no small error.
The Perfected Consort possesses the Inner True Cinnabar and Azure Jade Script of the Divine Tiger,
Which are not things that you, with your level of talent, could presume to transcribe.”

“Thus, I shall not conceal it from you. Today, as we join hands, how could it be merely about literature? We shall surely ascend the jadelike heavens on the light of dawn. If there remains anything you have not yet awakened to, you ought to quietly inquire whether it is fitting.

When the Perfected Consort saw the Lady’s letter, she laughed and said, ‘To clasp hands upon the Twin Terraces, to delight in this joyous gathering—our light and mechanism are as one, are they not?’

*True Reports, Scroll the First. True Reports, Scroll the Second. The Second Chapter: “The Turning of the Celestial Symbols.”*

The Perfected of the Clear Void bestowed the text, saying:

The Way of the Yellow and Red, the method of blending qi—these are but one of the techniques Zhang Ling received to propagate his teachings, a means for planting the seed. They are not the affairs of the Perfected. I have seen many who practiced this and cut off their posterity, yet never one who cultivated it and attained life. Among millions, none escape examination and punishment. Among tens of millions, perhaps one may chance upon it, and even then, only attain a distant semblance of deathlessness. Zhang Ling transmitted this to teach the world, yet even he did not practice such transformations.

Take care never to speak of these base, worldly Ways, for they corrupt the true qi of the celestial realms. To harbor lustful thoughts, to fix the mind on the observation of sensual forms, and yet claim to practice the supreme Way—this only serves to make plain the Three Bureaus’ examination and punishment. It is like embracing jade and leaping into fire, or burying a dog in a golden coffin.

The observation of sensual forms is called the Yellow and Red. The supreme Way is called the Hidden Scriptures.”

The depths of human ignorance reach such extremes. The Lady of Purple Tenuity bestowed these scriptures, saying: "The Yellow Script and the Red Realm, though secrets of longevity, are in truth inferior techniques for attaining life—far from what the perfected immortals of the Upper Palace, who wander in the radiance of the celestial scenes, may speak of. This Way serves merely to nurture and propagate life, not the supreme Dao.

Those who harbor lustful qi while attempting to practice the Hidden Scriptures only grasp the Water Bureau’s brush and sound the Three Bureaus’ drums. Even the Mysterious Stem cannot be relied upon, nor can liberation be depended upon. In short: purity invokes the descent of spirits; devotion commands the service of gods.

When true persons pair with their luminous counterparts, what they value lies in the union of equals, their mutual love resting in the two radiant forms. Though called husband and wife, they leave no trace of conjugal acts. This is but an empty name to guide perception. Should the Yellow and Red linger in one’s heart, even true persons cannot be encountered, nor can numinous beings be approached. One toils in vain at such practices, only to labor further under the Three Bureaus’ scrutiny."

At the hour of the cock’s crow, the Lady of the Southern Marchmount bestowed a writ, saying: “Now that the cock has crowed, the bond of affection is deep indeed.” The Perfected of Purple Yang bestowed a writ, saying: “The Great Void stretches far and free; high and low meet as one. The meaning of embodying worthiness is made manifest in the unseen workings of fate. Guard your heart against the doubts of the Yellow and the Red.”

The Lord of Mao Peak bestowed a writ, saying: “The mysterious standard touches the luminous scene; bowing low, it harmonizes with the dust and mist. The jade chime sounds in the chamber of transgression; the pure wind soars free. Can you not be exhorted to this?” With these words, the perfected ones departed. The True Consort lingered briefly behind, saying: “I trouble you, Illustrious Lord, to compose one more verse.” And she bestowed a writ, saying:

“Forget the orchid’s purity, and let your radiant heart align in perfect accord. Soon you shall frequently and reverently purify the celestial precincts, where your virtue will merge with the flowing light. It is fitting that joy arise from the principle of union. Lead the flourishing and submit to the measure. Illustrious Lord, your lofty spirit shines—cast aside stagnation and forget baseness.”

With these words, she took his hand and stepped down from the couch. Before they reached the doorway, she suddenly vanished.

On the night of the twenty-sixth day of the sixth month, eight perfected ones descended: the Lady of the Left of Purple Tenuity, first; the True Consort of the Nine Flowers of the Upper Clarity Palace, second; the Lady of the Southern Marchmount, Controller of Destinies and Perfected of the Upper Realms, third; the Perfected of Purple Yang, fourth; the Perfected of Pure Numinosity, fifth; the Lord of Mao Peak, sixth; the Lesser Lord of Mao, seventh; and one other, very young and poised, wearing a lotus crown and a crimson robe with a sword at her side—one never before seen. It was surmised she might be the Perfected Wang Ziqiao of Mount Tongbai. Much was discussed of matters on Mount Jinting, though many words were unintelligible.

The Perfected of Purple Tenuity and the Upper Perfected of the Nine Flowers Consort were revered. All bowed and addressed themselves as “your subordinate.”

The Upper Perfected said: “Yesterday, I went with Shushen to the Palace of Pure Emptiness to review the gains and losses of the perfected as immortals. Recently, forty-seven were abruptly removed, and only three were restored. We also reviewed the registers of your names, and all is well now. Xu is listed among the foremost ranks.” (Xu was the name of the Prefect; Yang Jun had submitted a memorial, so the name was not recorded.)

“I did not initially realize it was like this—how much better it is! His diligent refinement of the heart, his devotion to principle, his heart like cinnabar and intent exhausted—he treads as though upon ice and fire. If he persists thus, even the perfected cannot escape, nor can the Dao of immortality remain hidden. He must only sever all thoughts of lust and desire, and we shall soon be able to meet. This should be made clear to him.” These were the words of the Lady of the Southern Marchmount.

The Lord of Mao Peak said: “Boju is in my charge. The Great Venerable One will surely take note. In the lands east of the Yangtze, none has been seen so devoted to the Dao. Yet do not rely on Boju’s rank and forget the Way. Falsehood is the sickness of virtue; ostentation is the calamity of the body. Stagnation is the first loss; shame is the lock of the body. Dispel these four difficulties, and only then may one inquire of the Dao.”

Then the numinous chariot’s traces resounded, and the day grew faint. “If there is any thought of transgression, do not practice the Way of the Upper Perfected. Yesterday, I saw the Palace of Pure Emptiness strike these names from the rolls, and they were then subjected to examination and punishment, their fates handed over to the Three Bureaus. Can one not be cautious?”

The words to the right are those of the Lady of the Southern Marchmount: “Prefect Xu, be mindful during the year of mourning for the deceased. This is shown to the Immortal Marquis Xu thus.” (These are the words of the Lesser Lord.)

(With a great laugh upon finishing her words:) "Once the heart of stinginess is forgotten, what one gains will differ entirely. If base shame is not dispelled, one’s name shall not be inscribed in the Register of Life. Though Prefect Xu has already been {temporarily} removed, he must be repeatedly purged again and again." (These are the words of the Pure Numinous One.)

The Eastern Minister of Destiny knows well Prefect Xu’s reverent solemnity. The Lesser Heavenly King inquired yesterday: "Where does this man now reside? What Dao does he cultivate?" The Eastern Minister replied: "He is a scholar of my native region." (By "native region," this refers to Jurong and Mount Mao sharing the same territory—not that he is originally from Xianyang.) "Inwardly, he is enlightened and upright; outwardly, he blends with worldly affairs. Truly a man of fine talent. Now he cultivates the Dao of the Upper Perfected." These words accord with human sentiment, though they bear a trace of ostentation. (These are the words of the Lady of the Southern Marchmount.)

The following is from the twenty-fourth day of the sixth month. (All twenty-four entries bear Yang’s calligraphy.)

Xiao {Jinmao} is a man of true talent, inwardly reflective and outwardly harmonious. Like Zeng Shen leaving the fields, his cinnabar heart shares the same boat. Like undyed silk thrice moved, he comes to shelter the square-headed. (These four lines form an acrostic composing the graph *Sixuan*—the courtesy name of the Prefect.)

His name is recorded in the Great Ultimate; in golden script, he is inscribed in the Eastern Land. Seven times he has ascended in trailing robes; rapt, he congeals in the Grotto Chamber. Once inner burdens are dissolved, both hun and po grow supple. Guard this without weariness; accumulate it without cease. The Five Difficulties dispelled, he shall be enfeoffed as a marquis. (The sevenfold ascent refers to the practice of flying paces; the Grotto Chamber, to the affairs of the Cavernous Chamber.)

The above is what the Lady of the Purple Tenuity conveyed, to be shown to Prefect Xu.

The following entry was written by the Prefect himself:
The Lady of the Purple Tenuity instructed: "Unfurl the side-clouds of the flowery canopy..." (This matter appears in the third scroll.)

On the night of the twenty-seventh day of the sixth month, this was written. The following entry bears Yang’s calligraphy:

When accumulated essence evokes response, the myriad things all answer. If subtle sincerity is not yet complete, then the radiance of form remains imperfect. If the radiance of form is imperfect, then within the Grotto Chamber, clarity shall not be immediately attained. When I first received this method, I would always visualize it toward the northwest. Visualizing the northwest as small makes it easier to perceive. This may be clearly demonstrated thus. (The northwest is the luminous axis of Heaven and Earth, the mysterious gate of inner illumination.)

On the twenty-seventh day of the sixth month, this was conveyed by the Purple Yang. (On this twenty-seventh day, the host of perfected ones descended again, and the corresponding events were numerous, though none are recorded here.)

Here follows the translation:

---

This passage was transcribed by the Prefectural Secretary. The two lords each had six attendants. Lord Pei’s follower bore a staff adorned with green tassels, and one attendant carried an embroidered satchel. Lord Zhou’s follower bore a staff adorned with yellow tassels (without a satchel). These two passages were written in Master Jia’s own hand.

On the twenty-ninth day of the sixth month, the Perfected Consort of Ninefold Splendor bestowed this writing, saying:

When twin luminaries shine in response, clouds gather and the mysterious descends. The dragon flourishes in the five voids, plucking jade upon the {Gate of Goodness} Terrace. A long chant in the numinous {scarf’s silence}, the jade portals open in radiance. How distant are the affairs left behind, forever parted from the world! Crimson waves bear the rosy chariot, lightning hastens to the purple abode. Together we carry the resonance beyond purity, roaming the cloudy peaks and boundless cliffs. Is this not excellence? Is this not joy?

The sun is the fruit of the rosy clouds; the rosy clouds are the essence of the sun. You have only heard of the method for ingesting the sun’s fruit, yet have not seen or known the art of consuming the clouds’ essence. The Scripture of Cloud-Consuming is most secret, but the Way of Attracting Clouds is most easy. This is called the method of embodying life so that jade radiance and rosy clouds illumine the Upper Clarity.

The eyes are the body’s mirrors; the ears are the body’s {leaf-gates}. Gazing excessively dims the mirrors; listening too much seals the {leaf-gates}. I possess the stone for polishing mirrors and the technique for unsealing {leaf-gates}. With these, one may penetrate the myriad spirits and subtly perceive the most distant echoes. Is this acceptable?

The face is the courtyard of the spirit; the hair is the blossom of the brain. When the heart grieves, the face {scorches}; when the brain diminishes, the hair whitens. Thus the inner essence is lost, and the cinnabar fluids are depleted. I possess the Scripture of Youthful Countenance and the method for restoring whiteness. Is this acceptable?

Essence is the spirit of the body; clarity is the treasure of the self. Overwork scatters essence; excessive scheming dissipates clarity. Thus old age follows the decline of qi, and senility soon arrives. I possess the Way of Nurturing Essence and the Scripture of Prolonging Clarity. Is this acceptable?

---

These four Ways are the verified true chapters of the Shangqing Inner Scriptures. I now present them to you to aid and enhance your luminous illumination. Upon completion of the transmission, I shall bestow them upon you.

I respectfully assented, repeatedly entreating her favor.

On the night of the twenty-ninth day of the sixth month, the Perfected One of Tongbai descended together with her. Again, she instructed me to transcribe, saying:

The Eight Vastnesses and Four Poles are distant, their numinous peaks remote. Marvelous words sprout forth like buds; jade-like tones resound with vibrancy. At dawn, one soars over the pure ridges; mystic qi ascends to the heavens. The body transcends the Jade Void; the heart leaves behind all hardship and peril. One abides beyond the subtlest net, congealing harmony upon the still waves. Such a person shall surely revolve through the dark Han, pervading the true courts of the immortals. The Three Primes may then be seen, and a crimson name may be established.

Yet if one’s heart is swept away by reckless waves, the eyes fixed upon the hues of desire—if in movement one shares the snares of the deceptive, and in stillness stirs the seeds of contention—then this is but the semblance of progress on the immortal’s path, a widening gulf from the birth of true life. You must be vigilant.

When I finished transcribing, I received and examined the text, which was then bestowed upon me.

*(The preceding was the discourse of Tongbai. On the same evening, after Lady An had completed her transmission, Tongbai next [orally imparted] his instructions—hence it is called a "further transmission." Upon final review, it appeared as though it were still Lady An, thus this note is appended.)*

On the night of the thirtieth day of the sixth month.

The Nineflower Perfected Consort descended together with the Lady of the Purple Tenuity and the Lady of the Southern Marchmount. After the Perfected Consort had sat for a long while, she commanded her attendant maidens to open the brocade satchel and produce two scrolls, which she presented for transcription. Their titles are as follows:

*The Esoteric Writ of the Jade Radiance and Purple Glow: An Inner Vision*
*The Scripture of Returning to Dawn and Rejoining the Sun’s Light: The Central Mystery of the Youthful Brilliance*

(These two titles should properly belong to the scriptures of the Three Origins and Eight Convergences. Since Master Yang has thoroughly mastered the true characters, they are now rendered in clerical script for clarity.)

On the night of the first day of the seventh month, the Lady of the Purple Tenuity, the Lady of the Southern Marchmount, the Nineflower Perfected Consort, Ziyang, Tongbai, the Three Perfected Ones of Pristine Emptiness, and the Second Lord of Mao descended together. After a long while, I humbly presented myself before the assembled spirits, seeking the art of securing my person, desiring to know the distinction between noble and base, the convergence of lifespan and destiny, and the fixed limits of longevity. Thereupon the Perfected Consort smiled. After a long pause, she bestowed upon me this writing, which states:

The illustrious lord possesses a nature of serene simplicity, his mind untrammeled and bright. His virtue flows like an orchid spring, his pure resonance echoes through the golden palace. Truly, he is one who treasures hidden marvels, whose inner radiance shines with the light of secluded perfection. His spirit soars through the numinous scriptures, riding the numbers to harmonize with life. His pristine power dwells in the divine garden, his cinnabar record inscribed in the Jade Purity. He ascends in mist, seizing the light, his dark drum sounding afar. He is destined to become one of the Three Excellencies, attending the Celestial Emperor at dawn, a lofty assistant to the Four Counsels, bearing the commands of the Sagely Lord. He shall govern life and sever death, reward and punish spirits, command the thousand numina, seal mountains and summon clouds. He shall oversee the harmonious qi of yin and yang and be appointed as the Lord of the Ghosts and Spirits of Wu and Yue.

As for me, I was born of the flowering essence, my destiny congealed in contemplation. I soar through the nine heavens on the wings of the void, my ethereal voice riding the whirlwind chamber. Following the turning of the Four Awakenings, I ascend the mysterious ladder in unison with the image. My purple name is recorded in the Supreme, my pure script among the Eight Effulgences. My spirit illumines the western glow, my power shines within the inner ranks. Thus, I received the scriptures and rode the qi, attaining the office of Perfected Consort.

Moreover, I am to assist you in unifying the Three Huos, governing the myriad spirits, facing the North Emperor to receive your mandate, and issuing decrees to the mountains. We are also fated to join sleeves in the numinous chamber, riding the mist of the Seven Origins, gathering in the rare grove, our inner thoughts intertwined in karmic affinity. Therefore, your surname is Yang, and I am named An. I descended from the mysterious origin, while you received the scriptures in the Western Palace. From the north, you wield the luminous tally; from the east, you ride the turning axle.

Holding the yak-tail banner and grasping the battle-axe, you govern the eastern marches with sole authority. The Three Offices present their tributes, the rivers and mountains reveal their sources. The Celestial Soldiers offer their martial prowess, the Four Armored Ones guard the wheels. At this time, it is truly the height of your nobility, the grand spectacle of Perfected Immortals.

Among the Three Offices, there has long been a saying:
*"Yang and An, Great Lords,
Stewards of the Perfected Mandate—*
this refers precisely to us. For twenty-eight years now, you have been the Sage Sovereign’s equal in rank. In another twenty-two years, you shall ride the dragon and mount the clouds, ascending to heaven in broad daylight. First, you will journey to the Western Palace of Supreme Purity, paying homage to the Jade Emperor of the Three Origins in the northern court. Only then will you assume your duties at the eastern chariot.

This is because your jade-like clarity illumines the Purple Tenuity, your golden tone resonates in emptiness, and you are commended by the Great Ultimate. Your profound virtue rises naturally—no longer need you toil in arduous study or traverse mountains and rivers. If you exert yourself in refinement, you will attain a slight luminous purity, though this is hardly as effortless as your present ascent.

Yet worldly entanglements weave distinctions of noble and base, and mortals labor through the dusty paths of gain and loss."

Indeed, this is not something a true person should strive to manage—it is but the natural unfolding of ease and adversity, the spontaneous encounter with fortune or misfortune. When I witness your leisurely ascent, I am truly overjoyed; when I observe your setbacks, my countenance darkens with sorrow. These two emotions manifest upon my face, yet they are hardly sufficient to give rise to profound lament or enduring grief.

As for the hidden depths where kindred spirits meet, where black-haired companions share a love for the mysterious, where the light wheel of dust and mist intermingles with the forms of the worldly abode—how could I, on account of fleeting transgressions or the lowly bonds of youthful stagnation, bring shame upon the steadfast essence of one destined for transcendence? For yin and yang stand in opposition, and fortune and misfortune reverse their course. The two images being arrayed, gain and loss intertwine—these are but the paths of coming and going.

Now, those who dwell in the flourishing respite of the windblown dust are often the sinful ghosts of the lower realms, the doomed essences hastening toward death. Only by abiding in uselessness amid the clamor of the world does one attain the uncarved simplicity of the true; only by embracing the ordinary within and gazing inward does one plant the root of numinous immortality. Wealth and nobility, indulgence and splendor—these are the axes and saws that break the bones, akin to the carts and boats that bear the condemned. Glory and pride, contention and the pursuit of fleeting advantage—these are but the means to invite transgression and humiliation, the weapons that sever the thread of life. They are no fine thing.

Thus, the lofty ones of antiquity, perceiving the difficulty of foreseeing faults and the impossibility of enjoying wealth and honor, retreated into the depths of secluded forests, dwelling in the radiance of renowned mountains. They chewed the harmonious qi, rinsed and bathed in pure streams, seeking to distance themselves from these evil traces and secure their own abundant blessings. They soared freely, preserving their pristine essence.

Why, then, should you hasten after the distinctions of noble and base in the human realm, casting yourself into the marketplace of glory and disgrace? Moreover, the days of clashing armies draw near, and the three disasters approach. Divine winds sweep away the foul, and putrid vapors rise to the heavens. Bright metal is born in filth and mire, precious jade is cast into dung to attract dust. Cold garments are shaken free of blood, impure essence depletes the true. The mysterious Dao flees far into the distance.

At such a time, if you cannot endure the smoke of wind and fire and wish to embrace your true form in secluded forests, you may seek the Way of unbuckling the sword and practice the art of bidding farewell to the world. From the moment of parting at the gathering of darkened mouths, the traces of concealment and revelation will be determined by circumstance, entrusted to the discernment of the enlightened lord. Heavenly destiny responds to profound resonance, and connections are made by fate. The numinous script on the jade terrace aligns with the true契, merging with the radiance. Thus, words are few in speech, and the heart is exhausted by the brush. How could I alone sigh for one person? This is but an example of the division of names and roles.

When the writing was finished, she took it and gave it to so-and-so, then asked again, "Does this bring you some relief upon reflection?"

From the twenty-ninth day of the sixth month onward, there were fourteen entries in all, including writings recorded by Lord Yang. At the fourth watch last night, the Eastern Minister descended for an audience. He was accompanied by seven attendants. Upon entering the chamber, one held a purple-tasseled staff, another a patterned banner, one a Ten Perfections Numinous Banner, another a green talisman satchel, three bore ivory boxes, and one grasped a flowing-gold bell. He appeared younger than his two younger brothers, who had been standing in attendance. The Eastern Minister ordered them to sit, and so they sat.

After a long while, their conversation unfolded in detail.

The night before last, a divine maiden descended. I initially suspected she was a daughter of the Queen Mother of the West. Last night, she came again, confirming this. The Southern Perfection stated that she is the thirteenth daughter of the Queen Mother, named Wang Meilan, with the courtesy name Shenlin. She governs Mount Canglang and has received the scriptures, bearing the title "Cloud Forest Lady." (These two matters were briefly recorded on the night of the fifth day of the seventh month; further details will be recounted later. Thus, the Lady of Right Radiance first descended on the evenings of the third and fourth days of the seventh month.)

The two entries above were recorded by Lord Yang.

On the night of the fourth day of the seventh month in the year *yichou*, the third year of the Xingning reign of the Jin dynasty, the Lord of Life and Eastern Minister descended. He was accompanied by seven attendants. Upon entering the chamber, one held a purple-tasseled staff, another a patterned banner, one a Ten Perfections Numinous Banner, another a green talisman satchel, and three bore white ivory boxes—within which appeared to be writings. One grasped a flowing-gold bell. All attendants wore crimson robes. The Lord of Life appeared much younger than his two younger brothers. He wore a turquoise brocade *jun* cap with a purple-fur *jinpi* lining and a hibiscus crown. His two brothers had also come, standing in attendance until he ordered them to sit, and so they sat.

After speaking at length, on the night of the sixth day of the seventh month, the Lord of Life descended again. Following a long interval, he instructed the scribe, saying:

"If one must model oneself upon Fan Xuan, grasping the celestial patterns in purity rare among the age, then one may pluck the hidden blossoms of the deep and soar to lofty perches, tasting the resonance of supreme accord. Like still waters mirroring a mountain’s steadfast peak, the jade-like script lies desolate—yet to those who play with the treasures of the spirit, it awakens. Casting off worldly attachments, one tunes the zither of the pure and numinous, clarifying the luminous scene within emptiness. The Five Ways unfold in clarity, their hues transcending the waves of transformation. Desires merge with the insipid; emptiness unites with the obscure thoroughfare. Without sight, without hearing, one then approaches the subtle truth of the perfected. Profound awakening arises anew, inner virtue rounds into completion, and the spirit’s banner stands replete without. In the end, one may spur the clouds to ascend the heavens, inscribing the cinnabar records of the Lord of Life.

Yet if essence scatters amid ten thousand thoughts, life cannot be made firm. Drifting with the dust and waves, the heart fails to unite in truth—sufficient only to weary body and spirit among the crags. This would indeed mislead those who come to learn. Is the Way subtle and easy to seek, or is it arduous and difficult to attain?

Let this also be shown to Attendant Xu. (These two entries were again transcribed by the Attendant.) Attendant Xu desires to dwell in the mountains. Those who honor the Dao prize freedom from perversity; those who nestle in truth find peace in tranquil joy. Profound stillness is not the host of grand compliance, nor is fiery zeal the master of instruction. Thus, one must employ the vexations of the world to comprehend the absence of them. Is this not the meaning?

Change and decay—why must they follow the four seasons? Qi flows like breath; a thousand years pass like a lodging. Should Master Zhao not be concerned? One who trusts without doubt has already ripened in heart."

The Lord of Life spoke thus to the Lady of South Mountain: "Those who cultivate the Way ever dwell in profound tranquility and solitude, each time settling the spirit to wander in leisure. Content in their sustenance, they find sufficiency."

Gaze not toward the tombs and enclosures—
for sorrow and joy thus depart forever.
How could misfortune and obstruction ever arrive?

Each is endowed with a dwelling for the will,
each possesses the resonance of its nature.
How could one tread the perverse traces of things,
or distort one’s true vocation?

Why not indulge the utmost freedom of heaven’s standard,
and seek the inner delight of attaining the real?
Follow the secluded and pure to gladden the heart,
soothe one’s lodging to settle the mind.
Dwell on East Mountain to conceal one’s tracks,
grasp the mysterious hook in wondrous comprehension.
Preserve the隨珠 to contain illumination,
and dispel the five difficulties from the breast.

---

On the night of the fifteenth day of the seventh month,
the Lady of Purple Tenuity bestowed a letter, saying:
"Those who diligently refine their essence savor the numinous standard of the mysterious.
Those who congeal in tranquility are wrapped in the bedding of truth’s repose.
You have diligently cleansed your cinnabar heart,
striving to ascend the lofty ridge—
truly, this is the utmost handle of devotion to the Dao.
Yet the Dao is yielding, the real is empty;
guard simplicity in engaging with things.
Abide in stillness and follow your dwelling,
and the spirit will naturally shine forth.
In short, haste and impatience do not exhaust principle.
Those who oppose this only invite toil."

---

To Xu Yufu:

On the night of the fifteenth day of the seventh month,
the Perfected of Pure Numinosity bestowed a poem:

Yearning for one who soars,
now moved, now fulfilled.
Majesty does not inwardly connect;
the haughty woman is far banished.
Three and four in disarray—
entering the imperial court,
establishing eras and titles,
becoming the Great Age.
Surely you will shine forth,
as the four directors of the primal ministers.
Suddenly spreading wings,
you ascend to the Highest Clarity.

*(This is an acrostic forming the name 〈Suiyu〉.)*

---

To Xu Yufu:

*(On this night, the Middle Lady also bestowed a letter to Lord Xu,
answering his desire to know of the affairs within the Grotto-Heavens.
This is recorded in the fourth scroll.)*

Phoenixes nest in lofty trees,
plain robes gleam resplendent.
*(These eight characters form the sobriquet "Mu" for the Long Historian.)*

Tread compliance and contemplate the real,
congeal the heart in emptiness and mystery.
*(Taking these "thought" and "mystery" characters
completes the name "Long Historian.")*

The five lords’ stone is rich—
it suits your body’s convenience.
Hasten to ingest it.

To preserve youthful countenance,
thrice eight commands clarity.
Next practice the Dark and True,
unharness your carriage and rest.
You may recite the Grotto Chapters,
the Jade Blade aligns with fate.
*(These "Jade Blade" characters form the sobriquet "Yu Fu" for the Aide.
This matches the meaning of the *Qinglu* in external transmissions, hence "aligns with fate.")*

Focus the heart in lofty seclusion,
conceal your traces in quiet obscurity.
With unblemished vital qi,
take artemisia powders to dispel illness.
These are your proper tasks.
Next consume *shun* rice,
and do not neglect grains.
They will enrich marrow and banish affliction,
filling flesh and plumping skin.
Only then ascend the mountains,
chanting the Grotto’s verses and expounding its subtleties.
The Tiger of Yin with white fangs—
*(These four characters form "Yun Hu Ya.")*
also attuned to the turning of events,
you shall thus attain deathlessness.
Passing the *renchen* year,
rest beneath the flourishing trees.
Study and grasp the *Zhou Book*—
*(These eight characters form the name "Yang.")*

The Supreme Polarity plants the bamboo slips,
the golden name is Western Florescence.
Whether to practice or abstain,
naturally accords with the numinous tally.
Principle differs yet tally unites,
spirit and Grotto seek one another.
The *Dinglu* records the intermediary’s proclamations—
*(The matter of Daoist elixirs is spoken of in the *Dinglu*.)*
These all employ acrostics and metaphors for the four persons’ names,
each expounding the proper affairs of cultivation, practice, and ingestion.
Tracing the intent of the words, all connect in sequence—
yet how two persons’ speech is interwoven remains unknown.

Parables must be heeded;
heedlessness is heartless.
How could you ride the *yan* tracks
to seek this spirit in the void?
Subtle tones bear profound meaning—
apply them with care, do not treat lightly.
In all matters, respond to the divine mechanism,
and you shall preserve yourself to witness Great Peace.

To the right, Ying’s chant of this—
the *Maodinglu* speaks true admonitions.
Take note of them.
With immortal talent, do not vex the heart with crooked schemes,
and you shall attain it.
*(Words of life-preservation.)*

In the eighth month, that person must journey east to *Xiu* {暂足} for viewing. Incense must be burned. *(Parting words on life-preservation.)*

To the right: fifteen entries in all, from the year *yichou* onward. All bear Yang’s calligraphy. I revere your refined elegance and entrust my heart to your radiance. Ashamed of my faults and dullness—my vulgarity long evident—I resolve to spur myself on, to bathe in the kiln of your cultivation. May this be the threshold of my deliverance from adversity. I humbly beseech your favor and regard.

Xu Xuan, prostrate with awe, bows twice. *(The Grand Scribe’s formal name is Mi, styled Sixuan. Here he is simply called Xuan—this seems inappropriate.)*

Presented to Master Jia. *(This refers to the Grand Scribe’s hearing from Yang Xuanzhou of Ziyang that Jia Xuandao and others were overseeing the examination and verification of affairs. Hence this letter. Jia then submitted it to the Director of Destinies. The Director’s later response states: “Master Jia recently brought me this letter.” Yang’s account of the matter appears in the fourth scroll.)*

To the right: one entry, the Grand Scribe’s own handwritten copy. The Perfected of Taiyuan bestowed this text upon me and instructed me to transcribe it as follows.

If one seeks to advance {进貌} in this world, what matters most is the self. Those who seldom court external calamities shall never enter the realm of death. Thus did the scholars of old grasp the dark net to conceal their guiding thread, hide the gleaming mirror amid the tangle of affairs, concentrate spirit in the courts of mountain crags, and nurture the real at the ford of secluded valleys. Thereupon, they loosed their hair upon the high peaks, weaving the warp and weft of their lives. Radiant with luminous splendor, they gathered and absorbed the five numina, roamed the nine paths of the Dao, ascended the primordial to purify their forms, and cast their thoughts beyond the void. With no worldly affairs to entangle them, they sealed and stored the three qi, refined the wondrous essences—thus reversing the years of the sun’s decline and reverting to the state of infancy.

Yet if one’s affairs pile up like grains of sand, if carriages clog the roads, and if one’s resolve cannot be steadfastly upheld—how can the trials and verifications be brought to a halt? Things demand one another, and like breeds calamity. The gaze of Heaven and humanity does not leak with the seasons. Those who oversee reward cultivation; the trials lie in ceaseless renewal.

Master Jia recently brought me this letter, entrusting it to {亠衅且}{亠衅且}. This may be called having sentiment, yet to let slip my beam—does this not resemble deceit in reverse?

On the sixteenth day of the seventh month. *(This entry also bears a clerk’s note.)*

I have reviewed your inquiry. How earnest is your heart! You gaze toward the mountain ridges, your thoughts reaching into the distance, and joyfully turn toward the Way. I have always seen this intent in you. As for those who pursue the Dao...

To attain refinement is sufficient. Yet if one has sentiment but lacks diligence, then nothing can be accomplished. Diligence without focus likewise yields no achievement. One must ensure that stingy thoughts dissolve and disperse, that defilements and afflictions scatter and vanish. *(This also resembles Dongqing’s admonition to the Senior Scribe.)* Why do you not often gaze upon the Eastern Mountains? Yearning for the Three Peaks, lingering beneath the eaves, your eyes meet the forests and waters—yet those who have departed leave little further benefit. *(Whenever the "Three Peaks" are mentioned, they refer to the summits of Mount Sanmao, whose peaks are called "peaks of refinement.")*

**The Lady of Southern Marchmount to her disciples:**
Speech is the ruin or preservation of one’s nature and life. Trust is the hinge of gain and loss. Zhang Liang’s three appointments may be called steadfast in the Dao and enlightened in mind.

**The Lady of Southern Marchmount to her disciples:**
Her nature is most magnanimous and kind, yet what she hears is urgent, and her responses swift—this only contradicts the intent.

The matter of the fire-jujubes is not yet fitting to inquire about. *(The discussion of fire-jujubes follows later.)*

**The Perfected Consort of Jiuhua:**
