From the Taiyuan era onward, these five entries are all in Yang’s hand.

The reins of light descend to Canglang’s waves,
Leaping across the clear sea’s ford.
Crimson mists swirl beneath the sun,
Feathered canopies tilt the nine heavens.
The cloud-chariot drifts through empty vastness,
Suddenly tossed amid wind and waves.
Come seeking friends in the unseen,
Hand in hand to attend the Lord of Dawn.
The Prince of Wangzi harmonizes bright virtue,
Together they summon the jade worthies.
Below, they glance toward the Eightfold Palaces;
Above, they repose on the peaks of the rare groves.
Rinsing with purple jade’s richness,
Only then do they know the bitterness of the defiled paths.
Where now are those fine companions?
Only through diligence may one draw near.

On the evening of the eighteenth day of the seventh month, the Lady of Cloud Forest and Right Radiance bestowed this poem. *(This poem was given to the Senior Scribe, also concerning the clerk’s affairs.)*

Exalted joy in the rare groves’ emptiness,
Far wandering without bound or direction.
Desolate beyond form and number,
Being and nonbeing naturally merge in darkness.
{亠衅且}{亠衅且}’s virtue and rhythm harmonize,
Drifting, drifting, pacing the great void.
Lingering amid the waves’ ebb and flow,
Shaking bells to scatter in the wind.
Inwardly illuminating the Sevenfold Dao-Observances,
One may attain complete forgetting.
Why must one engage in endless exchanges?
Await this world’s literary communion.
The mysterious mind naturally awakens.

On the twenty-sixth evening of the seventh month, the Lady of Purple Tenuity composed this admonition for Senior Scribe Xu:

Lofty the Jasper Towers’ boundless gates,
Unfurling crimson to ascend the radiant chambers.
Purple banners stir the clouds and dawn,
Feathered auroras soothe the Eight Winds.
Pausing chariots to bathe in emerald streams,
Gathering blossoms on Moon-Support Peak.
Chewing the Threefold Numinous Flowers,
Exhaling and inhaling the Ninefold Spirit-Rays.
The cedar’s reckoning knows no end,
Harmonizing with the sun to nurture the young and ignorant.
Hand in hand, we enter the Hall of Luminous Perfection,
Gazing upward to await the Supreme August One.
At the Northern Dipper’s call, the feathered ones sing,
Jade mystery dazzles the assembly of worthies.
Clouds and rivers—how vast the celestial expanse!
Gain and loss are but my own resonance.
I crane my neck within the clamorous court,
Opening my heart to the foul and the pure.
Familiar with the realm of glory and disgrace,
Rarely do I tread the groves of emptiness.
A moment’s stillness—why cling to suffering?
Go forth and behold the azure waves.

*(This admonition was given by the Lady of Right Radiance. Three additional poems were sent with the celestial carriage, all transcribed by the Senior Scribe. The weak and bereaved drift like scattered reeds; the profound spirit remains unexhausted. Dependence and submission arise from different causes.)*

The cloud-ladder remains unreached;
though yearning stirs for onward advance,
one has yet to plumb the depths of the supreme principle.
Your talent is truly heaven-wrought, its limpid waves
congealing into lofty resonance.
Your aspiration nests the spirit in the Great Mystery,
awaiting the Purple Court to tread the void.

A heart that penetrates the stagnant and soaring,
a brush that flourishes in dark accord—
movement aligns with compass and square,
circles and squares alike;
stillness harmonizes with true savor,
breathing forth and drawing in to stir melody.
This may be called unfettered virtue, innate power—
truly a cause for reverence.

Yet impure thoughts remain unloosed,
mean attachments inwardly entrenched;
wayward longings do not recede,
the spirit-pool stays unclarified.
Thus we have not yet reached the point
to discourse on the inner and outer realms,
to navigate the confluence of the Two Radiant Ones.

For those who miss the moment,
the value lies in the power to change.
Let us release the bonds of conditioned emotion—
now is no hindrance.
Though briefly silencing the clamor of many ears,
this alone achieves harmony.

The path ahead—ever advancing—
such comparisons are not few.
The threads of leakage are manifold;
one must ever wage war in secrecy.
Should the passions scatter in error,
each affair becomes a loss.
The words of awakening are subtle—
how then to restrain them?
How then to dispel them?

On the night of the twenty-sixth day of the seventh month, a letter from Lady Youying of Yunlin to the Right King was received. "Do not reply to this." One passage was copied by the Senior Scribe.

Worldly treasures mingle in fragrant exchange,
Daoist lineages convene in the mystic firmament.
Shaking one’s robes, one seeks the hidden fields;
turning the carriage amid the winds of dust,
true virtue reflects the numinous radiance.
The sharp root blooms in splendid flourish,
secret words bring boundless fortune.
Serene purity upholds the precious real—
all things ever accord with the symbolic order.
Hand in hand, we share the same coverlet—
why dwell in the realm of human affairs,
where days breed harm and strife?

On the evening of the twenty-eighth day of the seventh month, Lady Youying of the Right King presented this poem in a letter to Senior Scribe Xu. (In his reply of the twelfth month, the Senior Scribe spoke of "all things ever accord"—this was his response to the poem. The phrase "all things ever accord" derives from the *Zhouyi*.)

One passage was copied by the Senior Scribe:

Pure echoes scatter through the void,
a divine wind washes the forest.
The body transcends the dark thoroughfare,
the will chants the numinous tone—
such is the man of benevolent nobility.
To show the origins and end of Master Pei to {Xiyin} would suffice.
This must surely harmonize.
Yet if the heart of unskillful guidance is inwardly revealed,
what manner of man is Pei?
({Xiyin} is {Xinyin}, childhood name Fanghui. The origins and end of Master Pei refer to the *Qingling Zhuan*. There are those who have repented their errors and those who master the Seven Classics—thus he was instructed to show them.)

On the evening of the seventh day of the eighth month, the Lady of Right Excellence presented a letter, instructing it be delivered to Senior Scribe Xu. The following passage was transcribed by Yang. Another was copied by the Senior Scribe:

One who steadfastly guards the True Unity—within a year, their hair ceases to whiten, and fallen locks regrow. Yet if one is inwardly bound to children and grandchildren, shackled by household affairs, and outwardly entangled in royal duties and the ties of friendship—ears and eyes overtaxed, voice and qi dispersed in service—then the Dao is not single-minded, and one’s conduct yields no benefit.

Those of true talent are often recluses, dwelling deep in forests and mountains, far from the world of men, embracing simplicity. Then must their countenance be like *Ziying*’s, their temples dark as mystery. Jade nectar and golden brew, fire-jujubes and intertwined pears—these are the medicines of ascension, not to be compared with golden elixirs.

Yet the benevolent noble’s body has not attained true correctness; impure thoughts fill his heart. I fear such beings will not deign to come. If genuine sincerity is not unified, the Dao too is without partiality—one ought not even inquire. The trees of fire-jujubes and intertwined pears have already taken root in your heart. But if thorns and brambles still mingle there, the two trees remain unseen. I wonder if you might prune the brambles to let these trees grow alone—how fine their fruit would be!

Though this be called a question.

To seek proximity to these mysteries, you should inquire of the presiding overseer. For three years, we shall correspond thus, beginning from this day. On the seventh night of the eighth month in the *chou* year (these two characters were later added by Director Xu), Cloud-Forest Right Radiance Queen Lady Wang orally transmitted this answer to Director Xu:

Those who calm the heart and empty the form, inwardly observe the inner chambers, embrace the mysterious and contemplate the divine, and single-mindedly guard the True One—such ones’ hair will not turn white, and the bald shall regrow their locks. (The character *zhen* here should be *fa-zhen* ["hair and truth"]. The *Yunji qiqian*, fascicle 92, *Record of the Words of the Many Perfected*, reads: "Now, those whose breasts are tangled with a hundred thoughts, whose spirits are shattered by cold and heat, who attend to official duties amid this world of dust, whose mouths speak of auspicious and inauspicious meetings, whose bodies dwell in the gates of gain and loss—with such manifold cares and ten thousand anxieties as these, though they may possess a true heart, it is surely not steadfast. To embrace the Dao yet not practice it, to grasp the treasure yet not employ it, and still to hope that one’s hair will not turn white—such a thing is rarely heard of.

Jade nectar and golden brew, intertwined spirit-pears, square-foot fire-jujubes, and dark-light magic mushrooms—I shall grant these to the Daoist Master Xu in the mountains, not to Director Xu in the world of men."

On the seventh night of the eighth month, Purple Tenuity Queen Lady Wang transmitted this answer to Director Xu.

The above six clauses were copied by an aide.

I intend to ride east to the mountain peaks,
To pause my light and summon the hidden and still.
Virtue borne on waves arrives,
Together we meet at Triple-Mushroom Ridge.
The magic mushrooms are indeed edible,
Granting you endless longevity.
With true reverence, offer the golden brew,
No need to wait for the hundred-fathom well.

On the sixteenth evening of the eighth month, the Pure Numinous Perfected transmitted this. The above piece was copied by Director Xu.

Emptiness and harmony may be guarded with strength,
Stillness and solitude may be guarded with softness.
Now, this stillness and solitude—this is the solitary light’s lone journey.
Within your Crimson Palace, can you ascend to the utmost clouds’ dark and distant edge?

The Dao is easy to hear of, but the trouble lies in its not being true.
Books are easy to obtain, but the trouble lies in their not being practiced.

Should one devote oneself solely to this,
Within the vast heavens,
True immortals would stand shoulder to shoulder.
I bear no fault toward those who cannot achieve it.
If the mind is unsettled yet one seeks to inscribe,
Does one intend to sell it?
If the will does not turn toward the real yet one pursues truth,
Does it not seem one seeks to display it?

With hope, I convey this.
On the night of the seventeenth of the eighth month,
The Lady of Right Florescence transmitted this writing
To Director Xu.
*(This appears to answer his quest for the true, feminine aspect of the One.)*

The first ancestor planted virtue—
The flowering branch of the Weng lineage *(referring to the seventh-generation ancestor, Xu Zhao)*.
To halt one’s steps and suspend one’s carriage,
There is no "too early" or "too late."
Simply let the heart firmly fix upon the real,
And the subtle, numinous mechanism will suffice.
As for soaring to lofty ridges,
Or slumbering in dark forests and marshes,
Disdaining the base affairs of the times,
Abandoning the nine relations to savor the divine—
These are indeed noble pursuits.
Yet if the heart is not single-minded,
And wayward thoughts fill the breast,
Though one treads the peaks of *

Last spring, the master of scriptures instructed me in the Way of the *fangzhu* and the pacing of the Grotto-Chambers, gradually cultivating the Eight Simplicities and the Nine Perfected. I dared not grow remiss in heart. Yet the Nine Perfected require profound stillness—worldly affairs entangle, and the trouble lies in lack of singleness.

Of old, those who sought the Dao would seek teachers and companions, accumulating years upon years, traversing mountains and peaks without cease, enduring hardship and peril, tasting every toil. Only then would they be entrusted with the essential instructions.

My virtue is meager, my transgressions weighty. Seated upright in my chamber of faults, I have nonetheless been selected and recorded by the host of Perfected. Warnings and admonitions have come in succession, awakening me time and again.

As the ancients said: "Not knowing is not the difficulty—practicing is." The grace you have bestowed, my lady, may unfold at its own pace. *(This "must" is the Prefect’s own hand, altering "the perilous crags of men.")* First, I shall move to the Eastern Mountains, and only then receive your direct transmission.

The coming of the Dao does not reckon swiftness or slowness; the height of your favor knows no bounds of early or late. Commanded by your envoy, how dare I not respond in kind? With reverence, I submit this reply.

(This is the Prefect’s reply to the previous discourse on the feminine aspect of the Right Radiance. The clerk transcribed it, and after the perilous crags were altered, this copy was preserved.)

*Declarations of the Perfected, Scroll the Second.*
*Declarations of the Perfected, Scroll the Third.*
*Book of Circulating Images, Chapter Three.*

During the Northern Prime of the Primal Mystery, the Lady of Numinous Illumination of the Eastern Palace—younger sister of Li Lingfei, the Jade Youth and Grand Protector, and daughter of Li Qingbin, the Dao Lord of the Northern Mystery—resided in the Vermilion Pavilion of the Thirteenth Terrace of the Square-Zhang Terrace. The Lady wore a robe of purple brocade, bore the talisman of the Divine Tiger, and held a bell of flowing gold. Two handmaidens attended her, both around twenty years of age. The Lady herself appeared to be thirteen or fourteen. She summoned one of the handmaidens, named Hidden Radiance. Both handmaidens wore robes of turquoise damask and carried two crimson jade caskets bound with azure cords. The white jade seals bore the inscriptions *Supreme Petition* and *Supreme Writ*. (This note [identifies] the Yu edition’s correction from “weave” to “inscribe,” matching the earlier Nine Flowers passage.)

The Lady wore a sash of bluish-jade hue, resembling the insignia pouch of mortals. The concealed petition measured some five *zhang* in length and three to four *chi* in width. As she prepared to depart, she presented a single sheet of verse, then chanted:

The earthly bonds embrace Heaven’s frame,
Sevenfold qi illumines the divine soaring.
Jade fans unfold at dawn’s first cry,
Nine tones resound within the crimson pivot.
Purple auroras rise at the vermilion gate,
Incense smoke drifts from the emerald window.
Four chariots dance with tiger-banners,
Azure wheels spin through the dark void.
Canopies of blossoms trail the clouds,
Falling phoenixes rein six dragons.
Riding the light, I course the Five Peaks’ slopes,
The Three Pristine gaze upon the Lord’s chamber.

As I just heard the foul *qi* of fleshly corruption,
The myriad impurities surge and churn within my breast.
Vile things assail the spirit with their stench,
Clamorous dusts clash and collide.
Bright jade—all is shattered and crushed—
Why alone does the body of sublime virtue endure?
Had I but raised my hands in parting sooner,
I would not now sit here, worms breeding in the earth.

On the night of the twenty-second day of the eighth month, the Lady of Numinous Radiance presented this verse.

(Here the Prefect writes "Lady of Numinous Radiance," while Master Yang’s text often reads "Radiance of the Numinous.")

As she prepared to depart, she chanted:
Let not the heart be swayed by chaos,
Let not the spirit be enslaved by dissipation.
When the Dao turns adverse, do not defy it;
When calamity weighs heavy, do not resist.
To lose one’s true nature forever—
Is to forsake my destined path.
Will I be reborn in the Xu family again?
I shall return when the time is right.
Strive on, and that is all.

The above eight passages from the Northern Origin were transcribed by the Prefect. King Ling of Zhou had thirty-eight sons; Prince Jin was the crown prince, known as Wang Ziqiao. The king’s third daughter, named Guanxiang (style name Zhong’ai), was the daughter of Lady Song. To Ziqiao, she was a half-sister by a different mother. She received from Ziqiao the Dao of flying liberation from the snares of the world and departed to dwell in the mountains of the Wei clan. Later, together with Ziqiao, she entered Luhun, where they remained for thirty-nine years.

Guanxiang attained the Dao and was appointed as the Inner Transmitted Consort of the Purple Clarity Palace, assuming the title of Lady of the True One in the Eastern Palace (this being the Lady of the True One, the King’s Consort). Seven of Ziqiao’s siblings achieved the Dao (five sons and two daughters). Among them, Meishou was Guanxiang’s full brother and likewise attained the Dao. (This appears to refer to a separate account of Meishou, now lost; however, in the records of Yuan’s writings, there is a dream in which someone says, “I am the younger sister of Wang Meishou.” This may well be the response.)

The above two passages were transcribed by Yang.

Riding the blazing chariot through the eight voids,
I linger in revelry within the Eastern Flower Chamber.
The Celestial Mother invites me to her pavilion,
Where I chant aloud, treading the numinous wind.
I came because I awaited the appointed time,
Thus did I cross the azure waves.

*Song of Lady Ying, the Right Consort*

Ascending the nine heavens against the whirlwind,
I rest my carriage at the Three Radiance Peak.
I tarry, gazing all around, for I await my time;
Without such waiting, one should simply be pure.
Why trouble oneself with the azure waves?
How could they compare to crossing the Dark Well?

*Lady of the Purple Tenuity’s Response to the Right Consort’s Song*

Within my golden court I inscribe these words,
Unbridling my carriage at the Three Radiance Precinct.
Night mushrooms unfold their blossoms,
Their petals chewed to sate eternal hunger.
I chant aloud, yet find no freedom—
Each verse arises from the waiting song.
The Hollow Cavern echoes with the numinous sound;
What then shall become of those without such waiting?

*Song of the Perfected One of Mount Tongbai*

At dawn I roam Mount Yujué,
At dusk I repose in the Hall of Lofty Radiance.
I shake my reins and tread the numinous peak—
No nearness to the azure waves.
At the three-*ren* verge of the Dark Well,
My steed finds no ford.
In the vast expanse of ninety thousand leagues,
The eight directions lie in full view.
To have waiting is not yet to reach the ultimate void;
The numinous sound suffers loss therein.

*Song of the Perfected One of Pure Numinosity*

Dragon banners dance in the Great Void,
Flying wheels course the slopes of the Five Peaks.
Wherever I go, all is free and unbound.
Moved by feeling, I chant a song of the unseen;
Without waiting surpasses having waiting.
When we meet, harmony is thus attained.
Why deem the azure waves too distant?
The Dark Well is not too much.
In the space of a single step through Yujué,
All beneath the four seas is gathered.
How could it compare to beyond the radiance of light,
Where three kalpas pass but once?

*Song of the Lady of the Central Watch*

Freely drinking, I observe the many blessings—
Suddenly, all four directions encircle me.
I know not how this comes to be,
For in truth, this is no journey of waiting.
When we meet, all is joy;
When we do not, there is no sorrow.
My form wanders the dark void,
And the two meetings naturally align.

*Song of Lady Li of Illustrious Numinosity*

I drive my carriage forth from Western Splendor,
Between having waiting and having none.
Now I gaze upon the peaks of the Five Peaks,
Now I bathe in the ford of the Celestial River.
I release my wheels to seek the empty boat;
Wherever I go, all is bound in tenderness.
A mustard seed suddenly becomes ten thousand acres,
Within it stands Mount Sumeru.
Small and great are fundamentally no different;
Far and near share a single cause.
They come with waiting,
While I draw near without it.

*Song of Consort An of Mount Jiuhua*

Without waiting lies the Great Void’s midst,
With waiting lies the Great Having’s verge.
Great and small are one wave,
Far and near converge in a single meeting.
I pluck the strings at the summit of the dark firmament,
Chanting and whistling, I move the eight *qi*.
Why not drink deeply of the numinous nectar?
With a glance, I delight the nine lineages.
Having and lacking attain the mysterious workings;
The two waitings thus cover each other.

*Song of the Perfected One of Mount Nanyue in the Great Void*

I repose in the tranquility of Eastern Splendor,
Directing the movement of the eight directions.
Looking down upon the mounds and anthills,
I perceive not the loftiness of the Five Peaks.
The numinous mounds equal the abyssal springs,
Great and small follow one another.
Long and short, more and less—none exist.
The great *chun* tree ends in a moment.
Why not yield to heaven and follow its course?
Let the spirit roam freely in the emptiness of sameness.

*Song of the Lords of the Azure Lads of All Directions*

I rein in the whirlwind to fan the Great Void,
The Eight Effulgences soar in lofty purity.
Looking up, I float beyond the Purple Dawn;
Looking down, I gaze into the abyss of darkness.
The dark heart dwells in the emptiness of sameness,
Above and below, no flowing or halting.
Within the two bounds of having no waiting,
Having waiting has no place to abide.
Embodying nothingness, one can die;
Embodying being, one preserves life.
The eastern guests join in the lofty chant—
Why dispute the two waitings?
I command my carriage of jade and brocade,
Reins held high, I wander in contemplation.
At dawn I roam the Vermilion Fire Palace,
At dusk I feast by the Pool of Moonlight.
My floating form rests at the tip of the rosy clouds,
The eight dragons stand in uneven array.
I journey without waiting,
Yet those with waiting ever follow.
In the high gathering, the fair ones repose—
The two waitings mutually affirm and deny.
Having and lacking are not fixed;
Each waiting returns to itself.

*Song of the Lady of the Purple Prime of the Southern Culmen*

*(Note: These songs and poems all appear to be in the style of initial revelations.)*

Yet the many Perfected Ones disdain the lofty chant—
The Supreme Void of the Upper Clarity, the Lad of Purple Prime, has never known a place of mixed descent.
I fear only that these words may be lost or mislaid.
The discourse on "waiting" all refers to the affair of the Lady of Right Radiance,
not to the Consort of Peace.

I soar upon the cloud-lit axle,
floating to observe the sky above the rosy clouds.
The empyrean stretches wide in dance,
the purple canopy rests upon the numinous quarter.
Crimson mist coils round the banners and pennants,
feathered fans stir the fragrant breeze.
Lightning roars as fierce beasts seize their prey,
thunder rumbles as the dark dragons surge.
The tuned pipes resound in the courtyard of Kun,
golden reed-organs sing to the divine bells.
I pluck the magic mushrooms by the azure waves,
gather blossoms on the eight still peaks.
My crimson countenance grows ever new with each day,
though kalpas pass, I remain a child.
I nurture my form in the quiet of the eastern summit,
the seven spirits commune of themselves.
Yet the dust of the world bears sorrow and lament—
it casts me down as a white-haired elder,
long lost in distant sighs.
I regret not having fled sooner.
On the evening of the third day of the ninth month,
this was composed by the Lady Wang of Cloudy Grove,
and shown to the Chronicler Xu.
I halt my chariot, gazing as the moon’s charioteer moves on,
turning my wheels back toward the azure waves.
Before I saw the wanderings of such a one,
I idly wondered how peace might be found.
A good cause awaits the green spring,
that I may unburden my heart and forget.

*To the right: The Lady of Right Radiance chanted this again and again.*

The Tortoise Watchtower stands in solemn majesty,
the earthen terrace is strung with pearls of moonlight.
Seated in the chamber of the Nine Numinous Ones,
we strike the jade chimes and chant the Great Nothingness.
Jade flutes harmonize with my spirit,
golden nectar dispels my cares.
As the feast grows merry within the Eastern Flower,
a thousand melodies are arrayed in perfect tune.
The Azure Lord calls me to rise,
I bow low, yearning for the forest court.
Feathered fans gleam with kingfisher radiance,
how the jade pendants chime and ring!
Together we point toward the lofty morning repose,
and vow to meet in the depths of the Image.

*To the right: The Purple Tenuity chanted these two songs.*

I ascend beyond the crimson empyrean,
borne on the flying gale to the northern mound.
Divine splendor illumines the immortal terrace,
the round luminaries tilt with the wind.
I open the radiance of the Cinnabar Prime,
the gate of light feeds on the moon’s essence.
Sleeves intertwined in the cloud-grove hall,
my hair and form return to childlike freshness.
How desolate—this lodging without abode!
How could right and wrong ever be my concern?

Amidst the ranks, self-disturbance vies—
how could one speak of nurturing life?

*To the right: Composed by the Purple Tenuity of the Dark Mound.*

I rein in the dawn, floating on purple mist,
the Eight Sceneries behold the flowing melons of water.
Feathered lads bear chalices of jade nectar,
jade blossoms toast with lush laminae.
We vow to meet at the Whitewater shore,
raising my withered pearl of life.
The azure chamber gleams with eastern dawn,
the Purple Creation drifts on the crimson morn.
The Twin Virtues grasp the Dao’s essence,
establishing the true lord’s domain.
The Eight Terraces lie within my gaze—
northward, I see the Flying Origin.
In clarity and stillness, I survey from the clouds,
dimly treading the shifting light.
Exhaling and inhaling, I master the cave’s elegance,
concealing radiance behind the eastern mountain.
Long have I dwelled amidst human affairs,
each day without idle leisure.
How could it compare to transforming this aged form,
returning to a child’s countenance?

On the evening of the sixth day of the ninth month,
composed in the Cloud Grove, addressed to Lord Xu.

I unyoke my wheels at the Great Auroral Heights,
gathering reins to ascend the Purple Mound.
In hand, the Eight Emptinesses—
I cast myself afloat amid the clouds.
A single glance governs the workings of creation,
a second gaze seeks the lofty wilds.
The Dao’s essentials are now complete.

On the evening of the sixth day of the ninth month,
Purple Mictrocosm Lady composed this,
addressed to Chief Scribe Xu
and to fellow disciples—
(the fellow disciple being Fang Hui).

This can dissolve a thousand sorrows,
seeking truth, one finds true companions.
What more could one seek?

At dawn, the auroral towers are framed,
jade chambers rise in the limpid heavens.
I grasp the three wondrous visions,
floating light soars through the utmost void.
Within the cinnabar void dwell the Perfected,
golden radiance nurtures their flourishing essence.
The eight winds stir embroidered coverlets,
verdant trees illumine the four numina.
The flowered canopy spreads its orchid brilliance,
purple reins urge the green steed onward.
Binding trust, I commune with the divine,
touching all things, I follow celestial sincerity.
Why be moved by external phenomena?
One must behold the jade and jeweled splendor.

On the ninth day of the ninth month,
Cloud Grove’s Right Radiance Lady composed this.

The purple void gleams with bright light,
the Dark Palace girds the crimson river.
In solemn ranks, the Upper Clarity chambers stand,
cloud terraces gleam, towering and majestic.
Eight chariots arrive at the vermilion pool,
feathered canopies tilt toward the celestial branches.
The thunderous wind revolves the three luminaries,
golden bells scatter jade blossoms.
Seven reins weave through the nine realms,
at ease, my gaze need not return home.
I ask the seekers of the Dao:
why remain mired in the dust and waves?
How could one not nest in eastern splendor,
cultivating the true and gathering grand harmony?

On the ninth day of the ninth month,
Purple Mictrocosm Lady composed this,
addressed to Xu and to Fang Hui—
(Fang Hui being the same as before).

The twin luminaries flourish in dark luxuriance,
heavenly radiance brightens the eight directions.
Cinnabar clouds float in the lofty dawn,
carefree, I ride the numinous wind.
Beating the feathered drum, I mount the white whirlwind,
raising my gaze within the jade tower.
The green canopy enters the harmonious dawn,
the azure pennant streams through the empty sky.
To the right, I salute the Lord of the Eastern Grove,
ascending to court the Emperor of the Great Void.
Jade guests carve phoenix-brain,
roaring with delight, they drink flying-petal nectar.
Cloud hooks turn in the winding chambers,
a thousand tones—how resonant!
Broidered banners summon fierce beasts,
flowered streamers rise and fall.
Fragrant mothers bend in song,
purple mist parts the roof beams.
Gathering reins at the lofty clear gates,
I unharness my carriage in the chamber of beauties.

Yesterday’s fate bore no sign,
spiritual transformation soars with the qi’s flight.
My heart, distant, stirs at the dark shore,
years pass like the towering sandalwood.
My form delights in filth and stench,
in motion and stillness, I lose the azure waves.
Yet my friends are not thus—
glory and disgrace were forgotten long ago.

On the night of the eighteenth day of the ninth month,
Cloud Grove’s Right Radiance Lady composed this.
She declared:
My words end here.

The crimson light floats in the dark dawn,
the purple carriage rides the misty journey.
Looking up, I transcend the green gates,
gazing down, I behold the vermilion fire city.
Eastern auroras unfurl their vast brilliance,
divine radiance illumines the seven numina.
Shimmering reflections ripple the three torches,
flowing freely, I equal the void.
Wind coils through the hollow heavens,
fragrant tones arise with each measure.
Hand in hand with the weaving maidens,
we share sashes in the gourd garden.
To the left, I circle the azure feathered banner.

The flowery canopy follows the clouds in their tilt,
my tranquil rest surpasses ninefold measures.
Right and wrong do not occupy my mind—
embracing truth, I dwell in the Great Stillness.

Golden *zi* (here corrected to "form")—how could it compare
to the filth and foulness of the world,
where life is bleak and without solace?

On the night of the twenty-fifth day of the ninth month,
Cloud Grove’s Right Radiance Lady composed and transmitted this.

Three reins raise the purple carriage,
clouds tilt toward the eastern forest’s slope.
Right Radiance chanted this Dao,
and from the right, thirteen soaring verses came—
all in Yang’s hand, with some passages transcribed by scribes.

To dispel stagnation and stinginess,
one must rely on exhausting virtue’s practice—
is this not most excellent?
Do not fear that virtue will go unrewarded,
but rather that the planting of blessings is too meager.
This single line may well be a field of fortune.
All matters are thus—
one may infer the rest by analogy.

On the third day of the twelfth month,
Cloud Grove’s Right Radiance Lady spoke.
This passage is in Yang’s hand,
with another version slightly variant.

Mu, humbly and with awe, says:
Your boundless benevolence,
graciously bestowing new poems—
cloud-like elegance woven in brocade,
golden tones and jade-like brilliance—
truly the rarest bloom of the literary grove,
the grandest display of embroidered splendor.
Their meaning runs deep and subtle,
gazing upward, one finds no limit.
I wear them in my cinnabar heart,
cherishing them in every turn.
Though my merit is shallow and crude,
the unseen recompense is already weighty.
The metaphor of the field of fortune—
how dare I not rouse myself?
Relying on your noble guidance,
my gratitude is as vast as mountains and seas.
In movement and stillness, I seek enlightenment—
I hope you will deign to record my plea.

Mu, humbly and with awe, says:
Presented before the loom of Cloud Grove’s Right Radiance Lady.
(This is the reply to the letter on dispelling stagnation and stinginess,
with a draft preserved.)

The Azure Lad often chants:
"To plant the roots of extinction,
one must uproot the seeds of life and death.
Brooding, one sinks into the nine springs—
all for clinging to this bodily frame."

The Master of the Great Void often chants:
"Observe when spirit bears form—
it is like a cart following a horse.
When the cart breaks, the horse bolts and flees,
dragging along this transient union.
Alas, the world does not recognize this—
all they cherish is the wind and fire.
Planting sins in the heavenly net,
they suffer poison in the hells below."

The Perfected of Western City, Lord Wang, often chants:
"Spirit is the boat that ferries form,
but the shallow shore is where they must part.
Form is not spirit’s eternal abode,
spirit is not form’s constant bearer.
Wandering the wheel of life and death,
they suffer only from hesitation of heart."

The Perfected of Lesser Existence, Lord Wang, often chants:
"Losing the Dao, one follows the ford of death,
the three souls stray from the path of life.
The day of life grows ever distant,
the day of death arrives all too soon.
Alas, the sorrowful face of suffering—
roots and blossoms already inverted.
Rising to meet the kalpa’s fall,
how can one know the return to withered age?"

On the autumn equinox of the previous month,
at the Jade Terrace Grand Assembly,
the four lords each chanted these words,
harmonizing with the strings of the *Xuanjun Guangshao*.
(In the tenth month, it was said "the previous month"—
here corrected to "between," for the autumn equinox must fall in the eighth month,
thus "the previous month" naturally makes sense.)

On the fifteenth day of the tenth month,
Right Radiance Lady spoke this and ordered it recorded.
These five passages are in the scribes’ hand.

The four luminaries shine in the void,
the vermilion carriage flies over the numinous mound.
The jade canopy shades the seven radiances,
drums and feathered banners float above the clouds.
The nine tones resound through the purple void,
jade echoes pierce the Great Nonbeing.
Feasting and chanting in the palace of the three luminaries,
singing and calling to our companions—
unaware that the *chun* tree has already come,
how could we know the flow of the two effulgences?
Though the fair one may forget both,
a hundred sorrows are not yet released.
The long forest is truly still,
in the cliffs, there is much delight.

On the seventeenth day of the tenth month,
Cloud Grove Lady composed this for Lord Xu.

Grasping the jade flowery canopy in her left hand,
she rides the radiance, treading the seven origins.
The three luminaries gleam with purple brilliance,
she rises and gazes, caressing the bright Perfected.
In an instant, she leaps and transforms—
all four sides are already divine.
Her numinous hair knows no bounds,
earnestly pondering the scriptures of the Upper Clarity.
Why does this random *shuiyu* arise,
causing you to lose focus?
Losing the *xuan* mechanism in a flash—
unaware that the years have parted.

On the eighteenth day of the tenth month.

Purple Tenuity Lady composed this.

The two preceding pieces bear Yang’s calligraphy.

Northward we ascend the Gate of Dark Perfection,
hand in hand weaving the lofty net.
Fragrant smoke scatters across the Eight Sceneries,
the Dark Wind stirs the crimson waves.
Gazing upward, we transcend the Ford of Lang Garden;
looking down, we glimpse the slopes of Cloudy Mound.
Jade flutes sing above the clouds,
phoenixes cry in the Nine Distances.
Riding qi, we float through the Great Void—
why tread upon mountains and rivers?
With golden tally we summon the feathered numina,
our marching host shatters the ten thousand demons.
Together we grasp the twin morning glories,
a thousand kalpas yet in infancy.
Losing the Real, we plunge into the chamber of strife—
how could one not understand this?
Lifting our eyes to the Palace of Great Radiance,
golden pavilions gleam with Purple Clarity.
Flowering chambers reflect the Great Simplicity,
all four porticoes are of vermilion jasper.
We cast our wheels into the Ford of Empty Sameness,
gathering the reins in verdant dance.
Jade blossoms fly as cloudy canopies,
the Western Consort unfurls her brocade banner.
Suddenly we turn beyond the shores of turbid dust,
in an instant we arrive at the courtyard of the fair one.
Long-awaited resonance brings timely descent—
what was summoned now dwells in darkness.
Riding the wind, we offer dawn’s melody,
together we feast from the cinnabar-jade flasks.
Dukes and lords are but fleeting shadows—
how could they know the numen of the Perfected?

The two preceding pieces were transmitted on the twentieth day of the tenth month.
(These too should be the admonitions of Right Radiance to the Chief Scribe.)

The two preceding pieces bear Yang’s calligraphy.
Though carriages and horses are weighty,
they are seized by passersby.
To yield one’s portion and follow fate—
this is how summons are answered.
There is no need for reluctance.

The {wooden figurine} was indeed small,
yet still stolen by a child-scribe.
Thus I grieved and cherished it—
now the unseen mirror has seized the thief.
This serves to distinguish the fearful from the good.
Though for now {silent},
the petty-minded will know its numinous efficacy.
There is instruction within,
not mere trifling.
If even in such small matters one cannot be forthright—
Respectfully reported.
Presented to Cloud-Grove Right Radiance, the Lady.
On the nineteenth day of the eleventh month.
(This answers Right Radiance’s transmitted matter,
though the original affair no longer exists.)

I, Mu, humbly and fearfully speak:
Mired in vulgar dust,
adrift in the murk of the world,
my transgressions grow with the years,
my faults accumulate with the days.
Fortunate to encounter this mysterious turning,
the numinous awakened its convergence.
Dispersing the mists of delusion,
I suddenly attained clarity.
The true and numinous, pure and refined,
together bestowed admonition and awakening.
Overwhelmed by such literary grace,
where blossoms form forests,
golden tones and jade resonance,
rules and patterns in perfect order—
a father and son of common worth
could never bear such a burden.
Rising early, I spur myself on,
daring not grow idle or lax.
{Anxiously} {anxiously} pouring forth,
my words cannot fully express myself.
I, Mu, humbly and fearfully speak.
(This too answers Right Radiance’s poem,
though it is unclear which poem,
and it too seems no longer extant.)

The above two passages are from the Chief Scribe’s own hand.

The numinous valley’s radiant waves flourish,
concealing the self in the capital of crags.
Clad in coarse cloth, equal to dragon-robes,
girded with rope, matching jade chimes.
The form coils in distant seclusion,
the spirit soars to the courts of the great dawn.
Above the clouds stand the steps of the worthy,
in the void resounds the true voice.
Restraining my crooked dawn-flight,
I inspect this green chariot,
gazing down upon the eight degrees within,
sighing over the {winding threads} of wind and dust.
Liberation leaves waves behind—
ascending this boundless purity,
I tremble at the exhaustion of the three fordings,
racing to sever the bonds of your years.

On the first night of the twelfth month.
Composed by the Lady of Southern Marchmount for Chief Scribe Xu.

The flying wheel ascends the high dawn terrace,
reining in at the dark mound’s corner.
Hand in hand with the Purple Emperor’s sleeve,
{driven} by the eight winds.
Jade splendor wings the green curtains,
blue {kerchief} fans the kingfisher skirts.
The crown’s chariot gleams, towering,
pendants tinkle with moon-pearls.
Lightly entering the midst of wind and dust,
blocking the nose to flee the path ahead.
Foul stench corrupts my qi,
a hundred afflictions twist my heart.
Why not rise on the whirlwind,
stepping lightly through the great void?

On the first night of the twelfth month.
Composed by Lady Zhao of the Left Terrace of Fangzhang for Xu Yufu.

At dawn I bow to the crimson dawn-glow,
gathering qi to wander above the clouds.
Treading the winding waves,
I suddenly witness the sorrows of worldly men.
Words and intent rise like lush growth,
yet the three immortal herbs do not scatter.
How much better to roam the dark realm,
stroking the jade zither for your delight.
You dwell in what has bounds—
I long for what is boundless within.

The Lady of Right Radiance composed this.
Driving the light-chariot, she roams with the worthy,
urging the reins beneath the eastern garden.
The Lady of Right Radiance chants this Dao:
chewing the dark phrases,
her gentle voice swells and flows.
The melody’s turns suit its unfolding,
her words and metaphors shine clear.
Her reverent song—
there is reason for it.
The Dark Ancestor is at peace—
I shall join him.

On the fourteenth day of the twelfth month.
Composed by the Lady of Cloudy Forest for the Chief Scribe.
(This answers the Chief Scribe’s poem—
the poem itself is no longer extant.)

These five pieces bear Yang’s calligraphy—
profound and pure, the Dao is hard to fathom,
yet they penetrate its subtle mysteries.
Such is Lord Xu:
soon he shall illuminate the sacred mound,
leaping through the radiant clouds,
his body soaring through the nine heavens,
his works guiding the host of immortals,
teacher and mentor of the Golden Gates.

With the intent to *rescue* and reform the multitudes,
his virtue flows with benevolence,
his teachings are ordered yet harmonious.
One might call him a celestial blossom of refined elegance,
a master craftsman for later generations.

The Axe-Child, in hidden dawn’s radiance,
ascends through the empty heavens,
entrusting his heart to the Dark Abode,
his spirit nesting within the collar of insight.
His mind wields the blade of stillness,
his form returns to the Great Beginning.
Within and without, he severs ties of kinship,
consigning secret meetings to hidden contemplation.

Though he reflects that entering the shelter of layered peaks
would veil his brilliance in clouded obscurity,
he rebelled against his father—
if his father’s folly permitted it.

Yet when kindred spirits are bound in the same cloud-bound records,
their names inscribed on the tablets of the numinous,
their destinies converging in encounter,
how could one not declare it?

Of old, Xue Lü, styled Jihe,
went to study the true Dao at the northern slope of Mount Zhong.
After seven trials, he failed to pass.
He was the younger brother of Lord Xue of Changli.
His failure stemmed from lust *{or the loss of a woman}*, losing his station,
stinginess and vulgarity clogging his inner being,
his nature stubborn as stone, unyielding—
thus he ruined his trial.

Yet the man was kind, gentle, and sincere,
his heart fond of the phoenix-like trill of whistling,
the resonance of dark strings.
Thus, in empty song, his spirit congealed,
the pure tones stirring his soul.
His spirit did not descend—
all because of his love for whistling and his longing for the phoenix’s cry.

Lord Changli,
a man of Yan and Dai,
lived in the time of King Wu of Zhou.
The Master begged the Supreme One on his behalf,
and the Supreme One thus allowed him to live,
*[or: to continue the work of the northern slope’s destiny]*
so that he might encompass the subtle and dissolve stagnation,
*[or: now the Yu edition reads “令” (to cause), which is correct]*
refining and tempering new radiance,
hastening his ascent to the emptiness beyond.

Lord Changli’s wish was this:
if the waves of transgression do not surge,
if lust and stinginess recede,
even after a hundred trials,
would he not be like Xue Lü of old?

Masters and disciples pledge to one another,
polishing and adorning to fulfill their nature.
If one can accomplish this,
I, too, shall seldom labor.
The conduct of the worthy—
this, again, deserves careful consideration.

The secret revelation traces back to the origins of past lives.
It is hoped that this may bring awakening.
With qi of the Yan nestled within and yielding without,
deep virtue delights in luminous scenes.
Thus, when such a one hears the northern wind, the heart grows sorrowful;
when beholding the dawn’s radiance, they embrace peace.
They yearn for swift steeds to gallop in admiration,
and praise gentle compliance that transforms into flourishing.
That person’s heart—
how could it not be thus?
This is the qi of their native land,
the inner resonance of returning to the first hill.

If one can trust in this,
you shall attain harmony.
But if avarice and desire obstruct,
cinnabar and crimson fail to flow freely.
The numinous ones take hands and depart in vain,
lofty companions gather their sleeves and turn away.
The spirit and qi do not glance upon their dwelling,
the silent penetration does not stir their eyes.
Such is fate—
truly, is it not lamentable?

*(Lord Changli’s younger brother, originally from Yan and Dai,
thus speaks of the customs of his homeland
to illustrate the heart of the elder scribe.)*

On the night of the sixteenth day of the twelfth month,
Youying delivered this message.

The two preceding texts were transcribed by Yang.
The Supreme Perfection Realized One,
Cloud Forest Right Radiance Lady Wang,
Southern Peak Purple Void Primordial Sovereign,
Nine Flowers True Consort,
Pure Numinous Realized One,
Purple Yang Realized One,
Paulownia Cypress Realized One,
and Illustrious Lady Li—
these eight,
on the night of the seventeenth day of the twelfth month,
in the eastern chamber of the Fangzhu Palace,
sang the songs of the Divine Consort:

*"Purple cassia grows in the jade garden,
crimson blossoms resound with a mournful cry.
The Moon Palace births buds from the abyss,
within the Sun lies a pool of nephrite.
To the left, the full orb of numinous radiance is drawn forth;
to the right, the crimson glow of rosy clouds is grasped.
Flowing gold illumines the vermilion court,
the eight scenes transcend the return of mist.
The green canopy floats in bright clarity,
commanding the nodes to summon the Supreme Subtlety.
The phoenix essence, the youthful countenance of splendor."*

The jadelike richness fills the hunger of the flesh—
Emending to "hunger" as per the Yuanyou manuscript, which is correct.
Grasping the dawn, they bow to the Great Simplicity,
Riding flames to soar the jade steps.
Exhaling and inhaling the six numinous qi,
Jade consorts follow with towels in hand.
Strumming the *jade-excited* southern cloud fan,
Fragrant winds stir the brocade robes.
Striking the *shang* note, the hundred beasts dance,
The Six Heavens seize their divine might.
*Youhei* and *yanqian* span billions of kalpas,
The ages rise in towering majesty.
The small fry are not yet cooked in the tripod—
They say, "I grieve beneath the crags."

(According to Yang Jun’s record: Within the red qi of the east, a voice spoke: *"The small fry are not yet cooked in the tripod— / They say, 'I grieve beneath the crags.'"*
This matter should be reported to the Controller of Destinies, hence the response in this poem, including the following verses.)

**Song of the Left Lady of the Northern Ting Palace in the Dark Clarity of the Supreme Subtlety:**
Dense mists are not true emptiness,
The Great Void is my abode.
How could the Dark Lord bear longing?
*Yingsi* vines shroud the lonely, what sorrow!
The falling phoenix reins in purple mist,
The bridle raised to ascend the morning shore.
Silent, boundless, without limit,
Radiant, gazing into the void.
Hidden mushrooms bloom on Phoenix Hill,
Lingering by the jade forest’s edge.
The dragon embryo cradles your form,
Eight jades revolve in the white dawn.
Jade blossoms flourish in the jade palace,
Broidered petals gleam on the crags.
The roc’s fan spans a hundred million plumes,
Stroking the *liyu* feathers to soar the empyrean.
In the western court, they command the long song,
Strumming the *jade-excited* zither on the void.
Eight winds entwine the green eaves,
*Juyan* mists suddenly disperse.
Divine youths hurl flowing gold,
The Supreme Subtlety opens its jade portal—
Emending to "portal" as per the manuscript.
The Three Origins rise in obeisance,
The Purple Sovereign waves his sleeve in praise.
Brightly shines the fan of light,
Brilliantly gleams the Long Star.
Transcendent, the blade of clarity—
A downward glance makes my heart ache.
Pity the earthbound immortals:
Why do they dwell in forests and ravines?

On the night of the seventeenth day of the twelfth month, the Supreme Prime Perfected One and the Lord Controller of Destinies produced this poem, stating it was a song from the inner chambers of the Azure Lad’s Palace, constantly chanted to harmonize with the spirits.

(That night, the host of perfected descended in assembly, yet only this text remained. The rest were not revealed. Later, in the *dingmao* year, during the resolution of the Ting matter, it was also the seventeenth day of the twelfth month—perhaps a coincidence, for the prior event could not have occurred in a *mao* year.)

The three entries above bear Yang’s hand.
The *Xuanxuan* then rises in sequence—
Annotated thus.

Thus, the *Xuanxuan* takes the Eight Winds as its lock—[the *Zhengao*, fascicle seventeen, leaf one, renders this as "sack of stone and wood," which is correct]—the key. Heaven and Earth serve as its ramparts, the Four Seas as its urn, and the Nine Provinces as its chaff. Layered with ten thousand distinctions, steamed by yin and yang, its forging is replete with piled-up embers, swelling and surging. Hard and soft, clear and turbid, the forms and categories differ. Inhaling and exhaling, merging and parting, Gong, Bo, and Rong—annotated thus:

The Nine-Perfected Beast is a divine fowl, dwelling amid the fiercest of the fierce, cunning in the throes of the most extraordinary. A thousand years are not enough to exhaust its transformations; ten thousand distinctions are not enough to contain its essence. Sun and moon are not enough to illuminate its brow; the Eight Marshes are not enough to immerse its feet. Pure clouds are too base for it, the Nine Boundaries too shallow, the Eight Vastnesses too small, the Four Poles too near. Ever shifting, ever changing, it constantly enters even the mustard seed’s interior. It is the Jade Morning’s jade treasure, the Supreme Subtlety’s majestic spirit.

(These two entries are explanations of the hidden text in the "Divine Tiger." It is unknown which Perfected One revealed them, nor are dates provided. Both were written in the same hand.)

My lord speaks in awe and trepidation: "Virtue’s radiance flows and shines, lofty and vast, all-encompassing. With every bestowed written message, grace extends in tender bonds. Your decrees bear the harmony of eternal compliance; your ancestral summons, the assembly of the Mystic Empyrean. Though I revere and long for honor and exaltation, I rejoice in the thought of the numinous decrees."

Fearing that the near brilliance of {flame’s embers} cannot rival the distant splendor of the Twin Radiance, and that this humble lodging of {shallow wisdom} is unfit to stand among the numinous contemplation of the Seven Origins—nobility and baseness occupy separate realms, high and low distinct stations. Looking up and down, I lose myself, knowing not where to rest.

Those who kindly guide urge diligent refinement; those who cherish with loyalty fret over indolence. Thus the *Great Change* speaks of ceaseless vigilance, and Confucius sighs over the weariness of unflagging effort.

Since receiving your teachings, I have cleansed my heart and roused myself, bathing in renewal. Your exhortations illuminate the wondrous subtleties of attaining the Dao; your admonitions lay bare the fundamental traces of past lives. Excess and stinginess erode one’s foundation; vulgar stagnation severs virtue. Though the physician Lu offers his needles and moxa, and Bian Que his medicinal stones, none can compare to your guidance.

Zizhang preserved the sagely teachings on his sash; Dong of the West wore soft and taut cords to correct himself. Thus do external restraints govern the inner self, and righteousness regulate the heart. Reverently embracing your pure instructions, I inscribe them in my innermost thoughts, treasuring them within the six viscera, upholding them in all my conduct, never daring to lose or neglect them. May the Five Perils melt like ice at the furnace’s gate, and the Seven Trials calm like winds in the valley’s depths.

Soon I shall wander freely on Eastern Mountain, building my retreat in Dragon Grove. The numinous edifice will stand in quiet grandeur, the garden’s depths serene. In the courtyard, cloud-borne chariots shall gather rare companions; in the hall, feather-robed Perfected Ones shall assemble. There, golden staves and five-spirit mushrooms shall be bestowed as treasures, and the azure waves shall offer gifts of longevity.

This aspiration has been my earnest wish day and night, a vow I dare not deceive before the divine luminaries. May you but grant it your discernment.

The Master, trembling with reverence, replied:

*(This is the Prefect’s response to the Right Radiance’s poem of the twenty-eighth day of the seventh month, which exuded rare fragrance, and also repays the earlier letter discussing Xue Lü’s affairs—though this may still belong to the twelfth month.)*

This single piece was transcribed by Scribe Yi.

*True Reports, Scroll the Third*
*True Reports, Scroll the Fourth*
*Chapter Four: "The Turning of the Celestial Mechanism"*

The Dao of immortals is profoundly still; even to pursue it leaves one without encouragement—how much more so to seek it in boundless expanse? Yet should Eastern Mountain suddenly bear trays of coagulated stone marrow, purple mushrooms gleaming through the groves, luminous jewels blazing like torches, swallow-womb jade illuminating the peaks, and numinous springs flowing freely; should the host of Perfected Ones array their hymns, and every visitor pluck dark blossoms to receive jade fat, gazing upon the Heavenly Immortals to disperse worldly cares—then we shall surely join hands and ascend the Great Void, riding the auspicious clouds in their woven chariots.

Should I not inquire whether you hasten with blade or strength to keep your appointment? These past two days—have you merely wandered hills and marshes, or has official or private urgency pressed upon you, leaving no fruit of your intent? The cause of your slackening and difficulty lies, I suspect, in dimly weighing the balance between presence and absence. If absence is my expectation, then I too shall be absent. Yet within the void there are truths—have you not glimpsed them? One cannot call such faint resemblances rare. What I hope for is but that you not leave me *unclothed*—these two days may pass unfulfilled, but when might you deign to turn your carriage toward Jinling?

*On the night of the twenty-ninth day of the eleventh month.*
*The Perfected Record Keeper addresses Lord Xu.*

How could one sever the near stagnation of the present to yearn for distant achievements, hard to complete? If you still nest your heart in groves and mounds, relying on the capital’s proximity, then gazing upon Jinling may stir fleeting thoughts—but I shall leave the choice to you. Do not say I lack means to follow or mirror your absence. A mind divided cannot test the unglanced-at; a spirit wearied cannot give rise to teaching. The conduct of the worthy—can it not be examined?

The Lord of Life Preservation addresses this.

The two preceding passages from Yang’s letter are indeed most truthful. In response to the missive of the twenty-ninth day of the eleventh month: those who attain the Dao do so by their ability to cast off all encumbrances and advance directly toward it. Thus, all affairs become purified of themselves, and every duty disperses like clouds. For those already endowed with excellence, this is no labor; for those who struggle through hardship, it may serve to manifest the heart. In the first month, a guest from Mount Gui will surely come to the Eastern Mountain. At that time, could you not lend your full strength?

Having read your noble command, my joy is boundless. Since the beginning of this month, both public and private matters have pressed upon my hand, preventing me from following my heart’s desire. Once the *zanzu* arrives in the capital, I shall reckon the days for the return journey, bathe, and personally attend court to pay homage—all within this month. If the auspicious day has not yet passed, I humbly request your instruction.

Moreover, regarding the conduct of the worthy, it warrants further scrutiny. Before receiving the supreme Dao, there were those who sought to sway others’ minds and those who claimed to be capable of refinement and encouragement. After receiving the hidden scriptures, such schemes all vanish into obscurity.

*(Here two characters are damaged, and a line has been trimmed away. Later, it appears there was further text. This discussion of the worthy’s conduct seems to continue from the previous letter, responding to the missive of the twenty-ninth day of the eleventh month. That earlier letter is no longer extant, and its wording differs. It also mentioned the guest from Mount Gui arriving in the first month. This reply may thus correspond to the Perfected Record Keeper’s later address, or perhaps such words were also included in Lady Youying’s letter. The record is incomplete, and clear evidence is lacking.)*

The two preceding pieces are copies in the Long Historian’s own hand. Let the diligent be diligent in their affairs, and let them immerse themselves in the profound subtleties. The cautious, too, may draw parallels and act accordingly. The difficulty of studying the Dao cannot be put into words. Those who feel shame at vulgarity are still far from the Way. Only after thorough cultivation may one attain true worth.

The worthy’s conduct must begin anew. For now, one should inwardly forget.

The Purple Tenuity Lady spoke these words.

*(This is the Purple Tenuity’s response to the Long Historian’s reply to Lady Youying regarding the worthy’s conduct. After the Long Historian’s wife passed away, he wished to take a concubine and attend to the affairs of the Seven Primes household, both of which are strictly forbidden. Hence, the matter is repeatedly addressed.)*

The brushwork flows with such ease—like the parable of Master Lu, it bears the efficacy of Wei and Xian’s counsel. To thaw the frozen furnace door is indeed a fine intent. One must set one’s heart truly upon this deliverance.

**Record of the Register of Destinies.**

*(This is the Central Lord’s response to the Long Historian’s reply to Lady Youying, further praising his words.)*

The heart has already arrived—there is no need to journey to the mountains. Those who empty their minds to face the Real, who offer single-minded sincerity to float upon the Dao—though they may wish not to be taught, how could it be so? Gazing toward the mountains and marshes is but an afterthought. Yet those utterly devoid of longing truly leave one disheartened. Now, let it cease.

**On the first day of the twelfth month, at night, the Register of Destinies addressed Lord Xu.**

*(Upon examination, this seems to respond to the matter of his arrival in the capital and inability to come. The affairs are intertwined and difficult to untangle.)*

**On the twenty-seventh day of the first month:**
Will you not even briefly visit the site where you intend to build your dwelling? The Perfected One of Tortoise Mountain should arrive on that day. If he does not truly come to the retreat, there need be no semblance of it. Do you merely wish for him to see me?

**On the fourteenth day of the first month, the Preserver of Life declared.**

*(This declaration closely resembles the previously questioned matter, hence its convoluted obscurity. From this first month onward, all pertains to events in the bingyin year.)*

---

**The following five passages were written by Yang:**

Reining in the light, I ascend the dawn’s empyrean,
Wandering and feasting in the Azure Vastness Palace.
Colored clouds entwine the cinnabar haze,
Divine mists scatter through the eight voids.
The Perfected on high chant in the jade chamber,
Lofty immortals sing in the gemstone hall.
Nine phoenixes intone the vermilion flute,
Hollow pipes harmonize with feathered bells.
Neck to neck within the Golden Court,
We bind our bonds as friends in the unseen.
Together we sip the jade nectar’s flow—
Yet already the blackened flame clings to the child.
How can one crouch in the path’s midst?
Ills and transgressions swell with each passing day.

**On the night of the ninth day of the second month, Cloud Forest composed.**

At dawn I roam the Palace of Great Simplicity,
Governing the gaze upon the Jade River.
At dusk I feast in the Resplendent Lofty Abode,
At morn I pluck the round radiance’s bloom.
I pluck the jade zither at the Northern Cold Terrace,
Seven spirits gleam in the purple haze.
Solemnly the lofty immortals rise,
Scattered like dust amid the worldly snare.
Lingering within the clamor and mist,
Transgressions and burdens ought not be many.

**On the sixteenth day of the second month, Lady Youying composed.**

The Dark Clarity’s distant gaze,
The setting light emerges from the eastern stillness.
Would that I might find a friend beyond the dust,
Living in rare seclusion, far from the world’s din.
I chant this again and again.

---

**The following three passages were written by Yang:**

The numinous ones conceal themselves on the Mystic Peak,
True spirits veil their cloud-borne radiance.
The dark chant is not without its time,
The wondrous response awaits its moment.
Who would say the void is silent?
The supreme resonance endures forever.
Hand in hand we ascend the Feathered Palace,
Feasting together in the Vast Cold’s halls.
I ask: who are these companions?
Only the jade youths remain.
The soaring clouds, the void’s steed—
They rise with pinions aloft in the empty sky.
Such men—how could they not long bow to the south,
Forever renouncing the thousand chariots?

**Purple Tenuity’s poem.**

Upon chanting this:
I harness the wind, I gallop the clouds,
At dawn I ascend the Great Stillness’s mound.
The crimson ford shakes the linked peaks,
Clear waves surge through the deep currents.
I pace the void, observing the nine wefts.

The Eight *Gang* [Principles]—*Yunji Qiqian*, Scroll 98, records that Cloud-Forest Right Radiance Lady {orally transmitted} to Yang the Perfected One, who composed this poem for Director Xu. All have already roamed:
For a brief respite, they feast amid the Three Gold Splendors,
Coming to observe the companions of steadfast resolve.
Diligent or idle, they do not linger.
Thus, a hundred sorrows accumulate.

On the night of the thirtieth day of the second month, Right Radiance composed:
Cold robes ford the Green River,
And so they meet Lord Fusang.
A grand assembly at the Great Forest’s ruins,
Resting and feasting in the Dark Flower Palace.
If one’s faith in the Dao is truly pure and sincere,
Why not dwell upon the Eastern Peak?

Purple Tenuity Lady chants this:
Crossing waves, traversing the azure vast,
Suddenly they arrive at Golden Mountain.
Gazing all around, they wander the whole day—
Rare are we, the cloud-borne ones.

Right Radiance intones this:
Guiding the light, they reach the Dawn Ford,
Riding the whirlwind to ascend the Supreme Clarity.
Cloud Terraces rise in towering majesty,
{Gates flourish} enclosing the jade-walled city.
Morning winds stir the cinnabar mists,
Crimson vapors scatter across the golden courts.
Green blossoms gleam on the dark peaks,
Purple haze arises beneath the cliffs.
Auspicious clouds coil around the cinnabar furnace,
Refined jade scatters as eightfold jasper.
Reclining, they gaze upon the Vast Cold Palace,
Where ten thousand *chun* trees restore youth.
Dragon {banners} unfurl with numinous lightning,
Tiger standards summon the crimson hosts.
Lofty perfected ones circle the Nine Luminaries,
Their penetrating vision equal to the hidden and manifest.
Who can tread the secluded path,
And seek my boundless years?

Purple Tenuity Lady composes:
Purple towers are built atop the void,
Dark halls surge with the rushing gale.
Jade and pearl adorn the numinous gardens,
Blossoms bloom, entwining with jasper.
They gallop the ford of the azure vast,
Eight winds stir the cloud-borne melodies.
Parting the feathered fans of the northern shade,
Grasping the staff, they sound the golden flutes.
Phoenix pipes harmonize with a thousand bells,
Western youths sing at dawn’s audience.
The heart opens beyond the void’s outer bounds,
The spirit’s lapel—how vast and bright!
Turning {to dance} upon the Great Void’s ridge,
The Six Qi govern the profound and obscure.
How could my path be found?

Right Elegance Lady composes:
Mists veil the Purple Tenuity’s halls,
Lofty terraces disperse the radiant gale.
Luan birds sing amid the flowered canopy,
Phoenix hooks guide the dragon’s {chariot-summons}.
Eight wolves bear crimson banners,
White tigers blow horned flutes.
Clouds surge, depicting the numinous palace,
Coming to this dust-choked clamor.
Loosening the reins where the fair one slumbers,
Together they summon one another.
Seeking the lineage takes but a moment,
Ten thousand years—yet a single dawn.
The cedar’s span meets its decline,
How could kalpas past be deemed distant?
The true gaze upon one another,
Lest the heart’s course {wither}.
The empty blade swings to the void’s end,
Coarse stagnation saddens the Five Spirits.

Right Purple Tenuity composes:
At dawn, the eastern morning’s radiance unfolds,
Soaring across the azure abyss.
Mountain waves shake the green shores,
Eight winds fan the dark mist.
Glancing back, the shifting chambers change,
Longing stirs the true and moves the heart.
Three gold coins may wander the plate,
The eastern peak suits eternal refinement.
Amid the tumult of the crossroads,
Who can tread the living ford?
{Whirling winds} sweep the Eight Rosy Peaks,
Lingering beneath the flying morning canopy.
Purple soars through the Great Void,
Glorious gaze beyond the Nine Heavens’ bounds.
Jade flutes stir the luminous clouds,
Spirit-mist severs the deep haze.
Lofty immortals feast with the Grand Realized,
Pure songs stretch without limit.
Coming and going through mountain and peak’s courts,
Why should there be delay in waiting?

On the fourteenth day of the fourth month,
Purple Tenuity Lady composes:
Dark waves shake the azure billows,
Vast fords drum ten thousand currents.
Driving the luminous gaze through the Six Voids,
Thoughts turn to roaming with the fair one.
Exquisite songs find no response from me,
To whom may the pure tones be cast?
Amid clouds, jade wheels gallop—
Why hasten through the dust’s throng?

Right Elegance Lady chants this song at the same evening:
Pines and cypresses grow on the dark peak,
Thriving as the cold forest’s towering trees.
{Luxuriant} blossoms flourish amid stern ice,
Unwilling to fear the white snow.
In troubled times, the deep and layered ravines.

Wandering life keeps the Dao ever pure,
This soaring carriage leaves swift tracks behind.
Tracing the distant one’s wheel-ruts,
Even lords and marquises may come and go—
Why then cannot the bonds be severed?

Right Elegance Lady composes.

Divine jade gleams at the numinous ford,
The Seven Origins illumine the spirit’s gate.
The numen shifts within the square inch of the heart,
A single leap ascends to the Grand Tenuity.
Exquisite tones ride harmonious song,
The lofty assembly too has its mechanism.
Gaze in unison with heaven and humankind,
In concert with the morning’s radiant flight.
Reining beyond the Six Directions,
How could there be peril or collapse?

On the night of the twenty-third day of the fourth month,
Purple Tenuity Lady composes:
Dark resonance lies beyond wondrous images,
Harmonious voices summon one another.
Numinous clouds thicken the purple dawn,
Orchid winds stir the green chariot’s call.
The Highest Perfected feast in the jasper terrace,
Their bearing marks them as earthbound immortals.
What they await is noble and far-reaching,
Thus they flourish with surpassing distinction.
Delighting in those Eight Pristine Brushes,
The Dao’s completion was never distant.
How can worldly affairs be foreseen?
They would but dissolve your form and qi.

On the night of the twenty-seventh day of the fourth month,
Southern Marchmount Lady composes.

Twelve pieces bear Yang’s calligraphy,
with additional transcriptions by various scribes.

Pure and still, I vow for Eastern Mountain,
Shaded by radiance, I dwell in the numinous grotto.
The heart’s echoes resound in the tranquil courtyard,
Canopies of verdant forests grow dense.
Circular brilliance illumines the southern casement,
Crimson phoenixes fan the secluded chamber.
Sleeves clasped within the quiet room,
We pledge to initiate wondrous arts.
Vast and bright, distant thoughts turn to the mysterious,
Desolate and serene, the spirit’s heart roams free.

On the night of the third day of the intercalary month,
Right Elegance Lady composes,
addressed to Director Xu.
(Note: In the Jin calendar, the intercalary month of the bingyin year was the fourth month.)

These bear Yang’s calligraphy,
with additional transcriptions by scribes.

Releasing the heart to the empty confluence of waters,
Reining the crimson steeds—
Why does the fair one come so late?
When will the Dao and virtue be achieved?

(Chanting this Dao verse:)
If you truly intend to follow the Master’s axe,
Then you should gather the five zhi herbs.
Even if the zhi herbs cannot be found,
You still cannot come.
If you come, then you may obtain them—
The zhi herbs shall be yours to eat.

(These lines of “obtain” and “come” are playful, rendered in Wu dialect.)

Right Elegance Lady chants this.

Two pieces bear Yang’s calligraphy.

The Eight Paths converge without a single origin,
Riding fate, I observe the clamor of the world.
Transformed amid the floating dust,
Loosening my robe, I join the Daoist family.
Swift as mist, yet uncollapsed,
I carry the true to the numinous heights.
Empty radiance coils through the jasper pavilion,
The dark harmony composes the phoenix’s song.
The road is smooth, without hindrance,
Numinous tones dance upon cloud-waves.
Virtues aligned, they flourish in Jade Capital—
What need is there for the world’s excess?

The transmission of the text complete,
She chants again.
After a long while, she once more bestows this poem,
Seeming unconnected to what was written above.

Serene, I observe the celestial truth,
Shedding burdens, I release all passions.
The body stills, the mechanism of the four steeds abandoned,
Exalting being, I thus preserve life.
Where might I find the Master of Equanimity,
To entrust fate and follow wherever it leads?

Composed by the Lady of the Central Watchtower.

A fleeting feast beneath the dust-laden winds,
Vicissitudes trace their return.
How could one know the span of the kalpa’s turning?
A glance back stirs sorrow in the heart.

Composed by the Lady of the Purple Tenuity.

These three pieces bear Yuan’s calligraphy.

The forest stirs with kindred resonance,
Clouds gather, awaiting the dragon’s song.
Mysterious numbers seek one another,
Every touch of rhythm bears its own sound.
Flying forth from Western Florescence,
Reins gathered, they suddenly come in search.
Though the Eight Distances hold no lack of joy,
In shared chanting, the principle itself commands reverence.
Mourning those within the Four Nets,
A hundred sorrows ever dwell in the heart.
Together we roam the Northern Frigid Terrace,
A divine wind unfastens your robe.

Composed by the Lady of the Southern Culmen on the night of the twenty-third day of the sixth month.

Ascending to Eastern Florescence,
Fanning the dance of the Great Mystery,
Flying reins soar ninety thousand,
The Eight Falls now made equal.
A moment’s gaze upon the rivers and mountains,
In the depths of the numinous peaks.
Of one wind, our qi naturally aligns,
In Dao’s harmony, the principle draws near.
Dragon zhi herbs grant boundless longevity,
Inward vision gathers the celestial truth.

At Eastern *Cen* (corrected to 岑, meaning "peak"), one may forever purify—
Why then be entangled by things?

Composed by the Lady of the Central Watch on the night of the twenty-third day of the sixth month.

*(The two preceding poems bear Yang’s calligraphy, later transcribed by Yuan. On the twelfth day of the fifth month, Zhongjun Yu inscribed these words. [This nine-character note appears outside the scroll. All that follows seems to have been conferred in the *dingmao* year, concerning the division of the Three Xu.] )*

Ah Ying thus resolved to renounce the world, dwelling in mountains and forests,
Diligently cultivating the savor of the Dao,
Purifying his spirit and focusing his essence,
Polishing the mirror of emptiness to clarity.
In solitary serenity, he rejoiced in the profound,
Alone yet abiding in union with the true.
He was a peer of Naiweng, master of distant Dao,
And a companion to Jiang Bozhen.
Consuming the *ye* elixir,
He ultimately reaped its benefits—
A matter of utmost consequence.

Formerly, he also entered the Red Mountain of Linhai,
Red Mountain also called Burning Mountain,
Where he encountered worthy companions:
Wang Shilong,
Zhao Daoxuan,
And Fu Taichu.

These several individuals had initially crossed the river in the first year of *Jianxing* of the Jin, entering the Eastern Mountains to study the Dao. They all met one another there. The practices of these several men all surpassed Ying’s. Ying thus became a disciple of Shilong, receiving the Dao of untying the bonds and cultivating the methods of reverse practice. He ingested the Jade Fluid, refined the essence of the brain, and within two or three years, his face radiated luminous splendor, his complexion reverted to youth, and he attained the utmost in Daoist accomplishment. Yet he regretted that his endowment was not abundant, preventing him from achieving the highest rank of transcendence.

Thereupon, the Director of Destinies commanded me to recommend him, submitting a memorial to the Upper Palace. His name was transferred to the Registers of the Eastern Direction, and he was appointed an Earthbound Transcendent. At that time, the Left Minister of the Three Offices’ General Prohibition dispatched the Keeper of the Handle, Hou Zhou Fang, and the Envoy of the Unorthodox, Yan Baihu, to the Red Mountain, intending to seize him and take him away, interrogating him regarding his transgressions. I was then struck dumb (the character likely should be *ya*, "astonished"). I swiftly sent an urgent report to the Director of Destinies, who immediately dispatched the Central Attendant Li Zun, wielding a fire-bell, to come and rebuke them. Thereupon, Fang and Baihu fled.

Before Li Zun’s arrival, Ying was terrified, his courage failing, and his *qi* dissipated.

Also relying on the youthful integrity of Li Kailin, styled Longgong, who assisted Ying in his responses—had it not been for these two and their master Wang Shilong, matters would have long since turned dire. Though Fang’s interrogation was grounded in truth, Ying’s replies were barely adequate.

The Three Offices produced vermilion tablets inscribed with the register of transgressions, each holding one copy as they questioned Ying, saying: "One who aspires to the Dao and yearns for life, who submits to the Perfected Ones above and nests their profound heart in reverent sincerity, who venerates the lofty numina—such a one ought to have worldly merits to their credit, misfortunes and evils unmet, hidden virtue spreading its roots, and a benevolent heart reaching upward. Only then may they tread the path to transcendence and have their name inscribed in the Azure Bureau. How then did your father’s hand slay Xie Gong? Moreover, you threw the Three Luminaries into chaos. You further promised to behead Li Yiji in the morning to substitute for Cai Fu’s rank. You fled to slay and shoot Pan Qisi and others, dismembered your retainer Cao Biao, drowned Tang Yun’s corpse in water, burned Xu Ang’s bones in fire, strangled Huan Zheng, carved up Zhen Hui, and committed cruel, violent, and wanton atrocities against forty-three souls. Their clamorous grievances now lie before the Celestial Thearch."

Piled high as mountains are your calamitous transgressions,
not a single meritorious deed to your name.
Moreover, you originally belonged to the Way of the Bo Clan,
yet feasted on the blood of living folk—
long-standing offenses and karmic debts
were already listed in the registers of the Three Bureaus.
Yet you presumptuously slipped through the net,
serving as a bondsman to the true qi.
Father and son, a single household,
each pledged to different masters,
living in discord,
never sharing the same libation wine.
Such grievous guilt
is now under dark scrutiny.
With sins so amassed,
how could you ever attain transcendence?
How dare you deceive the courts of the Most High,
hoping to have your name inscribed in the Purple Register of Immortality?
You have no defense.
The authorities will surely seize you.

Thereupon, he drew himself up, let out a long howl,
shook his coarse robe, and ran his fingers through his hair.
Then, composing his breath and sealing his lips,
he roared in reply:
“The Great Dao shows no partiality,
but befriends only the good.
Heaven and Earth have no intent,
yet mercy follows virtue.
Thus at Banquan, blood flowed in rivers,
yet the Dragon-Beard’s uprising met no resistance.
The Three Miao dyed the wilds crimson,
and the deer fled through the scarlet grass—
did this hinder the lofty communion of the Great Sage’s numinous transformations?
My seven-times-great father was Xu Zia."

"Accumulating benevolence and manifesting virtue,
he harmonized yin with birds and beasts.
When years of famine came,
the people starved,
and pestilence struck,
leaving but one in a hundred alive,
he then distributed his family’s wealth
to rescue the multitudes.
He personally prepared remedies,
laboring tirelessly in the outer lodgings.
At another’s funeral,
he grieved as if he had lost his own kin;
in relieving another’s suffering,
he agonized as if it were his own affliction.
Lives already lost
hung by a thread in his hands;
the destitute and dying
he cradled as his own children.
Those who survived the calamity,
relying on him to endure—
four hundred and eight souls.
His benevolence and virtue never faltered,
and later, they would be bestowed upon us.
Thus his merit was inscribed before the Celestial Emperor,
his virtue etched in the Numinous Pavilion,
causing our ancestral roots to flow with generational blessings,
our lineage to radiate with luminous posterity.
Hence the branches droop with blossoms,
and from birth, we have loved the immortal arts.
Five of us were destined for transcendence,
three have already ascended.
Our names are recorded in the Most High’s register,
our deeds chronicled in the Azure Palace’s annals—
how could the likes of you presume to share in this?" He finished speaking.

The *fang* and his companions burst into laughter, and Zun departed. Though this intention was indeed aided by Shi Long of the world, I also admired his bold words.

Thereupon, they were granted transcendence and recorded in the Eastern Palace, destined to become middling immortals. Yet within their bodies lingered unresolved karmic debts from past lives, which they would gradually atone for and resolve before the Most High. They were to receive scriptures and official appointments—no longer subject to the trials of the Three Bureaus, their names already fixed in the register of the deathless.

Now they have been relocated to Zhuye Mountain, also called Gaizhu Mountain. On its eastern face, two ridges rise to the west. Between them lies a stone bridge over a well.
