yet few attain ascension.

The scriptures are not without wonder,
nor do the numinous lack response.
But the foolish follow one another blindly,
unaware of the root of cultivating the true,
or the methods of nurturing the spirit, fostering nature, and securing stability.

From youth onward,
many incur harm within their forms.
The First Emperor of the body is not governed,
and the hundred spirits scatter in alarm.
Ten thousand trials arise—
this is what is meant by the overgrown city,
where thorns flourish within.

Without wondrous arts to guide oneself,
or the cultivation of the Dao to seek immortality,
one may covet glory and yearn for nobility,
only to fail when on the verge of success.
All this stems from losing the true and violating qi,
blind and benighted,
unable to recognize this mechanism.

Thus years are stolen, lives extinguished,
and ten thousand affairs come to naught.
Such is the path to seeking life.

The distance from life grows ever greater—
all is but vain self-affliction.
The Supreme possesses the Dao of the Mysterious Mechanism,
the essentials of the *Seven Spirits in the Pillow* gleaming forth.
This Dao is subtle, wondrous indeed!
At first, it was not transmitted to the dull and vulgar below.
Those who possess this Dao:
the First Emperor governs within the Mysterious Palace,
the ten thousand spirits stand guard,
and the heart aligns with Heaven.
Following the formulas with care and cultivating it,
one may ascend mountains and cross seas—
ten thousand trials cannot touch them.
Cultivating immortality and ascending in transcendence,
all desires follow the heart.
Is this mere empty speech?

Your father and son have inherited the Mysterious Mechanism through the generations,
mastering its principles to connect with the true.
Thus, your divine talents in spirit-cultivation
are praised by the host of perfected beings—
not by my acclaim alone.
Therefore, I shall inscribe you together in the *Records of Immortals*,
free from any suspicion beyond reason.
I have already consulted you on this,
so you may know my heart.
Receive and employ the *Golden Dragon and Jade Fish*—
this cannot be omitted.
The reason for this is that when you appear before the Supreme,
your numinous radiance must be somewhat prepared.

The *Divine Tiger Talisman* recently transcribed
seems to me insufficiently refined—
it would be best to rewrite it well.
Regarding the matter of *Xiang* and *Wang* you mentioned earlier,
when I recently met with *Xiyi*,
I also sensed good intentions,
though what was achieved was modest.
Still, you may naturally preserve your heavenly years.

I have seen the *Biographies* you composed—
no easy labor—
yet you were able to narrate the sacred traces,
unraveling and crafting marvels.
This is Heaven stirring your heart.
Yesterday, I also met with the Lord of Life and Destiny,
who greatly approved.
In the unseen realm, it shall surely be repaid to those with karmic affinity.
If your descendants know how to *burn incense and summon the Sacred Peaks*,
praying to the Heavenly Perfected,
their responses will surely descend.
Is this empty speech?

The Xie family, through the Tang and Chen dynasties,
has flourished like a luxuriant forest—
most gratifying indeed!
As for Anshi’s earlier audience,
what was bestowed is as we recently discussed in person.
There is no need to elaborate further.

The Perfected Lord Wang of Western City’s reply to Marquis Xu.
The above four sections are a separate handwritten letter,
later obtained by Lu Xiujing in Dongyang.
They are not of the same origin as the other traces,
and their diction and matters appear crude and spurious.

These do not align with the true purport—
likely composed by later hands.
Yue Zichang was not one who received the Five Talismans.
The "Tang and Chen" refers to the forty-sixth *dinghai* cycle recorded in the *Annals*.

*True Reports*, Scroll Eight.
*True Reports*, Scroll Nine.
"Harmonizing with the Prosperous Cycle," Section One.

The scripture states:
When performing the rites,
face north while holding the *Hidden Writ*—
this is for those who have just begun to study the wondrous Dao,
who have not yet ventured into subtleties afar,
who do not comprehend the cardinal directions of stellar positions,
nor recognize the pointing of the Mystic Dipper.
Thus, they must face north while holding the text to gradually seek understanding.
Once the meaning of the text is grasped,
and the turning of the stars with the seasons is known,
one should naturally follow the Dipper’s pointing,
proceeding and pacing accordingly.
In this way, there is no fixed direction—
not always facing north.
Facing north in all cases
is only for beginners.
Perhaps this can be understood by analogy—
other such matters need not be asked again.

(This answers the inquiry of the Chief Clerk regarding the meaning of facing north while holding the text in the *Scripture on Soaring Steps*.)

The Most High Perfected’s method of pacing the Way of the Five Stars
brings the Five Stars to descend into the chamber.
Holding the breath to ascend the net,
one must first invoke the names of the Five Star Ladies.
Only then may one cross the net and tread upon the stars.
This means that upon first ascending the net,
one pauses to invoke the names.
After invoking the names,
one then crosses the net and treads upon the stars.
If, upon reaching each star,
one can once more silently invoke the name of the star’s position,
it is all the better.
If this becomes cumbersome and difficult to maintain consistently...

Simply follow the established method as before. In ancient times, Master Yushagong, Beili Zichang, and the Old Man of Changling all ascended to heaven by adhering to this practice, never shirking its demands on account of difficulty. This is what is meant by "managing one’s livelihood." Merchants and traders toil ceaselessly—do they shrink from peril or hardship? Their sole aim is profit. If seekers of the Dao were to apply themselves with the same devotion as merchants, what could prevent them from attaining immortality?

Yet it is lamentable that beginners often claim to be wholly devoted at first, only to grow lax over time. Even if they persist, it is as though a cart’s axle is about to break, its every joint loosening and falling apart; or like an ox burdened with a heavy load, struggling to take each step on a long journey. Such are the pitfalls that plague learners, and the very things that those who have attained the Dao mock. If one can instead refine the inner mirror of the heart, this will stir the numinous. Then, divine beings will dispel your ignorance and bear you away in the chariot of celestial radiance.

*(This answers the inquiry regarding the method of pacing the Five Stars. The scriptural illustrations only mention moving along the net to and fro, while another method speaks of crossing the net to tread upon the stars—this passage now clarifies the matter. Its words of encouragement and admonition are truly incisive.)*

The Five Stars diagram is always oriented toward the south, with Venus positioned in the west and Jupiter in the east. This arrangement is followed in practice, and the reason is thus.

The Five Stars conceal and emerge, shifting without constancy, unlike the Northern Dipper, whose stellar forms remain ever fixed. Thus, one must establish positions according to the five directions, rather than following the stars’ transient locations. *(This answers the inquiry regarding the proper placement of the Five Stars diagram. The scriptures contain no definitive instructions, hence the need for this clarification.)*

The Three Eights’ Radiance and the Twenty-Four Spirits may be visualized in sequence, or all three Eights may be summoned at once. Alternatively, one may contemplate the Upper Radiance at dawn, the Middle Radiance at noon, and the Lower Radiance at midnight—this is left to the practitioner’s discretion. If one retreats to secluded cliffs, severs worldly affairs, inwardly focuses on the spirit-gates, and draws in the true qi, then at dawn all three Eights’ Radiance may be summoned at once, while at the other two times, each Radiance may be contemplated again in turn—this would be most excellent. Yet in the human realm, affairs are manifold, and such diligence is difficult to sustain. If the practice cannot be maintained, its benefits will naturally diminish.

The Western City’s Perfected Lord Wang and the Supreme Realized of Mount Tongbai both followed this Way. As recorded in the *Pao Xuan Yu* {*Bamboo Records*} and the *White Tablets and Azure Scriptures*: "One who does not visualize the Twenty-Four Spirits nor knows the names of the Three Eights’ Radiance..."

One who fails to visualize the Twenty-Four Spirits and does not know the names of the Three Eights’ Radiance shall not become a citizen of Great Peace, nor shall they serve as a minister to future sages. (This answers the intent of cultivation and visualization in the *Scripture of the Twenty-Four Spirits*, and is also a secret formula. The four formulas above are now found in a copy transcribed by the Chief Clerk. It is unknown which Perfected One Yang consulted for this—if not the Eastern Minister, then it must have been the Southern Perfected of Purple Tenuity.)

These are the essential secret practices compiled by the Most High Perfected. (The transcribed copy by the Chief Clerk bears this title. These are still the key methods taught by the assembled Perfected in their transmitted scriptures, matters of rejuvenation and reversing aging. The Chief Clerk was merely instructed to put them into practice—this is not a single completed scripture.)

The *Scripture of Great Simplicity and Cinnabar Radiance* states: On the face, one should always rub both hands until warm, then massage the face thoroughly, following its contours in all directions. This will make the face luminous, preventing wrinkles and blemishes. After five years of practice, the complexion will resemble that of a young maiden. This is called "the qi of mountains and rivers flowing freely, ever full and never depleted." First, rub the palms together until hot, then wipe both eyes. Next, stroke the hair in a combing motion. The arms should also be massaged alternately with the hands to prevent hair from whitening and veins from rising to the surface. This passage is from the middle scroll of the *Scripture of Cinnabar Radiance*. (This scripture has not yet been revealed to the world; it belongs to the lower rank of Perfected texts.)

The *Essential Radiance and Massage Section* of the *Scripture of the Great Cavern* states: Upon rising or retiring, sit upright. First, clasp the hands and place them behind the neck. Then tilt the head back to look upward, lifting the neck so that it strains against the hands. Repeat this three or four times to harmonize the essence, circulate the blood, and prevent wind-qi from entering. With long practice, one will neither die nor fall ill. Next, bend and stretch the body, extending the limbs to their utmost. Arch backward, twist to the sides, and shake all joints—each movement performed three times. These are oral instructions. (This exercise follows a sequential method, hence the need for oral transmission to refine it. It is also the art of "bear-hanging and bird-stretching.")

Upon rising, first use a handkerchief or thick cloth to wipe the neck on all sides and behind the ears.

Let the warmth encircle fully until it radiates gently. Stroke the neck along the flow of the hair, as if combing it countless times. After a long while, rub both hands together and then treat the face and eyes. With long practice, this will brighten the eyes, prevent pathogenic qi from invading, and keep the body free from greasy filth and grime.

When all is complete, swallow saliva twenty times to guide the inner fluids.

*(The above passage is from the first scroll of the* **Great Cavern Scripture of Essence and Radiance***, which has not yet been revealed to the world and is not among the Three Grades.)*

The *Scripture of the Supreme Numinous for Dispelling Demons* states: If the body feels unwell, press the tongue against the throat, rinse the mouth, and swallow saliva without count. In a short while, the discomfort will vanish, and one will feel the body relaxed and supple.

*(The above passage is from the* **Preface to the Scripture of the Supreme Numinous for Dispelling Demons***, which has not yet been revealed to the world and is not among the Three Grades. It likely pertains to the* **Seven Scrolls of Wisdom***.)*

The authorship of the preceding three passages remains unclear.

The *Scripture of the Supreme Numinous for Dispelling Demons*, Scroll One, further states: Frequently press and massage the ears on both sides, also without count, to sharpen hearing. This is called "tending the city walls," and its name is recorded in the imperial register.

It also says: Press the sides of the nose repeatedly to balance the breath.

The so-called "irrigating the Central Marchmount" is recorded in the imperial bamboo register. These two methods were transmitted and practiced by Lady Li of the Illustrious Terrace of the Square Zhang, Zhaoling.

*(This is also referred to in the* **Scripture of the Supreme Numinous for Dispelling Demons, Scroll One**, *and should likewise belong to the preceding category.)*

The *Scripture of the Divine Flow and Flourishing Hair from the Supreme Bamboo Register* prescribes the method of anointing: At the time when living qi arises, swallow saliva twice seven times. Upon completion, press the painful area of the body and pray facing the king, saying:

*"Left Mystery, Right Mystery,
The Three Spirits unite in perfection.
Left Yellow, Right Yellow,
The Six Flowers align in harmony.
Wind qi and malignant epidemics
Hide in the four directions.
Jade liquid flows with grace,
Above and below, all is unobstructed.
Within, water and fire are dispatched;
Without, inauspiciousness is repelled.
To attain long life and ascend as an immortal,
The body remains ever strong."*

Afterward, swallow saliva again twice seven times. By practicing this regularly, one will be free from illness. One should also press the painful area twenty-one times in haste.

This method was transmitted by Lady Wang of Right Radiance of the Cloudy Forest Palace of Canglang.

*(The* **Scripture of the Divine Flow** *from the bamboo register has also not been revealed to the world and is not among the Three Grades.)*

The *Scripture of the Three and Five in Sequential Flow, Written in Vermilion* states: When seated, one should often close the eyes and inwardly visualize, contemplating the five viscera and the intestines and stomach. With prolonged practice, one will naturally perceive them with clarity and precision.

*(These scriptures are among the true catalog of this canon.)* The *Scripture of Vermilion Characters on Stone and Light* states: One should often cover the mouth and nose with the hands, gently closing the eyes. After a long while, saliva will form in the palms. Then, use it to rub the face and eyes. Practicing this regularly will make the body fragrant.

*(This scripture is not among the Three Grades.)* The *Purple Radiance Inner Vision Central Method* says: One should often lie down with eyes closed, settling the body and softly regulating the breath, appearing as if asleep so that others nearby do not notice. Then, inwardly visualize and listen attentively to the four directions, directing one’s ears and eyes to focus beyond ten thousand *li*. With prolonged practice, one will naturally perceive events beyond ten thousand *li*. If one cultivates this with concentrated intention, one may even see beyond a million *li*. Moreover, the ears will constantly hear the sounds of gold and jade, as well as the music of silk and bamboo. This is a wondrous method. The "four directions" is a general term—one should begin by focusing on a single direction, inwardly directing vision and hearing. At first, there may be no sign of success, but with persistent sincerity, one will naturally enter the subtle realm.

*(This scripture is among the lower true catalog.)* The *Three Celestial Pass Scriptures of the Most High* state:

Keep the eyes gently pressed near the inner corners with the hands, closing them as one does so. When the passage feels unobstructed, pause. Exhale, then begin anew. With constant practice, the eyes will attain penetrating vision.

*(This scripture is among the lower true catalog. The "Three Celestial Passes" 〈Illustrations〉—the character "Illustrations" is suspected to be missing.)* The four precepts above are those commanded by the Mysterious Master.

*(The Mysterious Master is the Southern Perfected Lady. These four scriptures have not yet been revealed to the world.)* The *Scripture of Treasured Spirits Spoken by the Pure Numinous Perfected*.

*(The copy transcribed by the Prefectural Secretary bears this title. This refers only to the heading of the preceding matter. What follows consists of miscellaneous sayings by various perfected beings, with discrepancies in the order of titles—following the example of the* Zhen'gao*. Modern scholars all refer to it separately as the* Scripture of Treasured Spirits*. How could the* Scripture of Treasured Spirits *be a lesser teaching? This is merely a fragmentary transcription.)*

Now, to focus the mind on the Dao and the true, to inwardly visualize the numinous person—even in profound obscurity, one’s intent is fully observed. If external obstacles remain unremoved, and one merely recites while retaining distractions, one will truly be unable to reverse the years of the western elm or restore the youth of the Mysterious Lad. Yet if one delights deeply in the mysterious and is steadfast in purpose, then even if teeth are carved and the face wrinkled, or white blossoms sprout upon the crown, the Dao can transform one into an infant in but a moment. It depends solely on the strength of one’s resolve. Age is no barrier to learning. I once was such a person.

*(These matters are all being explained to instruct the Prefectural Secretary.)*

To seek the Dao, one must first clarify the eyes and sharpen the ears—these are the masters of all affairs. Moreover, the ears and eyes serve as the ladder for pursuing the true and the gateway for gathering the numinous. Success or failure hinges upon them, and survival or perishing depends on their {discernment}. Now, this direct method is shown here for practical use. (This refers to the essential techniques within the *Baoshen Jing*, hence called the "direct method.")

The Dao teaches: Regularly press with the hands the small cavities behind both eyebrows thirty-nine times. Then, with the palms and fingers, rub the upper parts of both eyes. Rotate the ears with the hands thirty times. The key lies in the number of repetitions, not the timing. Upon completion, reverse-stroke the forehead thirty-nine times, beginning from the space between the eyebrows and moving upward into the hairline, passing by the corners of the mouth. Swallow saliva as much as one wishes, without limit.

By practicing this consistently, the eyes will naturally become clear and bright. Within a year, one may read at night. This may also be done discreetly in the presence of others, without revealing its form. The small cavities behind the eyebrows are the palace of the Upper Prime Sixfold Union, governing the generation of eye radiance and the harmonious refinement of essence and light.

The Long Pearl penetrates the youthful, preserving and refining the eye spirits. This is the supreme Dao of the True Person’s sitting and rising, also named the *True Person’s Perpetual Internal Classic*. A true saying states: "If you wish to read at night, you must cultivate the Perpetual Abode."

The reason the True Person can observe all four directions and make the Eight Radiant Clouds shine brightly is truly due to the clarity of the Perpetual Abode’s methods. The region beneath the eyes and above the cheekbones is the Chamber of Preserving Clarity, the归婴至道 (the Perfect Dao of Returning to Infancy). Rotating the ears with the hands is the technique for gathering luminous reflection. Rotation thereby unblocks the principles, disperses the blood, and prevents the onset of wrinkles. The eyes’ brilliance shines darkly, and the harmonious spirit is full.

When a person is about to age, it rarely does not begin with the ears and eyes. Moreover, the signs of an aging form also first appear at the sides of the eyes. Stroking upward on the forehead while inwardly visualizing the Red Child and the twin luminaries of sun and moon, with the Upper Prime rejoicing—beginning from the space between the eyebrows for thirty-nine repetitions, ceasing only upon completion—this is called the Dao of the hands paying homage to the Three Primes, fortifying the brain and strengthening the hair.

Cover the four sides of the head with both hands, smoothing the hair into place, and do this as much as possible. Thereby, the blood in the head flows and disperses, and wind-dampness does not congeal. When all is complete...

Gently press the four corners of the eyes with the hands thirty-eight times, until one perceives light with clarity—this is the Dao of refining the spirit of the eyes. With long practice, one may behold the hundred spirits.

(All practices of this Dao and the various miscellaneous methods in this scroll follow strict regulations, which are fully expounded in the *Dengzhen Yinjue*. They cannot be exhaustively annotated here.)

Diligently cultivate this, ensuring the hands never leave the face, and one may attain the rank of Perfected Person without fail. Those who wish to practice this Dao must first swear an oath upon gold. The quantity of gold is determined by the sincerity of the practitioner—it is not merely a formality to be performed carelessly.

The Perfected Officials say: "To inquire about daily conduct, one must pledge with a golden covenant." This means it is not to be transmitted to the unworthy. This Dao originates from the *Taishang Baoshen Jing*, a scripture that was not initially disseminated in the world. Those destined to become Perfected Persons in the future may occasionally obtain it. The essentials of refining and returning to purity are all contained herein.

(Once the oath is firmly established, there are no further requirements, though it is fitting to present two pairs of golden rings when receiving this teaching.)

The Lady of the Purple Tenuity issues this instruction as follows.

*(The Lady of the Purple Tenuity, having heard Master Pei’s discourse on the* Baoshen Jing*, continues to expound upon the matters of the Treasure Spirit in this manner—thus, what Master Pei has spoken aligns with this very evening’s teaching.)*

Upon awakening from sleep at night, one should first knock the teeth together nine times, then swallow saliva nine times. Once done, press the hands along the sides of the nose, moving up and down dozens of times. Softly recite the incantation:

*"The Supreme Four Luminaries,
The Nine Gates emit essence.
Ears and eyes profoundly clear,
Communing with the real, reaching the numinous.
The Mystic Terrace in Heaven’s midst,
Flowing harmony, balance restored.
The Proud Maiden’s cloud-like grace,
The eye-child’s radiant brightness.
Flowering wisdom, resplendent clarity,
A hundred measures subtly pure.
Preserve harmony in the Upper Prime,
Wandering the Nine Citadels.
The Five Viscera take root,
Ears and eyes naturally arise.
The Heavenly Terrace, lush and serene,
Pillars and beams stand firm.
The Seven Po refine and temper,
The Three Hun rest in peace.
The Red Child bears the light,
Ever at my side.
Should any dare obstruct my ears and eyes,
The Supreme shall shatter them with the Flowing Bells.
Ten thousand evils vanish,
Every wish fulfilled.
Sun and moon guard the gates,
The heart treasury holds the Five Stars.
Invoked by the Perfected Sovereign,
All echoes heed with reverence."*

Upon awakening, perform this pressing and invocation without fail, not missing a single night’s rest. Though the true Dao may be attained, those like us still practice it constantly. When no longer lying down, one may perform it while seated. This is the supreme incantation of the *Taishang Baoshen Jing*, a Way that sharpens the ears and brightens the eyes, strengthening memory and fostering luminous clarity.

The breath in the nose is balanced and even,
No drooping snivel flows.
The four echoes resound, the eight permeate,
The face bears the glow of youth.
Mastering the hun and recording the po,
Repelling a thousand demons.
The seven apertures divide the flow,
Their hue like pristine blossoms.
This is the wondrous Way of the Perfected One’s rising and resting.
The reason it is called "rising and resting" is that it is constantly practiced.

Thereafter, swallow the saliva nine times,
Rub and wipe the face and eyes,
Inducing a slight warmth as the norm.
Do this whenever the occasion arises.

In the third year of the Xingning reign, the year *yichou*, on the twenty-third day of the sixth month, at night, this was transcribed.
That very evening, among those who practiced the Dao, many suffered from dullness of ears and eyes. Desiring to request this method, that very night a revelation descended, and it was still seen to be so.

*(This is Yang Jun’s personal account. The Prefect was past sixty, his ears and eyes beginning to fail, thus he inquired. Yang, unwilling to name him directly, attributed it to "those among us.")*
He further warned: "Daoists whose hearing is impaired have practiced the Yellow and Red without moderation. One must be cautious."

*(This likely serves as a warning to the Prefect.)*

The above is a passage of pure numinous instruction:
Comb the hair and arrange it,
Doing so many times over,
To circulate the blood and qi.

Scattering wind and dampness.
Frequent combing—alternate their use.
There is no need to loosen the hair.

The above is a discourse of Lady Ziwei.

The *Taiyi Lüjing* states: When arranging the hair, face the direction of the kingly earth. At the very beginning of combing, silently recite:
"Mud-pellet’s mysterious blossom,
Preserve essence, let it long endure.
Left is the hidden moon,
Right is the root of the sun.
Six Harmonies refine and purify,
A hundred spirits receive grace."
Upon finishing the recitation, swallow saliva thrice. If practiced constantly, the hair will not fall but instead grow daily. Frequently change combs, combing often but without causing pain. One may also have an attendant comb the hair thoroughly. Thus, blood and fluids will not stagnate, and the roots of the hair will remain firm.

The above was taught by An Jiuhua for practical use.
*(These two passages concern halting graying and preventing hair loss, and were also given in answer to the Prefect.)*

Lady Ziwei further instructed:
"Beneath the canopy of blossoming splendor, extend harmony to the celestial perfected.
Enter the valley of mountain streams, fill the source of the celestial mountain.
Then the numinous and ethereal become visible, and the myriad ghosts destroy themselves.
This is what is meant by ‘looking up to harmonize with the celestial perfected, looking down to press the mountain source.’"
*(The blossoming canopy is also called the blossoming court.)*

The celestial perfected is between the two eyebrows, at the corners of the brows. The mountain source is the base of the philtrum beneath the nose, slightly recessed into the valley. The blossoming court lies below the two eyebrows—it is the thoroughfare of penetrating vision. The celestial perfected is the upper chamber for drawing in the numinous. At dawn, noon, and dusk, constantly swallow saliva twenty-seven times, and urgently press with the fingers twenty-seven times in the yin manner as a regular practice. This will enable one to attain numinous clarity of vision and block the path of the myriad evils. Perform this thrice daily.
*(Lady Ziwei said: When a person suddenly falls ill and is near death, worldly physicians only know to needle the philtrum, unaware of needling the valley of the mountain source—this is a grave error. The original annotation begins here, as Yang appended it to the Prefect’s letter.)*

Press while reciting:
"Open and clear the celestial court,
Let me attain long life.
Penetrate vision for ten thousand miles,
Let soul and spirit return to infancy.
Destroy ghosts and repel demons,
Summon a thousand numinous beings.
Ascend to the Supreme,
Merge with the sun.
Obtain the rank of perfected person,
Inscribed in the register of the mysterious.
[As in the time of Duke Zhuang of Chu.]"

(This refers to King Zhuang of Chu during the Spring and Autumn period.) Market chief Song Laizi constantly swept the entire marketplace. After a long time, a beggar appeared, wandering the market to beg for food day after day. He would often chant:

*"The celestial court blooms with twin flowers,
The mountain source reveals yin’s evil.
At dawn, press the heavenly steed,
Come to the abode of the Supreme Perfected.
The perfected person cannot hide,
Thus vanquishing the hundred demons."*

Song Laizi chanted this while begging, yet none in the market understood his song. Only Laizi suddenly realized the beggar might be an immortal, though he still did not grasp the meaning of the verses. He then became the beggar’s disciple, abandoning his post to follow him. After thirteen years, the beggar transmitted to him the Dao of the Middle Immortals. Laizi now resides on Central Marchmount.

The beggar was Feng Yanshou, a Perfected One of Western Marchmount and a court historian during the reign of King Xuan of Zhou. The "heavenly steed" refers to the hands, and the "mountain source" to the area beneath the nose. Written on the night of the twenty-seventh day of the sixth month. *(Yang Jie concludes his transcription here.)*

Lady Yunlin Wang said: The Dao of the immortals and perfected ones takes the ears and eyes as its foundation. Excessive indulgence in sensual pleasures dims the eyes, while excessive sorrow blocks the ears. These two afflictions arise from within and rush outward—there are no others. Now, this method makes one’s hearing and vision increasingly sharp and clear.

Only those who fail to practice it find the practice difficult. To achieve supreme clarity and luminous perception, and to observe spirits and deities at will, one must purify the heart and sever all distracting thoughts, abandoning dissipation and excess. This is called "strictness at the outset."

At night before sleep, first tightly close the eyes and face east. With the base of each thumb, press and wipe from the eyes toward the ears, so that both palms meet at the nape of the neck—perform this twenty-seven times. Visualize three colored qi—purple, azure, and crimson—emerging before the eyes. This is the inner pressing of the Three Primordial Clouds, which irrigates and unites the Celestial Lads.

Recite the following incantation in silence:
*"Celestial Lads of the Three Clouds,
True Lords of the Two Eyes,
Radiant and luminous, you infuse essence,
Opening and clearing the spirit.
Great Mystery’s cloudy forms,
Spiritual steeds soaring lightly—
Guard and benefit the twin gates,
Unseal and penetrate the nine portals.
A hundred joints respond in resonance,
Morning fluid ascends to the Mud-Pill Palace.
The body ascends to the Jade Court,
Ranked among the Supreme Perfected."*

These forty-eight characters recited, swallow saliva fifty times, then open the eyes. This may be practiced as a regular routine, whether sitting or rising, not limited to night. If performed at the hour of birth for about a year, the ears and eyes will grow keen and bright. With prolonged practice, one may see clearly for a thousand miles, perceive spirits and deities, and hear sounds beyond ordinary reach. This is indeed a lofty Dao of the true immortals—not merely for brightening the eyes and opening the ears.

Those who aspire to study the Dao should strive to keep their practices and perceptions unknown to others in all matters. As the song in the Supreme Palace of the Most High declares:
*"Hands grasp the qi of the Eight Clouds,
Radiance guards the Two Lads.
The Supreme Perfected holds the bright mirror,
Its reflection unites the edge of sun and moon.
Cloudy forms brush the high gates,
Opening the Mud-Pill Palace.
Ten thousand sounds enter a hundred passages,
The Proud Maiden sits in the Dark Chamber.
The more one practices, the more vibrant and flourishing—
The numinous power naturally flows through."*

This song speaks precisely of the canon of ears and eyes. We, the immortals of Canglang Fangzhang, have always treasured and practiced it. This Way emerges from the *Four Illuminations Jade Canon of the Supreme*. It is transmitted only after swearing an oath upon blue-gold. Thereafter may it be practiced.

*(The above was all received by the Lady of Right Florescence, who instructed the Chief Scribe accordingly. Additionally, pledges of faith were employed, along with blue silk. It is also fitting to establish standards in accordance: twenty feet of blue cloth and two pairs of gold rings. These are the three original sections of the* Four Illuminations Jade Canon.*)*

Close the gates and bow in stillness—then the hundred ghosts will stand in awe. The Merit Officers may then be seen and spoken with, for this comes only through long practice.

On the second day of the seventh month, the Lady of South Marchmount instructed: When burning incense, do not look back, lest you offend the Perfected and summon demonic responses. When entering the chamber of stillness, first send someone ahead to announce your presence to those above. When approaching a meal, do not speak of matters of death. When bathing, constantly visualize the Six Dings, and your wishes will be fulfilled in all directions. When combing your hair, face the direction of the King’s land. At the first stroke of the comb, softly recite this incantation:
*"Mysterious flower of the Mud-Pill,
Preserve essence and prolong existence.
To the right, the hidden moon;
To the left, the root of the sun.
The Six Harmonies refine and purify,
The hundred spirits receive grace."*
Upon finishing the recitation, swallow saliva three times.

*(This passage is identical to that spoken by the Consort An, though the order of precedence is unclear. Judging by the reckoning of sun and moon, this appears to be the later version.)*

The above four instructions were given by the Lady of South Marchmount.

The *Orthodox Unity Canon of Leveling* states: Close the breath and bow in stillness, so that the hundred ghosts stand in awe. The Merit Officer Messengers, the Dragon-Tiger Lords, may then be seen and spoken with—this comes only through sincere and long practice.

*(The Orthodox Unity tradition possesses the* Orthodox Unity of Leveling. *Here, all matters concerning bowing in stillness are recorded. It must belong to the Orthodox Unity Canon, though some characters may be missing.)*

It further states: When burning incense, do not look back. To look back offends the Perfected and summons demonic responses. It also states...

Entering the chamber of stillness: first step forward with the right foot, then bring the left foot forward to align with the right. Only then proceed as usual. This allows one’s petition to be presented and heard above.

It further states: When partaking of food, do not speak of matters of death. Do not expose food, lest it attract a host of malevolent spirits.

It further states: Bathe frequently. On every *jiazi* day, one should wash one’s hair; if not, then at least on the first day of each month. This enables communion with the numinous. Bathing is not to be feared for its frequency—what is to be feared is one’s own inability. By washing away the stench of the corpse, the Perfected may enter.

The above six instructions were commanded by the Dark Mystery Master for practice and application. *(The preceding six clauses largely resemble those mentioned earlier, being a summary of received teachings. Here, they are recorded in greater detail, with two additional clauses appended for the Chief Scribe’s reference.)*

The above ten clauses were transcribed by the Chief Scribe.

When ingesting immortal elixirs, always face the direction of one’s natal destiny. After ingestion, do not speak of death, mourning, or inauspicious matters, lest it harm the embryo and injure the spirit, rendering the elixir useless.

The Lord of Life of the Eastern Minister. *(This clause originally followed the transmission of the* Mysterious Perfection of the Luminous Hall *method.)*

The above clause was written by Yang.

The *Scripture of the Nine Transformations and Ten Transmutations for Renewal* of the Most High states: If one treads upon filth or any impure place, one should bathe and perform the *Dissolution of Form* to purge it. The method employs ten *liang* of bamboo leaves and four *liang* of peeled peach bark, boiled in one *hu* and two *dou* of pure water until it reaches a single boil. Adjust the temperature and bathe the body, and all filth will be dispelled. This not only removes impurity but also prevents damp impediment, sores, and itching. Bamboo is hollow, plain, and internally white, while peach repels evil and breaks filth—thus these two substances are used to purge the turbidity within the body. When celestial beings descend to wander the earth and return, they invariably use this water to cleanse themselves. Even the talismanic waters and incantations of the mundane world—mere minor arts of external alchemy—cannot compare to this formula. If one bathes, it is even better, though this water is not used for washing the hair. The pure essence for refining the corpse is precisely for bathing—truly wondrous and arcane.

The above was commanded for use by the Lady of Purple Tenuity.

The above clause was transcribed by the Chief Scribe.

Those who receive the esoteric instructions and practice the concealed scriptures of the Great Elixir, preserving them within the Three Primordials’ Grotto-Chambers, shall each month pay homage to the Three Primordial Lords of Grand Simplicity. On the ninth day of the first month, the eighth day of the second month, the seventh day of the third month, the sixth day of the fourth month, the fifth day of the fifth month, the fourth day of the sixth month, the third day of the seventh month, the second day of the eighth month, the first day of the ninth month, the tenth day of the tenth month, the eleventh day of the eleventh month, and the twelfth day of the twelfth month at night, within a chamber of still repose, they shall face north. Having performed six bows twice over, they shall kneel, press their foreheads to the ground, and say:

“Reverently I address the Supreme Great Dao, the Lofty Void, the Jade Dawn, the Grand Simplicity, the Purple Palace, the Eight Numinous Ones, and the Three Primordial Lords; the Central Yellow Elder, the Peerless White Prime, the Supreme Emperor; the Five Elders, the High Perfected, the Upper Immortals, the Three Sovereigns of the Grand Culmen’s Imperial Essence. I, your disciple of the Great Grotto’s Three Luminaries, on this auspicious night, when the Celestial Pass opens ninefold, do ascend my petition to the Jade Emperor, the True Lord on High, beseeching to attain longevity in the world above, to live for boundless eons, to ride at the hour the yellow dawn’s green canopy and dragon-carriage ascend to the Purple Court, and to command the myriad spirits.”

At the Four Brightnesses, the attendants stand guard.
This is completed. Let no one know of it. (This entry is transcribed by the clerk.)

To the right: The Rites of the Four Dawns for the Grand Simplicity and the Three Primordial Lords.
On an auspicious day at midnight, the Supreme Great Dao and the Jade Dawn Lord customarily ascend on the fourth day of the first month, the eighth day of the second month, the fifteenth day of the third month, the eighth day of the fourth month, the ninth day of the fifth month, the sixth day of the sixth month, the seventh day of the seventh month, the eighth day of the eighth month, the ninth day of the ninth month, the fifth day of the tenth month, the third day of the eleventh month, and the twelfth day of the twelfth month to the Jade Firmament’s Jasper Chamber, casting their gaze upon the world to seek those of steadfast resolve and far-wandering hearts. On these days, at dawn when the sun rises, face north and bow twice. This may also be done in seclusion. Declare your innermost aspirations and desires. When finished, swallow saliva thirty-six times. (Transcribed by the Chief Scribe.)

The Azure Lad of the Eastern Sea customarily ascends on *dingmao* days to the Square Cauldron’s Eastern Florescence Terrace, gazing in the four directions. On such days, you may face the sun and bow twice at sunrise, thereby absorbing the sun’s essence. (Again transcribed by the clerk.)

To the right: Issued by the Purple Void Primordial Lord.
(These three matters pertain to the methods of the Hidden Dawn Audience for advanced disciples. Their scriptures are not revealed to the world, thus the Southern Perfected has brought them forth. They are also to be followed and practiced by the Chief Scribe.)

These three entries were transcribed together by the Chief Scribe and the clerk on a single sheet.
Customarily observe the second day of the second month, the third day of the third month, the eighth day of the eighth month, and the ninth day of the ninth month.

On the night of the tenth day of the tenth month, perform the visualization practices of the Cavern Secrets within your bedchamber. It is auspicious to remain alone and sleepless. That evening, the Guardian Scriptures Jade Lads and Jade Maidens, along with the Supreme Ultimate Masters of the Celestial Prohibitions, will descend from the void to observe you. On this night, burn incense with utmost devotion, as though awaiting their arrival. Whether sitting or lying down, engage in visualization, scripture recitation, or contemplation of the Real—whatever your intent directs. However, you must not attend to other matters that evening, for this is not the Way of seeking the Dao. If you maintain vigilance on this day, all the more will goodness accrue. At the outset of receiving the Cavern Secrets, you should consistently cultivate this practice, holding it firmly in mind.

Should you encounter ill dreams, they may arise from three causes: first, the mischief of the *po* souls; second, the testing of the heart; third, the predations of the corpse-demons. To dispel them, upon awakening, press the philtrum with your left hand thirty-four times, and gnash your teeth thirty-four times. Then softly intone:

*"Great Cavern of the True and Mysterious,
Refine and forge the Three Hun Souls:
The First Hun swiftly guards the Seven Po,
The Second Hun swiftly guards the Mud-Pill Palace,
The Third Hun receives the heart’s command.
Swiftly invoke the Supreme Lords of the Three Origins.
I have encountered an inauspicious dream—
The Seven Po and the wandering corpse
Have conspired with the source of myriad evils.
Hasten to summon Peach-Kang, Guardian of Life,
To report above to the Imperial Lord.
The Five Elders and Nine Perfected
All stand guard at the gates of the body.
The Yellow Chamber’s Divine Masters,
The Purple Gate Generals,
Wielding halberds and shaking bells,
Dispel and extinguish the malign influences.
Turn misfortune to fortune,
Severing all ties to life and death."*

Conclude. If you lie down again, you will assuredly receive an auspicious response. As for the baleful *qi* of ill dreams, it will be sealed beneath the Three Passes. After three years, only spiritually resonant dreams will manifest, and all dreams will become clear reflections of future events, utterly free from inauspicious omens or ill portents.

*(The character for "evil" [恶] as written by the Chief Scribe places* xin *beneath* you*. Its meaning is akin to* xin *beneath* xi*, signifying the harsh and malevolent heart of Metal in the West.)*

If you encounter an auspicious dream in the night—a good dream that your heart deems favorable—this is a sign of blessed resonance. Upon awakening, rub your eyes thirty-four times and gnash your teeth thirty-four times. Then softly intone:

*"Supreme High Essence,
Three Emperors of Cinnabar Spirit,
The Crimson Palace shines with clarity,
Blessed resonance conveys its message.
The Three Origins’ gentle *po* souls,
The Heavenly Sovereign bestows the scriptures.
All endeavors harmonize,
Ascending as flying immortals to the Upper Clarity,
Ever in the company of Jade Perfected,
Together assembling in the Purple Court."*

Conclude. These are the secret formulas of the Great Cavern, transmitted to those who first cross its currents.

*(These three matters also pertain to the affairs of the Cavern Chamber and Great Cinnabar school. The true scriptures have not yet been revealed to the world. The texts circulating in the present age merely touch upon these matters, with many additions and omissions.)*

These three entries were transcribed by the Chief Scribe.

*(This talisman was drawn by the Chief Scribe.)*
*(This talisman was drawn by the clerk.)*

The talismans above were originally drawn in vermilion. The *Inner Scripture of the Hall of Light*’s talisman for "Opening the Heart and Dispelling Delusion" was composed and employed by Perfected Lord Wang. It is to be activated at dawn on an auspicious day.

Having received the vermilion script from Lord Wang, bow twice in reverence. The prayer states:

"May the Five Spirits open the heart,
pierce hearing to silence all sound.
May the Three Hun gather essence,
steadfastly guard the cinnabar heart.
Let me be free from delusion,
the Five Viscera roam afar."

After bowing, conclude the prayer. Once the prayer is finished, ingest the talisman. Upon ingestion, swallow saliva five times and click the teeth five times. Perform this in secrecy, unseen by others. *(The two instances of "delusion" should both read as "forgetting.")*

If not performed on an opening day, take it on the first, fifteenth, or twenty-seventh day of the month—three times monthly. Within a year, the secret art will manifest its efficacy.

*(The talisman and these three entries were transcribed in duplicate by the Chief Scribe and clerk, with the clerk writing in vermilion.)*

The Controller of Destinies of the Eastern Minister states:

Formerly, Master Wang was granted the *Supreme Scripture of the Hall of Light and Mysterious Perfection* by the Most High. After purifying through fasting and abstaining from grains, visualize the sun and moon within the mouth: by day, the sun; by night, the moon. Let them grow as large as rings—the sun crimson with nine rays of purple light, the moon yellow with ten rays of white light. Visualize swallowing the luminous essence of their rays, practicing this in secrecy without count.

When not engaged in this visualization, let the sun and moon return to reside within the Hall of Light of the face: the sun on the left, the moon on the right. Let the two luminaries merge and communicate with the pupils of the eyes.

This Dao gathers and circulates generative essence, harmonizes the hun and spirit. The Six Ding spirits attend, and heavenly soldiers guard. This is the supreme Dao of the Perfected.

The *Scripture of Mysterious Perfection* of the Most High requires first swearing an oath before practice. Only after its observance may one hear the Dao of jade pendants and golden *yu-dang*.

Formerly, Ji Wei maintained a strict fast for three years, his sincerity unwavering in solitary devotion, until at last he attained it.

Thus the divine radiance illumines the body, and only then may one receive the scripture. This is the Dao of Mysterious Perfection—essential yet unburdensome. I have long treasured and concealed it, keeping it close at hand. Therefore, I reveal it only to those who are discreet and vigilant.

The *Scripture of the Mysterious Perfection of the Hall of Light* exists, though its text is brief. Its core lies in oral transmission, and one should practice precisely as instructed. Formerly, I, Wei, did not possess the scripture but followed this method alone—only then did I obtain it. If you wish to receive it, you may seek it from me. The *Hidden Scripture of Jade Pendants* is not something I have seen.

When traveling at night or lying in darkness, if fear arises in the heart, visualize the sun and moon returning to the Hall of Light. In an instant, the hundred evils will vanish of themselves. For those dwelling in the mountains, this is most excellent.

*(The above explains the method of visualization for the* Scripture of Mysterious Perfection. *Its greater scripture is contained in the Mao transmission.)*

The three passages above were transcribed by Yang. The inner method of the Most Void Perfected, the Red Lord of South Mountain, states: On the fifth night of the month, at midnight, visualize the image of the sun within the heart, entering through the mouth. Let it illuminate the interior of the heart, merging its light with that of the sun. When this is complete, you should feel warmth in the heart, with rosy radiance as verification. After a long while, recite the incantation:

*"Great brightness nurtures essence,
Within, the cinnabar heart is refined.
Lights merge and illumine,
Divine perfected ones come seeking."*

When finished...

Swallow the saliva nine times. On the fifteenth, twenty-fifth, and twenty-ninth days of the month, repeat the above practice. This will render one’s perception bright and keen, all senses clear and penetrating. The face will glow with jade-like radiance, the body with golden luster. After fifteen years of practice, the Great One will dispatch a jeweled chariot to receive you, ascending to the Supreme Empyrean. The practice should be frequent, not limited to these specific days.

The above passage is from the *Scripture of the Most High on Dispelling Demons*. (This scripture has not yet been revealed to the world. The above passage was transcribed by the Prefect.)

The method of the Eastern Florescence Perfected for absorbing the images of the sun and moon: men absorb the image of the sun, women the image of the moon. If practiced without fail each day, it sharpens perception, brightens clarity, and causes the five viscera to blossom. The hun and po souls are refined and tempered, the six bowels harmonized and at peace—this is the Dao of longevity and deathlessness. 〔 〕〔 〕. (These two characters are written in cinnabar in the original text as *moshou*.)

The above records the method of absorbing the images of the sun and moon. It may also be practiced by visualizing the sun in circular form. (The above passage was transcribed by Yang.)

The origins of these two methods are uncertain as to which Perfected One transmitted them. Emperor Ming of the Han dreamed of a divine being, nine feet six inches tall, with a halo of light encircling his neck.

The apparition soared before the palace hall, filling the Emperor with joy. He inquired throughout the court, and the learned scholar Fu Yi replied: "Your servant has heard that in the land of Tianzhu there is one who has attained the Dao, known as the Buddha. I have heard he can fly through the air and his body emits a radiant light—this must be the divine being from your dream." The Emperor then understood. He dispatched envoys—Zhang Qian, the Feathered Forest Captain Qin Jing, Academician Wang Zun, and eleven others—to the Great Yuezhi Kingdom to procure and transcribe the *Forty-Two Chapters of the Buddha’s Sutra*, which were later stored in the fourteenth chamber of the Orchid Terrace’s stone repository. At once, he ordered a Buddhist temple built north of the road outside the western gate of Luoyang. He also commissioned a Buddha statue and a depiction of Hariti at the Cool Terrace of the Southern Palace. The Emperor was deeply moved, and even before constructing his own mausoleum, he had a Buddha image installed in the palace hall. At that time, the realm prospered and the people lived in peace; distant barbarians, admiring the transformation, willingly submitted as vassals. The arrival of Buddhist images in China thus began in the reign of Emperor Ming.

*(This account roughly aligns with external records, though it appears Buddhism had already been present in Chang’an for some time—Pei Jun’s case being one such instance. Moreover, the Dharma originated in Tianzhu and Gandhāra, not the Yuezhi lands, which sets this account apart.)*

Now, desiring to speak of the various minor *fangzhu* where the Buddha is revered, it is fitting first to recount these matters.

According to records, the Zhang Qian mentioned here was not the one from the Former Han—perhaps only their names coincided. Fu Yi, styled Zhongwu, is attested in the *Book of Han*. The Qin princes Jing and Zun are obscure. This temple is called the White Horse Temple. Emperor Ming was later interred at the Mausoleum of Manifest Virtue; what is called here the "Longevity Mausoleum" refers to the practice of Han emperors, who, while still reigning, prepared their tombs in advance—much as people today construct their own burial mounds—rather than naming an actual mausoleum. External records also state that the court dispatched Attendant Gentleman Zhang Kan (or, as some say, Gentleman of the Palace Zhang [Xin]) to Tianzhu to copy and bring back scriptures and images, along with śramaṇas. Yet even this account may not reflect the true transmission, for it likely derives from the old notes of Master Yang. Nevertheless, in the authentic scriptures and pronouncements, references to Buddhist matters appear frequently.

The *fangzhu* are aligned with the four directions, hence their name. Each face measures one thousand three hundred *li*, and the four faces together span five thousand two hundred *li*. Its height reaches nine thousand *zhang*. There stands the Ever-Bright Mount Tai, and the Moonlit Mound, each encircling four hundred *li*. The minor mountains and rivers resemble those of our world, yet their grasses and trees flourish more luxuriantly, and their blossoms and fruits are more resplendent. The herb of immortality abounds, as do springs of sweet water; those who partake of them do not die.

The Palace of the Azure Lord is situated atop the Eastern Florescence Mountain, covering two hundred *li* in extent—entirely the abode of celestial immortals and highest perfected beings. Its halls and chambers are wrought of gold, jade, and luminous jasper. There is also the Dark and Frigid Mountain, upon which stands a separate outer palace, its structures spanning two hundred *li*. To the east and west of the great *fangzhu* lie smaller *fangzhu*, each three thousand *li* distant. These minor *fangzhu* also measure three hundred *li* on each side, encircling one thousand two hundred *li*, and each possesses its own Palace of the Azure Lord.

Moreover, they teem with middle-ranking immortals, numinous birds, and sacred beasts. The great *fangzhu* lies opposite the southeast of Kuaiji, yet from the shore of Kuaiji it appears seventy thousand *li* away. Gazing northeast, one sees the Scalding Vale and the Land of the Fusang Tree, which are another sixty thousand *li* distant from the *fangzhu*. (The *fangzhu* is the *yi* region, the Scalding Vale the *jia* region; thus from *yin* to *chen* spans ten thousand *li*. The five corners and seven directions are spoken of in terms of diagonal angles, totaling fourteen thousand *li*—hence the seventy thousand *li* from Kuaiji.)

To the west of the great *fangzhu*, atop the minor *fangzhu*, many follow the Dao of the Buddha.

Amidst these lands stand pagodas, intricately carved from gold and jade. Some rise a hundred *zhang* in height, their towers numbering in the dozens. Those who dwell above are all filial and deathless, for they partake of the deathless herb. They ingest the essence of the Five Stars and study the *Xia Gui Zang Jing*, employing its methods to traverse the skies. (Note: The *Xia* canon is called *Lian Shan*, the *Yin* canon *Gui Zang*—this differs from the present text. Though they follow the Buddha’s Way, they do not adopt the form or robes of *bhikṣus*. The world calls them the true household of bodhisattvas.)

To the east of the great *fangzhu*, atop the minor *fangzhu*, lie many rare and numinous treasures. There is white jade wine infused with golden nectar, and the Azure Lord stores celestial treasures here in abundance. Many immortals also dwell here, partaking of the deathless herb and drinking this wine. Their bodies take on the luster of gold and jade. They often play the Nine Numinous Flutes for their own delight. The sound of the flute carries forty *li*, its thirty holes carved into bamboo two or three *chi* long. When the nine flutes play in unison, the hundred beasts dance, and dozens of phoenixes arrive to harmonize with the melody.

The Palace of the Great *Fangzhu* is the Azure Lord’s constant abode. Those who dwell above are celestial perfected ones and lofty immortals, where the lords of the Grand Ultimate, the ducal ministers, and the various Directors of Destinies reside. Some practice the method of ingesting the rays of the sun and moon. Though they have already attained the Dao and become perfected, they continue this practice. (Mount Huo and Red City are also bureaus of the Directors of Destinies. Only the Grand Prime Perfected, the Lady of the Southern Marchmount, resides there. Li Zhongfu is in the West, Han Zhong in the South, and the remaining thirty-one Directors of Destinies are all in the Eastern Flower Capital. The Azure Lad serves as the Grand Director of Destinies, overseeing all. Master Yang also states: the Eastern Dipper’s attendant—it is unclear which rank he holds.)

Direct your attention inward and visualize a symbol within the heart, as large as a coin, glowing red. Then visualize the sun with nine rays rising from the heart, ascending through the throat to the teeth, where the rays linger before returning to the stomach. After a long while, with eyes closed, clearly perceive the heart and stomach, then exhale and rinse the mouth with saliva thirty-nine times before stopping. Perform this thrice daily. After a year of practice, illnesses will vanish. After five years, the body will radiate light. After eighteen years, one will surely attain the Dao, casting no shadow at noon, repelling a hundred ghosts and a thousand malign influences. Constantly visualize the sun within the heart and the moon within the Mud Pill Palace. At night, ingest the moon’s essence as you do the sun’s. Visualize the moon’s ten white rays descending from the brain into the throat, where the rays do not pass the teeth but return to the stomach.

This is the method of the perfected ones of *Fangzhu*, recorded in the *Sutra of Great Wisdom*, upper and middle chapters. Those who practice it steadfastly will witness the Great Peace. (This likely corresponds to the seventh section of the *Seven Chapters of Wisdom for Dispelling Demons*.)

The above was imparted by the Lady of the Southern Culmen. Practicing the Way of the sun in the heart and the moon in the Mud Pill Palace is said to be simple and easily grasped. Those who persist without interruption will expel the Three Corpses from the body, cure a hundred illnesses and a thousand afflictions, and master the Way of refining the hun and restraining the po. When the sun and moon perpetually illuminate the body, ghosts will have no place to hide. The Azure Lord still practices this method. I am one such practitioner and now reveal it to you. You may discreetly share it with those of sincere intent.

Practicing this Way does not hinder the methods of ingesting the sun and moon as prescribed in the precious scriptures; combining them is even better. Immortals accomplish a thousand tasks in a single day and night without feeling weary. How diligently they cultivate the Dao! Life must not be squandered.

(The "precious scriptures’ sun and moon" refer to those used in the Purple Texts.)

The above was imparted by the Lord of Western City. (This was also told to Master Yang, who was instructed to share it with the various Xu.)

To pursue the Dao is like shooting an arrow: one must aim straight and not waver to hit the target. Enter the mountains with unwavering resolve, and you will attain the true Perfection.

So instructed the Mysterious Clarity. (Note: The two lofty perfected ones, Mysterious Clarity of the Southern Culmen and Western City, should not have further revelations. Only one precept and one poem each remain. It is unclear when this teaching was imparted.)

The above eight passages are from Yang’s writings. Practicing these four Ways, according to the superior methods of the Jade Mystery, will astonish the senses within a year. One may then diligently pursue them without doubt.

(The Central Lord’s records on this matter lack the preceding pages, so the exact method is unknown.)

So says the Perfected One of the Grand Ultimate.

Reading the *Daodejing*’s five thousand characters ten thousand times will summon the cloud chariot to receive you. If after completing ten thousand recitations it has not yet arrived, read it twice a month. You must depart only when the cloud chariot comes.

The above two passages are from a certain master’s writings.

Shanshi Yuan received the method from Master Meng: at dusk, first recite the *Huangting Neijing* once before sleep, so that one’s hun and po may be naturally refined. Practicing this for twenty-one years will also lead to immortality—this is equivalent to ten thousand recitations. Reciting three or four times each evening is excellent.

The Lady of Northern Peak, Jiang, said: "Reading this sutra also keeps one free from illness. It is the Way of not dying." (This [second] method of twenty-one years, one recitation per evening, does not amount to ten thousand recitations. Perhaps "one" should be "seven" or "eight." Otherwise, two or three recitations per evening would suffice.)

When visualizing the Five Stars, one must carefully follow the *Eight Purities*, beginning with the King Star. Visualize it at the time when generative qi arises. If the King Star does not appear first, do not visualize it first. As for observing the stars, one may do so freely within the chamber. Diligence and sincerity are paramount—it is not necessary to see all the stars clearly before swift communion is achieved. Observation should be precise.

The Lord of Pure Numinosity instructed: The essential method of visualization is to perceive the Five Stars with the eyes, each descending toward you upon its radiant beam. Then, following the descent of the King Star, visualize it. Swallow one beam, then proceed to the Star of Stability, visualizing it in turn. After a long while, swallow one beam from each of the Five Stars, drawing them all into the mouth and swallowing them, matching the number of the Star of Stability. (This is an alternate method not found in the sutras.)

If suddenly visualizing the Five Stars, follow the usual method without focusing on their descent. (By this account, the latter is a solitary cultivation method.)

On the first night of the sixth month, the Perfected One of Azure Numinosity spoke. (The above four passages are from Yang’s writings. "Azure" should be "Pure.")

The five celestial script characters of the Sun’s essence are: "Sun’s soul, Pearl Radiance, Shining Veil, Green Reflection, Swirling Rosy Clouds, Crimson Youth, Mysterious Flame, Whirlwind Image." These sixteen characters comprise the Way of the Golden Watchtower’s Sage Lord, who gathers and ingests the flying root. Formerly received from the Celestial Emperor of the Great Tenuity, it is also called the *Sutra of Cinnabar Gold Essence, Stone Radiance, Water Mother, and Jade Embryo*.

The Right Florescence said:
*"Pearl rounds and gathers brilliance, the green veil congeals,*
*The sun’s rosy clouds blaze bright, the crimson youth holds numen,*
*Mysterious flame scatters light, the whirlwind’s image stirs the clear."*
Such is the Sun’s power, the might of its spirit.

(According to the *Purple Text*, this concerns the Sun’s soul, though its meaning is not entirely proper and must be inferred.)

The above two passages are from a certain master’s writings.

*"At dawn’s first glow, purple clouds map the dark ridge,*
*Resplendent, the round light flourishes,*
*Dazzling, it washes the radiant net.*
*Vast and distant, the numinous scene’s origin,*
*Forestalling the empty clarity’s splendor.*
*The Nine Heavens host jade guests,*
*In golden chambers, mist and dawn sing."*

The above is from the middle chapter of the *Sutra of the Great Cavern*. Here, several lines are excerpted. (These four lines also appear in the present *Cavern Sutra*.)

Foreign lands call the sun *Zhuoyaoluo*. The Perfected One of Square Cauldrons calls it *Round Radiance*. Dreaming of this *Zhuoyaoluo* is the Sun’s response. One who appears amid purple clouds is a spirit of the womb palace—this is the Way of the Mysterious Perfected.

The Sun’s virtue {broad and yin} is the symbol of long life. Purple clouds at dawn bring peace to the hun and po, health to the body, and tranquility to the spirit. This is where it begins.

When the four verses have been presented, the qi and intent become calm and harmonious. (These are Master Yang’s own words in a letter to the Chief Clerk.)

The Right Florescence’s commentary on the *Sutra of the Great Cavern* explains the meaning of dreaming of *Zhuoyaoluo*.

Farewell. (This is also his own remark. The Chief Clerk’s dream is not clearly described.)

The above four passages are from Yang’s writings.

*True Reports, Scroll Nine*
*True Reports, Scroll Ten*
*Second Harmony of the Auspicious Epoch*

*"Subtle sincerity moves through principle to stir the hidden Perfected,*
*Accumulated essence pierces the dark truth.*
*Gracefully riding cloud hues,*
*The numinous image leans on purple mist.*
*Vast and distant, it washes the round net,*
*Swiftly driving the flying wheel.*
*Mysterious wings open the dim,*
*Gazing back, grace renews itself."*

The Chief Clerk, having opened and read the missive, composed a poem in response. (This is the original annotation, which clarifies the intent to elucidate the dream’s meaning. The Chief Clerk wrote it himself. In all *True Writings* and ancient texts, characters imitating forms are rendered as "fǎngfú." Here, it is indeed "fǎngfú." From this character to the character "也," all are written in vermilion.)

Fan Youchong was a man of Liaoxi. Conceived through transformation, his form was altered. Now he resides here, constantly cultivating the Three Qi. The method of the Three Qi involves visualizing green-white qi and red qi, each like {a thread extending}, descending from the rising sun in the east and entering the mouth. {The hands are cupped} ninety times, stopping once satiated. After ten years of practice, the three-colored qi naturally reside within the body, and one attains immortality. This is the *High Prime Lord’s Method of the Inner Radiance of Grand Simplicity*. Perform it daily at dawn, practicing with eyes closed. The results improve with each day. The method is rare, yet its effects are profoundly verified. Lord Xu may practice it as well. (Fan is the Central Supervisor of Huayang; the details are recorded in Scroll Four.)

The above is another passage from Yang’s writings.

The Jade Consort of Eastern Florescence of the Eastern Sea, Chun Wenqi, transmitted the *Method of Ingesting Mist* to the Perfected Woman of the Containing Reality Terrace, Zhang Weizi. It is to be practiced regularly at dawn, in the stillness of one’s chamber.

Sit or recline as you please. First close your eyes and inwardly visualize, faintly perceiving the five viscera. Then exhale through the mouth twenty-four times. Perform this with eyes closed, so that the eyes perceive the five-colored qi swirling and entwining upon the face, guiding them to gather thickly. Then draw this five-colored qi into the mouth fifty times. Afterward, swallow the saliva sixty times. Then softly recite the incantation:

*"Great rosy clouds radiate brilliance,
Spiritual mists drift in all four directions.
The qi congeals in the Jade Bend,
Five colors illumine the Grotto-Heaven.
Divine smoke embraces and unfolds,
Metal and stone blossom with true essence.
Purple emptiness billows in lush abundance,
Refining the form to preserve its wholeness.
Emerging in light, concealed in mystery,
The Five Spirits transform and divide.
United brightness fans the void,
At times riding the six clouds.
Harmonizing and gathering my body,
Ascending to the Nine Heavens."*

Afterward, click the teeth seven times and swallow the saliva seven times. Then open the eyes, and the practice is complete. This Dao is wondrously efficacious. In the Divine Continent’s Mystic Capital, many have attained this technique. Those who practice it long will often ride clouds and mists in their travels.

The above is another passage from Yang’s writings.

Another transcribed method: The *Way of Guarding the Mysterious and White* is practiced daily at dawn. Sit or recline as you wish. Visualize black qi within the Mud-Pill Palace, white qi within the heart, and yellow qi within the navel. Let the three qi arise together, like clouds covering the body. Then transform them into fire, which encircles the body. The body becomes thoroughly permeable, inner and outer as one. Practice from dawn until midday, then cease. At this point, ingest qi one hundred twenty times. When all is complete, the Dao is precisely thus.

To grant one long life and immortality, repelling all harm—this especially forbids the consumption of the flesh of the six livestock and the five pungent flavors. One must sleep and dwell apart, in quiet contemplation. Sexual intercourse is particularly forbidden; engaging in it leads to death. At first, visualize exhaled qi as small as a bean, gradually expanding until it pierces the heavens. Three coils of smoke encircle the body, merging into one undifferentiated whole. Suddenly, fire arises within the three coils of smoke, then combines with the inner radiance to refine the entire body. Within the body, the five viscera become luminously transparent. This, too, is an essential Dao.

The above two passages were transcribed. All three matters are recorded in the *Huayang Treatise*, Scroll Four. Here, they are copied again, for these are the methods one may cultivate. The original text remains in that scroll.

The Supreme Ultimate Perfected One decreed: The *Taipei Emperor’s Envoy* (these three characters were later defaced and cannot be discerned again) *Divine Talisman for Annihilating Ghosts and Spirits* is to be encased in a double-layered purple pouch and tied upon the head. (Entering defiled places, it averts [meat and] avoidance.) (These nine characters were further obscured by blue [ink]; with a knife, they are now entirely unrecognizable, and not the characters written here.) The talisman is guarded by two *Direct Envoys of the Three Heavens*. Should any malevolent ghost or myriad evil approach one who wears this talisman, they shall perish. (Below this, ten more characters were also defaced.)

(Where earlier text was indecipherable) men and women each wear one. These have already been inscribed separately. The Lesser Lord now copies this talisman to be worn together. It appears in the *Scripture of the Jade Horse*, also named the *Northern Emperor’s Writ*. (Among the *Seven Primal Talismans*, one lacks a title; tradition holds this to be that talisman, though the *Jade Horse Scripture* has never been seen in the world, and thus no certainty can be claimed.)

One part realgar, two parts orpiment, three parts massicot. These are the Three Yellow Flowers. First add one part cinnabar to a vessel and grind thoroughly. Next add realgar and grind thoroughly. Then add orpiment and grind thoroughly. Finally add massicot and grind together until well blended. (Mix with clarified glue while grinding.) The term “one” here denotes a single portion by intent, regardless of quantity. (This explains the method of preparing the Three Yellows for talisman-drawing; true talismans often employ this.)

The above three clauses were written by Yang. When compounding the medicine, one must be precise. Those who lack precision blame the formula’s inefficacy rather than their own failure. Such a person is truly at fault. One may copy the formula and prepare it thus: use five *liang* of calamus (though some use ten *liang*—this is merely the practice of those unfamiliar with the Daoist lineage). Use two *liang* of evodia root bark and three *liang* of purple cloud-lichen blossoms. This is the oral instruction of Lord Zhou. (This concerns the preparation of the initial divine pills; the formula appears in Su’s transmission, having been composed by Zhou Ziyang, and was thus imparted to the Prefect.)

The above clause was written separately. Prepare one *hu* of processed *atractylodes*. Wash thoroughly with clean water and soak until plump. Then pound finely into powder. Combine with two *hu* of clean water and cook over (gentle fire) until soft. Place in a silk bag and squeeze to extract the liquid. Pour into a bronze vessel and steam over boiling water. Add one (dou) of white honey and a quantity of large dried jujubes, pitted and pounded until skin and flesh are fully blended. Take one (dou) of this jujube paste and mix into the *atractylodes* and honey. Squeeze until thoroughly combined, forming a paste like *bu*. Consume three or four pellets the size of a bullet daily. After one dose, a hundred illnesses vanish; after two doses, ten thousand harms cannot afflict.

Three times, the complexion gains radiance. Four times, the ears and eyes grow sharp. After three years, the countenance becomes like a maiden’s. The immortals do not die.

Another method:
Prepare one *hu* of processed *atractylodes*. Wash thoroughly with water and allow to plump. Then dry and pound finely into powder. Take four *dou* of large jujubes, remove the pits, and pound until smooth. Combine with five *dou* of clear wine in a bronze vessel. Simmer and stir until it forms a paste-like preparation. Consume three pellets the size of a plum daily. A hundred illnesses cannot harm you. The face becomes like a child’s, and one withstands cold and frost.

Another method:
Take five *jin* of *atractylodes* powder and three *jin* of *poria*, boiled three times. Pound to obtain five *jin* of powder. Combine the two substances and grind together for three thousand strokes. Store in an airtight vessel. Take five *ge* each morning. A hundred disasters, poisons, and epidemics cannot assail you. The face remains youthful, and the body grows strong. With prolonged use, one can leap across peaks and valleys. The ears grow keen, and the eyes bright.

(These three formulas were transcribed by an assistant. They appear to have been transmitted by Lady Ziwei. They follow the *atractylodes* narrative.)

**Method for Refining Hemp Fat:**
Combine three *hu* of clean water, one *hu* of hemp fat, and two *jin* of *xiebai* (Chinese chive). Simmer the three ingredients together. Cover with a wooden lid to prevent the fat’s essence from escaping. Reduce to one *hu*, then mix with wine for consumption. It may also be taken alone.

(This formula was transcribed by the Prefect. It was originally recorded separately among the *Four-Stamen Elixir* methods. Some versions of the text also include two *jin* of *cong* (green onion).)

**The Supreme Ultimate Realized One’s Belt-Releasing Powder:**
Take one *daosui* of white powder. Suddenly, the heart will ache as if pierced. After three days, thirst will arise. Once one *hu* of liquid is consumed, the *qi* will cease. Cessation means death. After the body is encoffined, the corpse vanishes, leaving only the clothes behind. This is the immortal who sheds their belt in broad daylight. If one knows the name of the drug, the heart will not ache, but after drinking one *hu*, the *qi* will still cease. Once ceased, it is done.

When one senses the abandoned corpse lying upon the earth, jade maidens and jade youths will arrive at that very moment, bearing a blue palanquin to bear it away. Should one wish to pause, the heart will ache for three days, and one must drink in measured portions. This formula may also be used by an entire household. The *Cloud-and-Mist Robe* of nine *liang* is its chief ingredient. (The origin of this passage is unknown; it likely refers to the *White Membrane Powder*. The formula has not been seen in the world.)

The above passage should not be mixed with those who are not in a state of purification, nor with those who have not embodied the true Dao. Later generations ought to correct this. The highest of the Dao is found in the *Divine Tiger Scripture*. Unless one has received transmission, none may be permitted to see the paper upon which it is written. This is yet another failure to embody the truth.

The Southern Perfected One said: If the writing of the *Divine Tiger* text is not precise, the myriad things will not serve one’s use, and the heart’s labor will be in vain. When receiving the paper, take care; write with reverence, burn incense, and first inscribe the opening text. One should constantly burn incense beside the written text, ensuring the smoke remains pure and unbroken. Sincerity must be unwavering; the pursuit of the Dao depends solely on tirelessness. Is this not also close to neglect?

Those who attain the Dao always regret not having heard and received it sooner. Those who lose the Dao always regret not having been diligent and earnest. What is meant by *precision*? It is single-minded devotion to the matter. What is meant by *earnestness*? It is reverent cultivation of one’s practice. If one adds to this vigilance and caution, and guards it with the intent to evoke resonance, then one draws near to the truth. You must attend to this without forgetfulness.

(The preceding five passages all seem addressed solely to Lord Yang.)

To receive the scripture is to take a teacher—yet is this not a cause for shame? Since true sincerity is never exhausted, those who undergo examination are not few. You, sir, once studied *Guardian of the One* under Master Su Lin. You should first purify yourself and receive the precepts. If you can attain this means of transcending the world, the possibilities are beyond measure.

The Perfected Consort of Nine Flowers declared: To guard the One within the Five *Dou* is the supreme practice of the True One—all methods of the Perfected of Earth. Wang Zhen of Shangdang, Meng Jun of Jingzhao, and Sima Jizhu all first followed this Way at the outset. Lu Nüsheng and Zhang Jun of Handan now dwell on Central Peak and Mount Hua, precisely guarding this One. By this means, one may gradually ascend the Dao and advance without difficulty.

The One within the Five *Dou* is the inner method of Master Juan. Formerly transmitted within the Terrace of Mount Emei, it surpasses all external practices of guarding the One, the Mysterious One, and their kind—none have matched its traces.

The Lesser Perfected One said: (The True One of the Five *Dou* is precisely what is preserved and employed in Master Su’s transmission during the solstices and equinoxes.)

The Middle Perfected One stated: With unceasing diligence, I shall share the Flowing Pearl Perfection—this too is the supreme Way of the Middle Perfected. (The Flowing Pearl pertains to the Nine Palaces tradition; its scripture has not yet emerged into the world. The preceding five passages all seem addressed to Lord Ya.)

It is further said:
